يعطف أيضاً، وفي صورة عدم العطف لا تعلق لأحدهما بالآخر فكذا في العطف، واعترض بأن الشرط في الاستثناء الاتصال العرفي وهو متحقق فإن العرف لا يعده متأخراً عن الأول، وجوابه ظاهر، لأن الجمل المتعاطفة قد تستوعب الساعات إذا ذكر الاستثناء بعدها، ولا يحكم عاقل بأنه متصل بالأولى لا حقيقة ولا عرفاً وغير المتعاطفة اثنين أو ثلاثة إذا قرن بعدها استثناء، مثل المتعاطفة اثنين أو ثلاثة فإن اكتفى بهذا الاتصال العرفي فالمتعاطفة وغيرها سيان فيحكم برجوعه إلى الكل إذا كانت الجمل قليلة، بحيث يقال في العرف إنه كلام واحد وإن لم تكن متعاطفة بخلاف الكثير وإن كانت متعاطفة أن غير المتعاطفة لا يجوز فيها الرجوع اتفاقاً إلا إلى ما يليه، فقد ظهر أنه لا يكفي هذا الاتصال العرفي بل الذي هو شرط هو السكوت من غير عذر أو الأخذ في كلام آخر، وظاهر فيما نحن فيه أنه ترك الكلام الأول وأخذ في الآخر فلا يصح الاستثناء عنه بعده فتدبر، وهذا يكفي للناظر المنصف، واعترض أيضاً بأن الدليل لو تم لدل على عدم جواز تعلقه بالكل مع أنه يجوز بقرينة، ولك أن تجيب بأنه ربما ينزل الانفصال منزلة العدم لأمور خطابية وينزل الجمل المتعددة بالعطف منزلة جملة واحدة، فلا يعد أخذه في أخرى تركاً لها، بل إتماماً لها في المقامات الخطابية، لكن يحتاج إلى القرينة لكونه خلاف الظاهر فلا يدل دليلنا على عدم الجواز مطلقاً، بل إذا لم يكن صارف فقط، ألا ترى أنه كثيراً ما ينزل وجود الشيء منزلة العدم في المقامات الخطابية، فينزل العالم منزلة الجاهل لعدم العمل بمقتضاه وبالعكس لظهور أمره حقيقة أو ادعاء وغير ذلك مما بين في فن المعاني، فكذا ههنا فاحفظ فإنه من مزال الأقدام، ولنا ثالثاً : لو كان متعلقاً بالكل، لزم توجه الفعلين إلى متعلق واحد وهو التنازع ، ولا شك أن باب غير التنازع أكثر فيحمل عليه إلا بدليل لأن الظن تابع للأغلب فتدبر (واستدل) على المختار (أولاً : لو قال علي عشرة إلا أربعة إلا اثنين لزم ثمانية) فلم يتعلق الاستثناء إلا بما يليه وإن تعلق بالكل لزم ستة (ويجاب بأنه في غير محل النزاع لعدم العطف والجملة) ههنا (قيل) في شرح المختصر (و) لم يتعلق بالكل للتعذر) المانع إياه ( وإلا) يتعذر بل يصح (كان الاثنان مثبتاً) لكونهما مستثنيين عن الاستثناء المفيد للنفي (منفياً) لكونهما أيضاً مستثنيين من العشرة المثبتة وثبوت شيء واحد وانتفاؤه محال (أقول) في رده (وحدة الموضوع من شروط التناقض وليس الأظهر، وليست وحدة الموضوع متحققة ههنا لأن الاثنين المثبتين من جملة الأربعة المستثناة والمنفيين من جملة الستة الباقية وإن قيل نوع الاثنين واحد فوحدة الموضوع متحققة قلت: اجتماع المتنافيين في الواحد النوعي غير مستحيل كما لا يخفى فتدبر (و) استدل (ثانياً بأن عمله لعدم استقلاله ضروري) فإن غير المستقل يقتضي التعلق والارتباط (وما وجب للضرورة يقدر بقدرها ولا يتعداها (والأخيرة متعينة) للتعلق لأن الكلام فيما لا صارف وبها تندفع الضرورة، فلا يتعلق بما عداها (ويجاب بأنه وضعي أي وضع للتعلق بالجملة (لا) ضروري حتى لا يتجاوز قدرها، وفي «التحرير» إن أريد أنه وضع للتعلق بالأخيرة فتم مطلوبنا، وإن أريد أنه وضع للتعلق بالكل فهو ممنوع وظاهره غير موجه لأنه منع على المنع ووجه بأنه ممنوع وباطل لأنه يستعمل للأخيرة، والأصل الحقيقة، وفيه : أن الخصم لا يسلم الاستعمال من غير صارف عن الأولى، ومطلق الاستعمال لا يفيد مع أنه لو تم لغا مقدمات أصل الدليل، وربما يقرر بأن المراد بالضرورة عدم الإفادة من غير تعلق، وإن كان التعلق وضعياً فالاستثناء لعدم استقلاله ضروري التعلق، والأخيرة تكفي فلا يتعلق بما عداها فحينئذ يندفع لكن يرد حينئذ وروداً ظاهراً ما أشار إليه بقوله (أقول: وأيضاً الكلام في قدر الضرورة فإنه لم لا يجوز أن تكون الضرورة مقتضية للتعلق بالجميع، كيف لا وأنه عند الخصم موضوع للإخراج عما قبله متعدداً كان أو واحداً فإفادته موقوفة على التعلق بالكل ففيه الضرورة (فافهم) ولا مخلص عنه إلا بأن يقال إنه ضروري التعلق لأنه غير مستقل، والأصل في المعمول أن يلي العامل إن كفى الإفادة، وههنا الأخيرة كافية لدفع ضرورة التعلق فالظاهر تعلقه بالأخيرة فتأمل فيه تأملاً صادقاً وما) في المنهاج من النقض بالحال والشرط والصفة وغيرها فإن مقدمات الدليل جارية فيها مع أنها للكل اتفاقاً (ففيه أنه لا اتفاق إلا في الشرط) في التعلق بالجميع (خاصة كما صرح به الإمام فخر الدين (الرازي) صاحب المحصول فلا نقض إلا به لا بالصفة وغيرها، فإنها للأخيرة عندنا وسيأتي وجه الفرق بين الشرط والاستثناء فيندفع به النقض فانتظر.
الاستثناء
هذا
الشافعية قالوا : أوّلاً: العطف يجعل المتعدد (كالمفرد فيجعل الجمل كالواحدة فالمتعلق بالواحد هو المتعلق بالكل (أقول : إنما يتم لو كان عطف الثانية على الأولى بدون الاستثناء) فإنه حينئذ صار الكل بالعطف واحدة فلا معنى لتعلق الاستثناء بواحد لا غير (وهو) أي عطف الثانية على الأولى بدون الاستثناء (ممنوع) بل يجوز أن يتعلق أولاً بالأخيرة ثم هي مع عطفت على الأولى، وصارت الكل بمنزلة جملة واحدة فلا يلزم تعلقه بالكل (وأجيب في المشهور بأن ذلك أي صيرورة المتعددة كالواحد (في) عطف (المفردات حقيقة نحو : جاء زيد وبكر أو حكماً كالجمل التي لها محل من الإعراب أو وقعت صلة) وأما في عطف غير المفردات فلا للقطع بأن نحو ضرب بنو تميم وبكر شجعان ليس في حكمه) ويظهر من الدليل وجوابه أن الاستثناء من المعطوف المفرد استثناء من المعطوف عليه، لأنهما كشيء واحد، وهذا يناسب ما مر من أن قيود أحد المتعاطفين قيود للآخر للتشريك، وقد مر الكلام فيه، ثم يرد عليه أن الصفة والغاية لا يتقيد به إلا المفرد الأخير مع أنه كالاستثناء وسائر القيود فالحق إذاً جواب المصنف، وهذا تنزلي فافهم (و) قالوا :(ثانياً : لو قال : والله لا أكلت ولا شربت إن شاء الله تعالى تعلق بهما اتفاقاً) بيننا وبينكم فلا يحنث بالأكل ولا بالشرب (وأجيب بأنه) أي إن شاء الله تعالى (شرط) لا استثناء) فليس مما نحن فيه فإن ألحق به لأنه تخصيص مثله فيكون مثله في الأحكام (كان) قياساً في اللغة وقد نهينا عنه، وإن قالوا: وجدنا محاورات المخصصات الغير المستقلة على نمط واحد فلا قياس قلنا ليس كذلك بل الشرط للحكم التعليقي بخلاف الاستثناء فإنه تنجيز ولا يلزم اتحاد ما وضع لنوعي الحكم التعليقي والتنجيزي في الأحكام، ألا تری أن الشرط قد يفيد انتفاء الجزاء بالكلية والاستثناء ليس كذلك، ودعوى الاستقراء في الجنس من غير استقراء هذا النوع منه لا يصح، بل لا بد في استقراء الجنس من
And it is also conjoined. In the case of no conjunction, one has no relation to the other, so likewise in conjunction. It was objected that the condition in exception is customary connection (al-ittisal al-'urfi), and that is realized, because custom does not consider it to be later than the first. Its answer is apparent, because conjoined sentences may occupy hours when the exception is mentioned after them, and no rational person judges that it is connected to the first, neither in reality nor customarily. And non-conjoined sentences, two or three, when an exception is appended after them, are like conjoined two or three. If one is satisfied with this customary connection, then conjoined and non-conjoined are equal, so it is judged to revert to all if the sentences are few, such that customarily it is considered one speech, even if not conjoined, unlike many, even if conjoined. But non-conjoined, it is not permissible to revert (to all) by agreement, except to what immediately precedes. So it has become clear that this customary connection is not sufficient; rather, the condition is silence without excuse or beginning another speech. And it is apparent in our case that he left the first speech and began another, so exception after it is not valid. So ponder. And this is sufficient for the impartial observer. And it was also objected that if the proof were complete, it would indicate the impermissibility of attaching it to all, though it is permissible with a qarina (contextual indicator). And you may answer that perhaps separation is treated as non-existence for rhetorical purposes, and multiple sentences conjoined are treated as a single sentence, so beginning another is not considered leaving it, but rather completing it in rhetorical contexts. However, a qarina is needed because it is contrary to the apparent. So our proof does not indicate absolute impermissibility, but only when there is no diverting factor. Do you not see that often the existence of a thing is treated as non-existence in rhetorical contexts, so the knowledgeable person is treated as ignorant for not acting accordingly, and vice versa due to the obviousness of his matter in reality or by allegation, and other matters explained in the science of meanings. So here as well, so memorize, for it is a slippery slope. And thirdly for us: if it were attached to all, it would necessitate directing two actions to a single object, which is conflict (tanazu'). And there is no doubt that the sphere of non-conflict is more frequent, so it is interpreted accordingly unless there is evidence, because conjecture follows the majority. So ponder. And they proved (the chosen position) firstly: if he says, 'I owe ten except four except two,' eight is incumbent. So the exception attached only to what immediately follows; if it attached to all, six would be incumbent. And it is answered that this is not the locus of dispute because there is no conjunction and the sentence... here it is said in Sharh al-Mukhtasar: and it did not attach to all due to impossibility which prevents it. Otherwise, if it were not impossible but valid, the two would be affirmed (as affirmed) because they are excepted from the exception which conveys negation, and negated because they are also excepted from the affirmed ten, and the affirmation and negation of one thing is impossible. I say in refutation: unity of subject is a condition of contradiction, and it is not obvious. Unity of subject is not realized here because the affirmed two are from the excepted four, and the negated two are from the remaining six. If it is said that the type of two is one, then unity of subject is realized, I say: combination of contradictories in a single type is not impossible, as is not hidden. So ponder. And they proved secondly: because its operation is necessary due to its lack of independence, for what is not independent requires attachment and connection. And what is necessitated by necessity is measured by it and does not exceed it. And the last clause is specified for attachment because the speech is about that which has no diverting factor, and by it necessity is removed, so it does not attach to what is other than it. And it is answered that it is conventional (wad'i), i.e., it is placed to attach to the sentence, not necessary such that it does not exceed its measure. And in al-Tahrir: if it is meant that it is placed to attach to the last, then our desired is established; if it is meant that it is placed to attach to all, it is denied and its apparent is not directed because it is a denial upon denial. And it is directed that it is denied and false because it is used for the last, and the principle is reality. And therein: the opponent does not concede usage without a diverting factor from the first, and absolute usage is not beneficial, and if it were complete, the premises of the original proof would be invalid. And perhaps it is established that by necessity is meant lack of benefit without attachment, and even if the attachment is conventional, the exception, due to its lack of independence, necessarily requires attachment, and the last suffices, so it does not attach to what is other than it. Then at that point it is repelled, but then there occurs an apparent objection to what he indicated by his saying: I say: also the discussion is about the extent of necessity, for why is it not permissible that necessity demands attachment to all? How not, since according to the opponent it is placed to exclude what comes before, whether multiple or single, so its benefit depends on attachment to all, so there is necessity in it. So understand. And there is no escape from it except by saying: it necessarily requires attachment because it is not independent, and the origin for the dependent element is to follow the operator if it suffices for benefit, and here the last suffices to remove the necessity of attachment, so the apparent is its attachment to the last. So reflect on it with true reflection. And what is in al-Minhaj of rebuttal by condition, state, attribute, etc., for the premises of the proof apply to them while they are for all by agreement. So therein there is no agreement except in the condition regarding attachment to all, especially as stated by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, the author of al-Mahsil, so there is no rebuttal except by it, not by attribute and others, for they are for the last according to us, and the distinction between condition and exception will come later, so the rebuttal is repelled by it, so wait. Exception. This. The Shafi'is said: Firstly: conjunction makes the multiple like a single, so it makes sentences like one, so what attaches to one is what attaches to all. I say: This would only be complete if the conjunction of the second to the first were without the exception, for then all becomes one by conjunction, so there is no meaning to attaching the exception to one only. And it, i.e., the conjunction of the second to the first without the exception, is denied; rather, it is permissible that it attaches first to the last, then it is conjoined to the first, and all becomes like one sentence, so its attachment to all is not necessitated. And it was answered in the well-known view that that, i.e., the multiplicity becoming like one, in conjunction of single words is real, like 'Zayd and Bakr came', or by ruling like sentences that have a grammatical position or occur as a relative clause. As for conjunction of non-single words, no, because it is certain that like 'Banu Tamim and Bakr struck, are brave' is not in this ruling. And it appears from the proof and its answer that exception from a single conjoined word is exception from the conjoined to it, because they are like one thing. And this befits what has passed that restrictions of one of the conjoined are restrictions for the other due to partnership, and the discussion has passed. Then it is objected that the adjective and the limit are not restricted except by the last singular, while it is like the exception and other restrictions. So the truth is the answer of the author, and this is concessional, so understand. And they said: Secondly: if he said, 'By Allah, I will not eat and I will not drink, if Allah wills,' it attaches to both by agreement between us and you, so he does not break his oath by eating or drinking. And it was answered that it, i.e., 'if Allah wills,' is a condition, not an exception, so it is not of what we are discussing. If it is likened to it because it is a specification like it, so it would be like it in rulings, it would be analogy in language, and we have been forbidden from it. And if they say, we found that the usages of non-independent specifiers are on one pattern, so no analogy, we say: not so, but the condition is for suspensory ruling, unlike exception, for it is immediate, and unity of what is placed for types of suspensory and immediate rulings in rulings is not necessary. Do you not see that the condition may entail the negation of the consequence entirely, while the exception is not like that. And the claim of induction of the genus without induction of this type from it is not valid; rather, in induction of the genus it is necessary...
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a detailed disputation on whether an exception (istithna') after a series of conjoined sentences (ma'tufat) returns to all the sentences or only the last one. The Hanafi position is that, by default, it returns only to the immediately preceding clause (al-akhirah), unless there is a contextual indicator (qarina) to the contrary. The Shafi'is argue that the conjunction ('atf) makes the multiple clauses like a single sentence, so the exception applies to all. The text first presents Hanafi arguments and rebuttals. A key Hanafi argument is based on custom ('urf): when multiple conjoined clauses are lengthy, custom does not consider the exception connected to the first. The proper condition (shart) for exception to return to all is that the speaker does not take a pause or start a new speech; here, starting a new clause after the conjunction is like a new speech, so the exception only attaches to the last. Another Hanafi argument is from the example of 'ten except four except two': the result is eight, not six, showing that the second exception only applies to the adjacent clause. This is a qiyas (analogy) that exception attaches to what it follows. The Shafi'is counter with the example of an oath conditioned by 'if Allah wills' (in sha Allah), which applies to all clauses by agreement. The Hanafi response distinguishes that 'in sha Allah' is a condition (shart), not an exception, and conditions have different rules: they suspend the ruling, while exceptions are immediate. Thus, analogy is not valid. The passage concludes that the Hanafi position is the chosen one (al-mukhtar). The discussion also touches on technical usul concepts such as darura (necessity), qarina, tanazu' (conflict), and the distinction between conventional (wad'i) and necessary (daruri) attachment.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna'): An exception; a particle (e.g., illa) that excludes something from the preceding general statement.
عطف ('atf): Conjunction; linking words or sentences with a conjunction like 'wa' (and), 'fa' (then), etc.
قرينة (qarina): A contextual indicator or circumstantial evidence that modifies the apparent meaning of speech.
ضرورة (darura): Necessity; the need for the exception to attach to something for the speech to be meaningful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, if someone says 'I give Zayd ten and I give Bakr five except two,' how much does Bakr receive?
A) Five dirhams (the exception is ignored).
B) Three dirhams (five minus two).
C) Eight dirhams (the exception applies to all).
D) Zero dirhams (the exception invalidates the gift).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi default is that an exception after conjoined sentences restricts only the immediately preceding clause, a principle supported by custom, logical necessity, and the famed 'ten except four except two' analogy.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
15 min
The Shafi'i Challenge and Hanafi Defense on Istithna' after Conjoined Sentences
Shafi'i objections and Hanafi responses on istithna' after conjoined sentences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Shafi'i argument that conjunction unifies clauses for the purpose of exception, and critically evaluate the Hanafi rebuttal distinguishing condition from exception.

Core Idea
The Shafi'i claim that 'atf makes multiple clauses like one is rebutted by the Hanafi distinction: exception applies to the last clause, and the oath example is inapposite because it involves a condition, not an exception.

Having established the Hanafi position in the first part, we now turn to the Shafi'i objections and the Hanafi responses that solidify the school's stance. The Shafi'is present two main arguments: first, that conjunction ('atf) turns multiple sentences into a single sentence, so an exception to any part is an exception to all; second, that in oaths conditioned by 'in sha Allah', the condition applies to all clauses by agreement, suggesting that exceptions should similarly apply to all. The Hanafi response carefully dismantles each argument by analyzing linguistic structure and the fundamental difference between condition (shart) and exception (istithna'). This lesson sharpens your understanding of how usul principles are debated and defended.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i first argument and its basis
The Shafi'is argue that 'atf (conjunction) makes multiple clauses functionally single, so an exception to one is an exception to all. They support this with examples like 'Zayd and Bakr came' where the conjunction unifies the subjects.
Key concept: al-'atf yaj'alu al-muta'addida kal-wahida (conjunction makes the multiple like one).
2
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal to the first argument
The Hanafis respond that this unification only holds if the exception were not present; with an exception, the second clause is a new speech. They also note that unification is only real in single words, not in conjoined sentences without grammatical position. The exception, being a restriction, does not retroact to earlier clauses unless a qarina is present.
The Hanafis distinguish between 'atf of single words (real) and 'atf of sentences (not real).
3
Present the Shafi'i second argument from the oath example
The Shafi'is cite the oath 'By Allah, I will not eat nor drink, if Allah wills,' where the condition 'if Allah wills' applies to both clauses by agreement, arguing that exception should behave similarly.
This is a strong analogy for the Shafi'is because it seems to show that a restriction after conjoined clauses covers all.
4
Examine the Hanafi distinction between shart and istithna'
The Hanafis rebut by showing that 'in sha Allah' is a condition (shart), not an exception. Conditions are suspensory: they make the ruling contingent on the condition. Exceptions are immediate: they directly exclude. These are different linguistic operations, so analogy is invalid. Additionally, conditions can negate the entire consequence, while exceptions only remove part.
Key distinction: shart = ta'liq (suspension), istithna' = tanjiz (immediate exclusion). The Hanafis reject qiyas in language (qiyas fi al-lugha).
5
Summarize the tarjih and its significance
The Hanafis consider their position preponderant because the Shafi'i arguments fail: the first relies on a false unification, and the second confuses two separate categories. The practical impact is that in legal documents (wills, oaths, contracts), the Hanafi default is to apply the exception only to the last clause, leading to different outcomes than the Shafi'i approach.

Source Text

يعطف أيضاً، وفي صورة عدم العطف لا تعلق لأحدهما بالآخر فكذا في العطف، واعترض بأن الشرط في الاستثناء الاتصال العرفي وهو متحقق فإن العرف لا يعده متأخراً عن الأول، وجوابه ظاهر، لأن الجمل المتعاطفة قد تستوعب الساعات إذا ذكر الاستثناء بعدها، ولا يحكم عاقل بأنه متصل بالأولى لا حقيقة ولا عرفاً وغير المتعاطفة اثنين أو ثلاثة إذا قرن بعدها استثناء، مثل المتعاطفة اثنين أو ثلاثة فإن اكتفى بهذا الاتصال العرفي فالمتعاطفة وغيرها سيان فيحكم برجوعه إلى الكل إذا كانت الجمل قليلة، بحيث يقال في العرف إنه كلام واحد وإن لم تكن متعاطفة بخلاف الكثير وإن كانت متعاطفة أن غير المتعاطفة لا يجوز فيها الرجوع اتفاقاً إلا إلى ما يليه، فقد ظهر أنه لا يكفي هذا الاتصال العرفي بل الذي هو شرط هو السكوت من غير عذر أو الأخذ في كلام آخر، وظاهر فيما نحن فيه أنه ترك الكلام الأول وأخذ في الآخر فلا يصح الاستثناء عنه بعده فتدبر، وهذا يكفي للناظر المنصف، واعترض أيضاً بأن الدليل لو تم لدل على عدم جواز تعلقه بالكل مع أنه يجوز بقرينة، ولك أن تجيب بأنه ربما ينزل الانفصال منزلة العدم لأمور خطابية وينزل الجمل المتعددة بالعطف منزلة جملة واحدة، فلا يعد أخذه في أخرى تركاً لها، بل إتماماً لها في المقامات الخطابية، لكن يحتاج إلى القرينة لكونه خلاف الظاهر فلا يدل دليلنا على عدم الجواز مطلقاً، بل إذا لم يكن صارف فقط، ألا ترى أنه كثيراً ما ينزل وجود الشيء منزلة العدم في المقامات الخطابية، فينزل العالم منزلة الجاهل لعدم العمل بمقتضاه وبالعكس لظهور أمره حقيقة أو ادعاء وغير ذلك مما بين في فن المعاني، فكذا ههنا فاحفظ فإنه من مزال الأقدام، ولنا ثالثاً : لو كان متعلقاً بالكل، لزم توجه الفعلين إلى متعلق واحد وهو التنازع ، ولا شك أن باب غير التنازع أكثر فيحمل عليه إلا بدليل لأن الظن تابع للأغلب فتدبر (واستدل) على المختار (أولاً : لو قال علي عشرة إلا أربعة إلا اثنين لزم ثمانية) فلم يتعلق الاستثناء إلا بما يليه وإن تعلق بالكل لزم ستة (ويجاب بأنه في غير محل النزاع لعدم العطف والجملة) ههنا (قيل) في شرح المختصر (و) لم يتعلق بالكل للتعذر) المانع إياه ( وإلا) يتعذر بل يصح (كان الاثنان مثبتاً) لكونهما مستثنيين عن الاستثناء المفيد للنفي (منفياً) لكونهما أيضاً مستثنيين من العشرة المثبتة وثبوت شيء واحد وانتفاؤه محال (أقول) في رده (وحدة الموضوع من شروط التناقض وليس الأظهر، وليست وحدة الموضوع متحققة ههنا لأن الاثنين المثبتين من جملة الأربعة المستثناة والمنفيين من جملة الستة الباقية وإن قيل نوع الاثنين واحد فوحدة الموضوع متحققة قلت: اجتماع المتنافيين في الواحد النوعي غير مستحيل كما لا يخفى فتدبر (و) استدل (ثانياً بأن عمله لعدم استقلاله ضروري) فإن غير المستقل يقتضي التعلق والارتباط (وما وجب للضرورة يقدر بقدرها ولا يتعداها (والأخيرة متعينة) للتعلق لأن الكلام فيما لا صارف وبها تندفع الضرورة، فلا يتعلق بما عداها (ويجاب بأنه وضعي أي وضع للتعلق بالجملة (لا) ضروري حتى لا يتجاوز قدرها، وفي «التحرير» إن أريد أنه وضع للتعلق بالأخيرة فتم مطلوبنا، وإن أريد أنه وضع للتعلق بالكل فهو ممنوع وظاهره غير موجه لأنه منع على المنع ووجه بأنه ممنوع وباطل لأنه يستعمل للأخيرة، والأصل الحقيقة، وفيه : أن الخصم لا يسلم الاستعمال من غير صارف عن الأولى، ومطلق الاستعمال لا يفيد مع أنه لو تم لغا مقدمات أصل الدليل، وربما يقرر بأن المراد بالضرورة عدم الإفادة من غير تعلق، وإن كان التعلق وضعياً فالاستثناء لعدم استقلاله ضروري التعلق، والأخيرة تكفي فلا يتعلق بما عداها فحينئذ يندفع لكن يرد حينئذ وروداً ظاهراً ما أشار إليه بقوله (أقول: وأيضاً الكلام في قدر الضرورة فإنه لم لا يجوز أن تكون الضرورة مقتضية للتعلق بالجميع، كيف لا وأنه عند الخصم موضوع للإخراج عما قبله متعدداً كان أو واحداً فإفادته موقوفة على التعلق بالكل ففيه الضرورة (فافهم) ولا مخلص عنه إلا بأن يقال إنه ضروري التعلق لأنه غير مستقل، والأصل في المعمول أن يلي العامل إن كفى الإفادة، وههنا الأخيرة كافية لدفع ضرورة التعلق فالظاهر تعلقه بالأخيرة فتأمل فيه تأملاً صادقاً وما) في المنهاج من النقض بالحال والشرط والصفة وغيرها فإن مقدمات الدليل جارية فيها مع أنها للكل اتفاقاً (ففيه أنه لا اتفاق إلا في الشرط) في التعلق بالجميع (خاصة كما صرح به الإمام فخر الدين (الرازي) صاحب المحصول فلا نقض إلا به لا بالصفة وغيرها، فإنها للأخيرة عندنا وسيأتي وجه الفرق بين الشرط والاستثناء فيندفع به النقض فانتظر.
الاستثناء
هذا
الشافعية قالوا : أوّلاً: العطف يجعل المتعدد (كالمفرد فيجعل الجمل كالواحدة فالمتعلق بالواحد هو المتعلق بالكل (أقول : إنما يتم لو كان عطف الثانية على الأولى بدون الاستثناء) فإنه حينئذ صار الكل بالعطف واحدة فلا معنى لتعلق الاستثناء بواحد لا غير (وهو) أي عطف الثانية على الأولى بدون الاستثناء (ممنوع) بل يجوز أن يتعلق أولاً بالأخيرة ثم هي مع عطفت على الأولى، وصارت الكل بمنزلة جملة واحدة فلا يلزم تعلقه بالكل (وأجيب في المشهور بأن ذلك أي صيرورة المتعددة كالواحد (في) عطف (المفردات حقيقة نحو : جاء زيد وبكر أو حكماً كالجمل التي لها محل من الإعراب أو وقعت صلة) وأما في عطف غير المفردات فلا للقطع بأن نحو ضرب بنو تميم وبكر شجعان ليس في حكمه) ويظهر من الدليل وجوابه أن الاستثناء من المعطوف المفرد استثناء من المعطوف عليه، لأنهما كشيء واحد، وهذا يناسب ما مر من أن قيود أحد المتعاطفين قيود للآخر للتشريك، وقد مر الكلام فيه، ثم يرد عليه أن الصفة والغاية لا يتقيد به إلا المفرد الأخير مع أنه كالاستثناء وسائر القيود فالحق إذاً جواب المصنف، وهذا تنزلي فافهم (و) قالوا :(ثانياً : لو قال : والله لا أكلت ولا شربت إن شاء الله تعالى تعلق بهما اتفاقاً) بيننا وبينكم فلا يحنث بالأكل ولا بالشرب (وأجيب بأنه) أي إن شاء الله تعالى (شرط) لا استثناء) فليس مما نحن فيه فإن ألحق به لأنه تخصيص مثله فيكون مثله في الأحكام (كان) قياساً في اللغة وقد نهينا عنه، وإن قالوا: وجدنا محاورات المخصصات الغير المستقلة على نمط واحد فلا قياس قلنا ليس كذلك بل الشرط للحكم التعليقي بخلاف الاستثناء فإنه تنجيز ولا يلزم اتحاد ما وضع لنوعي الحكم التعليقي والتنجيزي في الأحكام، ألا تری أن الشرط قد يفيد انتفاء الجزاء بالكلية والاستثناء ليس كذلك، ودعوى الاستقراء في الجنس من غير استقراء هذا النوع منه لا يصح، بل لا بد في استقراء الجنس من
And it is also conjoined. In the case of no conjunction, one has no relation to the other, so likewise in conjunction. It was objected that the condition in exception is customary connection (al-ittisal al-'urfi), and that is realized, because custom does not consider it to be later than the first. Its answer is apparent, because conjoined sentences may occupy hours when the exception is mentioned after them, and no rational person judges that it is connected to the first, neither in reality nor customarily. And non-conjoined sentences, two or three, when an exception is appended after them, are like conjoined two or three. If one is satisfied with this customary connection, then conjoined and non-conjoined are equal, so it is judged to revert to all if the sentences are few, such that customarily it is considered one speech, even if not conjoined, unlike many, even if conjoined. But non-conjoined, it is not permissible to revert (to all) by agreement, except to what immediately precedes. So it has become clear that this customary connection is not sufficient; rather, the condition is silence without excuse or beginning another speech. And it is apparent in our case that he left the first speech and began another, so exception after it is not valid. So ponder. And this is sufficient for the impartial observer. And it was also objected that if the proof were complete, it would indicate the impermissibility of attaching it to all, though it is permissible with a qarina (contextual indicator). And you may answer that perhaps separation is treated as non-existence for rhetorical purposes, and multiple sentences conjoined are treated as a single sentence, so beginning another is not considered leaving it, but rather completing it in rhetorical contexts. However, a qarina is needed because it is contrary to the apparent. So our proof does not indicate absolute impermissibility, but only when there is no diverting factor. Do you not see that often the existence of a thing is treated as non-existence in rhetorical contexts, so the knowledgeable person is treated as ignorant for not acting accordingly, and vice versa due to the obviousness of his matter in reality or by allegation, and other matters explained in the science of meanings. So here as well, so memorize, for it is a slippery slope. And thirdly for us: if it were attached to all, it would necessitate directing two actions to a single object, which is conflict (tanazu'). And there is no doubt that the sphere of non-conflict is more frequent, so it is interpreted accordingly unless there is evidence, because conjecture follows the majority. So ponder. And they proved (the chosen position) firstly: if he says, 'I owe ten except four except two,' eight is incumbent. So the exception attached only to what immediately follows; if it attached to all, six would be incumbent. And it is answered that this is not the locus of dispute because there is no conjunction and the sentence... here it is said in Sharh al-Mukhtasar: and it did not attach to all due to impossibility which prevents it. Otherwise, if it were not impossible but valid, the two would be affirmed (as affirmed) because they are excepted from the exception which conveys negation, and negated because they are also excepted from the affirmed ten, and the affirmation and negation of one thing is impossible. I say in refutation: unity of subject is a condition of contradiction, and it is not obvious. Unity of subject is not realized here because the affirmed two are from the excepted four, and the negated two are from the remaining six. If it is said that the type of two is one, then unity of subject is realized, I say: combination of contradictories in a single type is not impossible, as is not hidden. So ponder. And they proved secondly: because its operation is necessary due to its lack of independence, for what is not independent requires attachment and connection. And what is necessitated by necessity is measured by it and does not exceed it. And the last clause is specified for attachment because the speech is about that which has no diverting factor, and by it necessity is removed, so it does not attach to what is other than it. And it is answered that it is conventional (wad'i), i.e., it is placed to attach to the sentence, not necessary such that it does not exceed its measure. And in al-Tahrir: if it is meant that it is placed to attach to the last, then our desired is established; if it is meant that it is placed to attach to all, it is denied and its apparent is not directed because it is a denial upon denial. And it is directed that it is denied and false because it is used for the last, and the principle is reality. And therein: the opponent does not concede usage without a diverting factor from the first, and absolute usage is not beneficial, and if it were complete, the premises of the original proof would be invalid. And perhaps it is established that by necessity is meant lack of benefit without attachment, and even if the attachment is conventional, the exception, due to its lack of independence, necessarily requires attachment, and the last suffices, so it does not attach to what is other than it. Then at that point it is repelled, but then there occurs an apparent objection to what he indicated by his saying: I say: also the discussion is about the extent of necessity, for why is it not permissible that necessity demands attachment to all? How not, since according to the opponent it is placed to exclude what comes before, whether multiple or single, so its benefit depends on attachment to all, so there is necessity in it. So understand. And there is no escape from it except by saying: it necessarily requires attachment because it is not independent, and the origin for the dependent element is to follow the operator if it suffices for benefit, and here the last suffices to remove the necessity of attachment, so the apparent is its attachment to the last. So reflect on it with true reflection. And what is in al-Minhaj of rebuttal by condition, state, attribute, etc., for the premises of the proof apply to them while they are for all by agreement. So therein there is no agreement except in the condition regarding attachment to all, especially as stated by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, the author of al-Mahsil, so there is no rebuttal except by it, not by attribute and others, for they are for the last according to us, and the distinction between condition and exception will come later, so the rebuttal is repelled by it, so wait. Exception. This. The Shafi'is said: Firstly: conjunction makes the multiple like a single, so it makes sentences like one, so what attaches to one is what attaches to all. I say: This would only be complete if the conjunction of the second to the first were without the exception, for then all becomes one by conjunction, so there is no meaning to attaching the exception to one only. And it, i.e., the conjunction of the second to the first without the exception, is denied; rather, it is permissible that it attaches first to the last, then it is conjoined to the first, and all becomes like one sentence, so its attachment to all is not necessitated. And it was answered in the well-known view that that, i.e., the multiplicity becoming like one, in conjunction of single words is real, like 'Zayd and Bakr came', or by ruling like sentences that have a grammatical position or occur as a relative clause. As for conjunction of non-single words, no, because it is certain that like 'Banu Tamim and Bakr struck, are brave' is not in this ruling. And it appears from the proof and its answer that exception from a single conjoined word is exception from the conjoined to it, because they are like one thing. And this befits what has passed that restrictions of one of the conjoined are restrictions for the other due to partnership, and the discussion has passed. Then it is objected that the adjective and the limit are not restricted except by the last singular, while it is like the exception and other restrictions. So the truth is the answer of the author, and this is concessional, so understand. And they said: Secondly: if he said, 'By Allah, I will not eat and I will not drink, if Allah wills,' it attaches to both by agreement between us and you, so he does not break his oath by eating or drinking. And it was answered that it, i.e., 'if Allah wills,' is a condition, not an exception, so it is not of what we are discussing. If it is likened to it because it is a specification like it, so it would be like it in rulings, it would be analogy in language, and we have been forbidden from it. And if they say, we found that the usages of non-independent specifiers are on one pattern, so no analogy, we say: not so, but the condition is for suspensory ruling, unlike exception, for it is immediate, and unity of what is placed for types of suspensory and immediate rulings in rulings is not necessary. Do you not see that the condition may entail the negation of the consequence entirely, while the exception is not like that. And the claim of induction of the genus without induction of this type from it is not valid; rather, in induction of the genus it is necessary...
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is a detailed disputation on whether an exception (istithna') after a series of conjoined sentences (ma'tufat) returns to all the sentences or only the last one. The Hanafi position is that, by default, it returns only to the immediately preceding clause (al-akhirah), unless there is a contextual indicator (qarina) to the contrary. The Shafi'is argue that the conjunction ('atf) makes the multiple clauses like a single sentence, so the exception applies to all. The text first presents Hanafi arguments and rebuttals. A key Hanafi argument is based on custom ('urf): when multiple conjoined clauses are lengthy, custom does not consider the exception connected to the first. The proper condition (shart) for exception to return to all is that the speaker does not take a pause or start a new speech; here, starting a new clause after the conjunction is like a new speech, so the exception only attaches to the last. Another Hanafi argument is from the example of 'ten except four except two': the result is eight, not six, showing that the second exception only applies to the adjacent clause. This is a qiyas (analogy) that exception attaches to what it follows. The Shafi'is counter with the example of an oath conditioned by 'if Allah wills' (in sha Allah), which applies to all clauses by agreement. The Hanafi response distinguishes that 'in sha Allah' is a condition (shart), not an exception, and conditions have different rules: they suspend the ruling, while exceptions are immediate. Thus, analogy is not valid. The passage concludes that the Hanafi position is the chosen one (al-mukhtar). The discussion also touches on technical usul concepts such as darura (necessity), qarina, tanazu' (conflict), and the distinction between conventional (wad'i) and necessary (daruri) attachment.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): Condition; a suspending clause that makes the ruling conditional upon its occurrence.
قياس في اللغة (qiyas fi al-lugha): Analogy in language; applying a linguistic rule from one category to another without direct evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject the Shafi'i analogy that exception should apply to all conjoined clauses because a condition (shart) in an oath applies to all?
A) Because the Hanafis do not accept analogy (qiyas) in usul al-fiqh.
B) Because condition (shart) is suspensory, while exception (istithna') is immediate; they are different linguistic operations.
C) Because the Hanafis believe that oaths are not subject to conditions.
D) Because the Shafi'i example of 'in sha Allah' applies only to the first clause, not both.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's position that istithna' attaches only to the last clause is defended by exposing the category error in the Shafi'i analogy between condition and exception.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
Hanafi Rebuttal of Shafi'i Arguments on Exception Attachment
Hanafi response to four Shafi'i proofs on istithna attachment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four Shafi'i arguments for universal exception attachment and state the Hanafi rebuttal for each.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, an exception attaches only to the last clause unless a contextual indicator shows otherwise.

This lesson dives into a classic usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: when a speaker says, 'I did not eat, nor did I drink, except ...', does the exception apply to both clauses or only the last? The Shafi'is advance four proofs for universal attachment; the Hanafis systematically rebut each. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to critically evaluate linguistic evidence in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position and first proof
The Shafi'is argue that conjunction (atf) makes multiple clauses function as one unit, so an exception applies to all. Identify this claim and the Hanafi response: the exception first attaches to the last clause, and only then is the last clause conjoined to the first.
Note the Hanafi distinction between conjunction of individual words and full sentences.
2
Examine the second proof based on oaths
The Shafi'is cite the example: 'By Allah, I will not eat nor drink if Allah wills' – here 'if Allah wills' suspends both clauses by agreement. The Hanafis respond that 'if Allah wills' is a condition (shart), not an exception, and conditions differ in being suspensory and virtually advanced.
Key difference: condition can be advanced virtually, exception is delayed and categorical.
3
Analyze the third proof regarding speaker's purpose
The Shafi'is claim that if the purpose is to except from all, repetition is cumbersome, so a single delayed exception covers all. The Hanafi answer denies that repetition is inherently objectionable and notes alternative ways to indicate all (context, explicit wording).
The Hanafis also argue that 'determination' (ta'ayyun) of delay as the only way is denied.
4
Assess the fourth proof about suitability and arbitrariness
The Shafi'is argue that an exception is suitable for all clauses, so restricting it to the last is arbitrary (tahakkum). The Hanafis agree on suitability but introduce proximity (qurb) and certainty as preponderating factors (tarjih) that make the restriction non-arbitrary.
The Hanafi reply shows that both sides could accuse each other of arbitrariness, but the Hanafis have a valid preferrer.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
In legal interpretation, a Hanafi will apply an exception only to the immediately preceding clause unless a qarina indicates otherwise, while a Shafi'i will apply it to all preceding clauses. This affects oaths, contracts, and testamentary statements.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the position defended here.

فلا يلزم تعلقه بالكل (وأجيب في المشهور بأن ذلك أي صيرورة المتعددة كالواحد (في) عطف (المفردات حقيقة نحو : جاء زيد وبكر أو حكماً كالجمل التي لها محل من الإعراب أو وقعت صلة) وأما في عطف غير المفردات فلا للآخر للتشريك، وقد مر الكلام فيه، ثم يرد عليه أن الصفة والغاية لا يتقيد به إلا المفرد الأخير مع أنه كالاستثناء وسائر القيود فالحق إذاً جواب المصنف، وهذا تنزلي فافهم (و) قالوا :(ثانياً : لو قال : والله لا أكلت ولا شربت إن شاء الله تعالى تعلق بهما اتفاقاً) بيننا وبينكم فلا يحنث بالأكل ولا بالشرب (وأجيب بأنه) أي إن شاء الله تعالى (شرط) لا استثناء) فليس مما نحن فيه فإن ألحق به لأنه تخصيص مثله فيكون مثله في الأحكام (كان) قياساً في اللغة وقد نهينا عنه، وإن قالوا: وجدنا محاورات المخصصات الغير المستقلة على نمط واحد فلا قياس قلنا ليس كذلك بل الشرط للحكم التعليقي بخلاف الاستثناء فإنه تنجيز ولا يلزم اتحاد ما وضع لنوعي الحكم التعليقي والتنجيزي في الأحكام، ألا تری أن الشرط قد يفيد انتفاء الجزاء بالكلية والاستثناء ليس كذلك، ودعوى الاستقراء في الجنس من غير استقراء هذا النوع منه لا يصح، بل لا بد في استقراء الجنس من استقراء كل نوع منه فليس إلا القياس فتدبر، فإنه واضح على أن الشرط مقدم تقديراً) لأن له صدارة الكلام باتفاق النحاة فيصح تعلقه بالأوّل، لأنه مقارن له تقديراً (بخلاف الاستثناء) فإنه مؤخر فلا يتعلق إلا بما يليه، فقياسه على الشرط قياس مع الفارق، قال «مطلع الأسرار الإلهية»: تقدم الشرط تقديراً يرشدك إلى مذهب أهل الميزان فإنه لو كان الشرط بمنزلة الحال والظرف لا يلزم التقدم وتأمل فيه فإن للمجادل أن يقول : إن كلمة كم وإن وقع مفعولاً لا يكون مقدماً للصدارة، وفيه ما فيه (وقد يقال في شرح المختصر الشرط يقدم على ما يرجع إليه) فقط (فلو كان للأخيرة قدم عليها فقط دون الجميع وإن كان للكل تقدم على الكل فلا يلزم من التقدم التقدم على الكل ولا الرجوع إليها فلا يصلح ما ذكرتم (فارقاً) بين الشرط والاستثناء (أقول) في الجواب المراد أنه أي الشرط لما زال عن مكانه) واستدعى التقدم (لم يتعين الأخيرة بالاتصال لأنه زال هذا اللصوق فيقدم على الجميع دفعاً للترجيح بلا مرجح) فإنه لو تقدم على البعض دون بعض وبعد زوال المكان نسبته إلى الكل على السوية يلزم الترجيح من غير مرجح قطعاً، فقدم على الكل فتم الفارق (فافهم) ولا يرد عليه أنه لم لا يجوز أن لا يكون للأخيرة فمكانه قبله فقط وإذا كان تعلقه بالأخيرة أصلح فلا رجحان من غير مرجح مع كونه منعاً على المنع إذ هو في صدد دفع القياس غير موجه لأنه صالح بحسب المعنى للكل، والكلام فيما لا صارف والاتصال في اللفظ لما سقط اعتباره، فليس تعلقه بالأخيرة أولى، لأن نسبته إلى الكل على السوية فلا أصلحية أصلاً كما قررنا فتدبر (وأيضاً : أنه) أي : لا أكلت ولا شربت إن شاء الله تعالى في غير محل النزاع لتحقق قرينة الكل وهو الحلف) والكلام فيما لا قرينة فيه وهذا لا يضر المستدل، فإنه لا يزيد على المناقشة في المثال إذ المقصود قياس الاستثناء على الشرط فتدبر (مع أنه نقل عن بعض الأدباء أن الشرط مختص بالجملة التي تليه فهو والاستثناء سواء (فإن تقدم اختص بالأولى، وإن تأخر فبالثانية) فلا يتم استدلالكم عليهم (و) قالوا :(ثالثاً : الغرض قد يتعلق بالكل) أي قد يكون الغرض الاستثناء عن الكل، فإما أن يكرر بعد كل جملة وإما أن يؤتى بعد واحد أو يؤتى بعد الجميع والتكرار مستهجن) فبطل الأول، وفي الثاني ترجيح من غير مرجح بقي الثالث (فيلزم الظهور فيه) أي ظهور الاستثناء المتأخر عن الكل في الكل (لتعينه) أي التأخر عن الكل (طريقاً إليه) أي إلى التعلق بالكل وهو المدعي قلنا لا استهجان) أصلاً في التكرار إلا مع قرينة الاتصال والتعلق بالكل ولا كلام فيه على أن (التعين أي تعين التأخير طريقاً إليه (ممنوع لجواز نصب قرينة الكل) فهذا طريق آخر (أو) لجواز التصريح بإلا كذا في الجميع فهذا طريق آخر (و) قالوا رابعاً: صلح الاستثناء المذكور عقيب الجمل (للجميع فالقصر) على الأخيرة (تحكم، قلنا) الاستثناء المذكور (صالح) لكل من الأخيرة والجميع، فالكل) (تحكم) فما هو جوابكم فهو جوابنا على أن القرب من الأخيرة (والتيقن) بكونه لها (مرجح) فلا تحكم (مع أنه لا يستلزم) ما ذكرتم (الظهور) في الكل ومدعاكم هذا بل حديث التحكم والترجيح من غير مرجح يكون للقدر المشترك كالجمع المنكر إلا أن يقال : هذا الدليل لإبطال رأي التعلق بالأخيرة لا
The exception [istithna]: The Shafi'is said: First: Conjunction (atf) makes the multiple like a single [phrase], so it makes the sentences like one, so what is attached to one is attached to all. (I say: That would only be if the second was joined to the first without the exception). For then the whole becomes one by conjunction, so there is no meaning to attaching the exception to only one. (That is, the conjunction of the second to the first without the exception is denied). Rather, it is possible that it first attaches to the last, then that last is conjoined to the first, and the whole becomes like one sentence, so it does not necessitate its attachment to all. (And it was answered in the well-known [view] that making the multiple like one is true in conjunction of individual phrases like 'Zayd and Bakr came' or in effect like sentences that have a place in parsing or occur as a relative clause). As for the conjunction of non-individuals, it is not [like that] by cut determination, because 'Banu Tamim and Bakr are brave' is not in its ruling. And it appears from the proof and its answer that the exception from a conjoined individual is an exception from the conjoined-to, because they are like one thing. This suits what has passed that the qualifications of one of the conjoined are qualifications for the other for participation, and the discussion has passed. Then it is objected that the adjective and limit are not restricted except to the last individual, while it is like the exception and all qualifications, so the correct is if so the answer of the author, and this is concessive, understand. (And they said: Secondly: If he said: By Allah I will not eat and I will not drink if Allah wills, it attaches to both by agreement) between us and you, so he does not break the oath by eating nor by drinking. (And it was answered that it, i.e., 'if Allah wills', is a condition, not an exception) so it is not from our subject. For if it is attached to it because it is a specification like it, then it would be like it in rulings, it would be qiyas in language and we have been forbidden from it. And if they say: we find the discourses of dependent specifications are on one pattern, so there is no qiyas, we say: not so. Rather, the condition is for suspensory ruling contrary to the exception, for it is categorical, and it is not necessary that what is placed for the two types of suspensory and categorical rulings be united in rulings. Do you not see that the condition may entail the complete negation of the result, while the exception is not like that. The claim of induction in the genus without induction of this species is invalid; rather, induction of the genus requires induction of every species, so it is nothing but qiyas, so ponder. For it is clear that the condition is advanced virtually, because it has precedence of speech by agreement of grammarians, so it is correct to attach it to the first, because it is concurrent with it virtually (contrary to the exception), for it is delayed, so it attaches only to that which it immediately follows. So qiyas of it upon the condition is qiyas with a difference. The author of 'Matla' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya' said: The virtual advance of the condition guides you to the school of the people of the balance; for if the condition were like the state and adverb, advance would not be necessary. And reflect on it, for the disputant can say: the word 'kam' even if it occurs as an object is not advanced for precedence. And there is in it what is in it. (And it is said in Sharh al-Mukhtasar: the condition is advanced only over what it refers back to). So if it is for the last, it is advanced only over it not over all; and if it is for all, it is advanced over all. So advance does not entail advance over all nor reference back to them, so what you mentioned does not serve as a difference between the condition and exception. (I say) in the answer: the meaning is that the condition, when it departed from its place and required advance, did not become specific to the last by connection because this adherence has gone; so it is advanced over all to avoid preference without preferrer. For if it were advanced over some not others, and after departure of place its ratio to all is equal, preference without preferrer would necessarily follow, so it is advanced over all, so the difference is complete. (Understand) and it is not objected that why may it not be that it is not for the last, so its place is only before it, and if its attachment to the last is more suitable, then there is no preference without preferrer, while it is a prevention upon prevention, for it is in the context of repelling the qiyas, it is not directed because it is suitable in meaning for all, and the discussion is where there is no diverting factor, and the connection in wording when its consideration has fallen, so its attachment to the last is not more likely, because its ratio to all is equal, so there is no superiority at all as we established, so ponder. (And also: that it, i.e., 'I will not eat and I will not drink if Allah wills' is outside the subject of dispute because there is a contextual indicator of all, which is the oath). And the discussion is where there is no indicator, and this does not harm the arguer, for it is no more than a discussion of the example since the purpose is to compare the exception to the condition, so ponder. (Though it is transmitted from some literati that the condition is specific to the sentence that follows it, so it and the exception are equal. So if it is advanced, it is specific to the first; if delayed, to the second). So your argument upon them is not complete. (And they said: Thirdly: The purpose may be attached to all), i.e., the purpose may be to except from all. So either it is repeated after every sentence, or it is brought after one, or it is brought after all. Repetition is objectionable. So the first is invalid, the second involves preference without preferrer, so the third remains. So it necessitates appearance in it, i.e., appearance of the exception delayed after all in all, because delay is determined as the way to it, i.e., to attachment to all, which is the claim. We say: no objection at all in repetition except with a contextual indicator of connection and attachment to all, and no discussion in it. As for (determination, i.e., determination of delay as a way to it) is denied because it is permissible to set up a contextual indicator of all, so this is another way. Or it is permissible to explicitly say 'except so-and-so' in all, so this is another way. (And they said: Fourthly: The mentioned exception is suitable after the sentences) for all, so restricting it to the last is arbitrary. (We say): The mentioned exception is suitable for each of the last and all, so [your claim of] all is arbitrary. So what is your answer is our answer, except that proximity to the last and certainty of it being for it is a preferrer, so it is not arbitrary. Though it does not entail the appearance you mentioned in all, and your claim is this. Rather, talk of arbitrariness and preference without preferrer applies to the common element like the indefinite collective, except that it is said: This proof is for invalidating the opinion of attachment to the last, no...
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi rebuttal to four Shafi'i arguments concerning the attachment of an exception (istithna) phrase when it appears after multiple conjoined clauses. The Shafi'is argue that an exception should apply to all preceding clauses, while the Hanafis maintain that it applies only to the last clause unless a contextual indicator (qarina) shows otherwise. The author systematically addresses each Shafi'i proof. The first Shafi'i argument relies on conjunction (atf) making multiple clauses function as one; the Hanafi response distinguishes between conjunction of individual words and full sentences, and notes that the exception can still attach to the last clause alone because the conjunction of the last to the first occurs after the exception is attached. The second argument uses the example of an oath with 'in sha Allah', which the Shafi'is consider an exception that attaches to both clauses by consensus; the Hanafi reply insists this is a condition (shart), not an exception, and highlights key differences: conditions are suspensory and can be virtually advanced, whereas exceptions are categorical and delayed. The third argument appeals to the speaker's purpose: if the intention is to except from all, repetition is cumbersome, so a single delayed exception must cover all; the Hanafi response denies any inherent objection to repetition and notes alternative ways to indicate inclusion of all, such as contextual clues or explicit phrasing. The fourth argument claims that an exception is equally suitable for all clauses, so restricting it to the last is arbitrary; the Hanafi answer agrees on suitability but points to proximity (qurb) and certainty as preponderating factors (tarjih) that make attachment to the last non-arbitrary. Throughout, the author uses logical reasoning, grammatical principles, and analogical arguments (qiyas) typical of Hanafi usul al-fiqh, asserting that in the absence of a contextual indicator, the default is attachment to the immediate preceding clause.

Key Terms
الاستثناء (al-istithna): A grammatical construction that excludes one or more items from a general statement, e.g., 'I came except Zayd'.
الشرط (al-shart): A conditional phrase (e.g., 'if Allah wills') that suspends the ruling on a condition.
العطف (al-atf): Grammatical conjunction that coordinates two elements.
القرينة (al-qarina): A contextual indicator that clarifies the intended meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in this passage, how does an exception (istithna) phrase attach to multiple conjoined clauses?
A) It attaches to all clauses equally.
B) It attaches only to the first clause.
C) It attaches only to the last clause unless there is a contextual indicator for all.
D) It does not attach to any clause.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, an exception (istithna) following multiple conjoined clauses attaches only to the last clause unless a contextual indicator (qarina) shows the speaker intended otherwise.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
Dispute on Scope of Exception After Multiple Sentences
Debate over exception scope after multiple sentences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that istithna' attaches only to the immediately preceding sentence and evaluate the opposing position.

Core Idea
An exception after multiple independent sentences applies only to the last, because delay and proximity preponderate.

This passage presents a core Hanafi usul principle: when an exception (istithna') appears after a series of separate sentences, it attaches only to the last sentence. This is contrasted with conditional clauses (shart), which are grammatically advanced and thus apply to all. The debate has a direct impact on the interpretation of Quranic verses like the qadhf verse (24:4). We will walk through the five key arguments of the opponents and the Hanafi responses, culminating in the practical thamarah al-khilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
Recognize the dispute: does an exception placed after multiple independent sentences apply to all sentences or only to the last?
Independent sentences mean no conjunction linking them.
2
State the Hanafi Position
The Hanafi position is that the exception applies only to the last sentence. Understand the rationale: exception is inherently delayed in speech and attaches to what immediately precedes it.
Contrast with conditional clauses which have grammatical precedence.
3
Analyze the Opposing Arguments
There are five main arguments from the opposing schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali): analogy with shart, suitability for all, avoidance of repetition, suitability without repetition, and the numerical example.
Each argument is presented and then refuted by the Hanafis.
4
Examine the Hanafi Responses
For each opposing argument, the Hanafi response: disanalogy with shart (condition advanced, exception delayed), proximity and certainty as preponderators, denial of awkwardness in repetition, and distinction of the numerical example as a single sum.
Note the use of linguistic principles and avoidance of preponderance without a preponderator.
5
Apply to the Quranic Example
Apply the rule to the verse of qadhf (Surah al-Nur, 24:4): the exception 'إلا الذين تابوا' is limited to the last clause 'وأولئك هم الفاسقون', so repentance does not restore testimony.
Contrast with the Shafi'i etc. position that applies it to all clauses, accepting testimony after repentance.

لأنه استقراء كل نوع منه فليس إلا القياس فتدبر، فإنه واضح على أن الشرط مقدم تقديراً) لأن له صدارة الكلام باتفاق النحاة فيصح تعلقه بالأوّل، لأنه مقارن له تقديراً (بخلاف الاستثناء) فإنه مؤخر فلا يتعلق إلا بما يليه، فقياسه على الشرط قياس مع الفارق، قال «مطلع الأسرار الإلهية»: تقدم الشرط تقديراً يرشدك إلى مذهب أهل الميزان فإنه لو كان الشرط بمنزلة الحال والظرف لا يلزم التقدم وتأمل فيه فإن للمجادل أن يقول : إن كلمة كم وإن وقع مفعولاً لا يكون مقدماً للصدارة، وفيه ما فيه (وقد يقال في شرح المختصر الشرط يقدم على ما يرجع إليه) فقط (فلو كان للأخيرة قدم عليها فقط دون الجميع وإن كان للكل تقدم على الكل فلا يلزم من التقدم التقدم على الكل ولا الرجوع إليها فلا يصلح ما ذكرتم (فارقاً) بين الشرط والاستثناء (أقول) في الجواب المراد أنه أي الشرط لما زال عن مكانه) واستدعى التقدم (لم يتعين الأخيرة بالاتصال لأنه زال هذا اللصوق فيقدم على الجميع دفعاً للترجيح بلا مرجح) فإنه لو تقدم على البعض دون بعض وبعد زوال المكان نسبته إلى الكل على السوية يلزم الترجيح من غير مرجح قطعاً، فقدم على الكل فتم الفارق (فافهم) ولا يرد عليه أنه لم لا يجوز أن لا يكون للأخيرة فمكانه قبله فقط وإذا كان تعلقه بالأخيرة أصلح فلا رجحان من غير مرجح مع كونه منعاً على المنع إذ هو في صدد دفع القياس غير موجه لأنه صالح بحسب المعنى للكل، والكلام فيما لا صارف والاتصال في اللفظ لما سقط اعتباره، فليس تعلقه بالأخيرة أولى، لأن نسبته إلى الكل على السوية فلا أصلحية أصلاً كما قررنا فتدبر (وأيضاً : أنه) أي : لا أكلت ولا شربت إن شاء الله تعالى في غير محل النزاع لتحقق قرينة الكل وهو الحلف) والكلام فيما لا قرينة فيه وهذا لا يضر المستدل، فإنه لا يزيد على المناقشة في المثال إذ المقصود قياس الاستثناء على الشرط فتدبر (مع أنه نقل عن بعض الأدباء أن الشرط مختص بالجملة التي تليه فهو والاستثناء سواء (فإن تقدم اختص بالأولى، وإن تأخر فبالثانية) فلا يتم استدلالكم عليهم (و) قالوا :(ثالثاً : الغرض قد يتعلق بالكل) أي قد يكون الغرض الاستثناء عن الكل، فإما أن يكرر بعد كل جملة وإما أن يؤتى بعد واحد أو يؤتى بعد الجميع والتكرار مستهجن) فبطل الأول، وفي الثاني ترجيح من غير مرجح بقي الثالث (فيلزم الظهور فيه) أي ظهور الاستثناء المتأخر عن الكل في الكل (لتعينه) أي التأخر عن الكل (طريقاً إليه) أي إلى التعلق بالكل وهو المدعي قلنا لا استهجان) أصلاً في التكرار إلا مع قرينة الاتصال والتعلق بالكل ولا كلام فيه على أن (التعين أي تعين التأخير طريقاً إليه (ممنوع لجواز نصب قرينة الكل) فهذا طريق آخر (أو) لجواز التصريح بإلا كذا في الجميع فهذا طريق آخر (و) قالوا رابعاً: صلح الاستثناء المذكور عقيب الجمل (للجميع فالقصر) على الأخيرة (تحكم، قلنا) الاستثناء المذكور (صالح) لكل من الأخيرة والجميع، فالكل) (تحكم) فما هو جوابكم فهو جوابنا على أن القرب من الأخيرة (والتيقن ) بكونه لها (مرجح) فلا تحكم (مع أنه لا يستلزم) ما ذكرتم (الظهور) في الكل ومدعاكم هذا بل حديث التحكم والترجيح من غير مرجح يكون للقدر المشترك كالجمع المنكر إلا أن يقال : هذا الدليل لإبطال رأي التعلق بالأخيرة لا لإثبات مذهبه ولك أن تقول في الجواب أيضاً بأنه إن أريد أنه صالح للكل في نفس الأمر والاستعمال الصحيح من غير قرينة فلا نسلم ذلك كيف يسلم ذلك من ادعى الظهور في الأخيرة والوضع لها، وإن أريد أنه صالح لها عقلاً واستعمالاً ولو مع قرينة فمسلم. لكن لا يفيدكم كما لا يخفى (و) قالوا (خامساً: لو قال: علي خمسة وخمسة إلا ستة فبالكل) أي يتعلق الاستثناء حينئذ بالكل (اتفاقاً) والأصل الحقيقة قلنا: إنه في غير محل النزاع لوجوه من أنها ليست جملاً، وأن التعلق بالكل لصارف وهو تعذر استثناء الستة من الخمسة، وأنه لو تم الاستثناء فيه عن الكل بما هو الكل في كل واحد والكلام فيه لا في الأول كما لا يخفى أتباع الروافض خذلهم الله تعالى قالوا :أولاً : حسن الاستفهام أيهما (المراد) من التعلق بالأخيرة أو الكل وأنه دليل الاشتراك لأنه لو كان لأحدهما فقط لتبادر وضاع السؤال (قلنا) ليس هو دليل الاشتراك بل الاستفهام إما للجهل (بالحقيقة) لكونها نظرية مجهولة قبل إقامة البرهان (أو لرفع الاحتمال) فإن الظهور في أحدهما لا يمنع احتمال خلافه، إذ ليس محكماً فيه، فيحسن الاستفهام لإزالة الاحتمال ليصير محكماً فيه وهذا الرافضي كيف عمي عن الحق ولم يدر أن حسن الاستفهام لو كان دليل الاشتراك لصار الألفاظ النظرية الحقيقة أو الخفية الدلالة ومظنونها كلها مشتركة، ومن لم يجعل الله له نوراً فما له من نور (و) قالوا (ثانياً: صح) الاستثناء المذكور عقيب الجمل (للجميع وللأخيرة) فقط والأصل (الحقيقة) فيكون حقيقة فيهما (قلنا) هذا جهل، الأصل) عدم الاشتراك بل المجاز خير منه ثم إنه إن أراد الصحة للجميع من غير قرينة وللأخيرة كذلك، فهذا دعوى من كمال بلوغه درجة الغباوة، وكيف ساغ له في مقابلة من يدعي الظهور في أحدهما، وإن أراد الصحة أحدهما، وإن أراد الصحة مع قرينة في أحدهما ففيه مجاز قطعاً، فإثبات الاشتراك منه حماقة فتدبر ( أقول) الاستدلال منقوض بما عدا الأخيرة فإنه صحيح) والأصل الحقيقة ولعله مجاز (بالاتفاق) فإن قلت : إذا كان مجازاً بالاتفاق فلا تثبت الأصالة كونه حقيقة في مقابلته، قلت هذا يعود على الدليل، فإنه حقيقة في أحدهما بإجماع من يعتد بإجماعهم، فلا تثبت الأصالة الاشتراك في مقابلته فتدبر القاضي وحجة الإسلام وأتباعهما (قالوا : بين الجمل بالعطف (يجعلها كالواحدة (والانفصال وانقطاع كل عن صاحبتها حقيقة (يجعلها كالأجانب فيخرج الاستثناء من الأولى (تارة) على تقدير كونها كالواحد (ولا يخرج) الأولى تارة أخرى) على تقدير كونها كالأجانب فلها شبهان والأشكال) والأشباه (يوجب الأشكال) فيتوقف (قلنا إيجاب الأشكال ممنوع) وإنما يوجب لو كانت متساوية في القوة وليس كذلك لما تقدم من الدلائل الدالة على تقوية أحدهما (فائدة) * (الاستثناء في آية القذف التي مر تلاوتها (مقصور على ما يليه) هو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأُوْلَيْكَ هُمُ الْفَاسِقُونَ ﴾ [النور: ٤] (عند الحنفية، فلا يقبل شهادة المحدود في قذف إذا ﴾ تاب) لعموم قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا نَقْبَلُوا لَمْ شَهَدَةٌ أَبَدا ﴾ [النور: ٤] وعدم خروج التائب عنه بالاستثناء (خلافاً للشافعي رحمه الله) كما هو المشهور (ومالك وأحمد كما) هو (في التيسير) فيقبل عندهم، وإنما خالفوا (رداً) له أي للاستثناء (إليه) أي إلى ما يليه (مع) قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا نَقْبَلُواْ
Because the induction of every type of it is nothing but analogy, so ponder. It is clear that the condition is advanced in estimation, because it has the precedence of speech according to the grammarians, so it can be attached to the first, because it is concurrent with it in estimation. Unlike exception, for it is delayed, so it attaches only to what follows it. So measuring it upon the condition is an analogy with a difference. "Matali' al-Asrar al-Ilahiyya" said: The advancement of the condition in estimation guides you to the school of the people of balance. For if the condition were like the state and the adverb, advancement would not be necessary. Ponder on it. For the disputant can say: The word 'kam' even if it occurs as an object is not advanced due to precedence. And there is something in it. And it is said in Sharh al-Mukhtasar: The condition is advanced upon what it refers back to. So if it is for the last, it is advanced upon it only and not all; and if it is for all, it is advanced upon all. So advancement upon all does not necessitate advancement upon the last nor reference back to it. So what you mentioned does not serve as a differentiator between the condition and exception. I say: In the answer, what is meant is that the condition when it is removed from its place and demands advancement, the last is not specified by connection because this adherence is removed, so it is advanced upon all to avoid preponderance without a preponderator. For if it were advanced upon some and not others, and after the removal of place its relation to all is equal, preponderance without a preponderator would necessarily follow. So it is advanced upon all, thus the difference is complete. Understand. And it is not objected: why is it not permissible that it is not for the last, so its place is only before it? And if its attachment to the last is more suitable, there is no preponderance without a preponderator... (text continues with responses to arguments)...
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute about the operation of exception (istithna') when it follows multiple independent sentences. The Hanafi position is that an exception at the end of a series of separate sentences applies only to the last sentence, not to all. The author presents and refutes five arguments from opponents who claim that such an exception applies to all sentences. The first argument uses analogy with conditional clauses (shart), claiming that if a condition is placed after multiple sentences it applies to all. The author responds that condition and exception are different: condition is inherently advanced in meaning, so it can attach to all, while exception is delayed and only attaches to what immediately precedes it. The second argument is that the exception is suitable for both all and the last, so specification to the last is arbitrary. The author counters that proximity and certainty of attachment to the last provide a preponderance. The third argument is that repeating the exception after each sentence is awkward, so placing it once at the end shows it applies to all. The author denies that repetition is awkward except when connection is indicated. The fourth argument is that the exception is suitable for all, so restricting it to the last is arbitrary. The author replies that the same objection applies to their claim that it applies to all. The fifth argument uses an example: 'I owe five and five except six' where the exception must apply to the total (ten minus six = four) by agreement. The author says this is not analogous because it is a single sum, not multiple sentences. Then the author refutes two arguments from the opponents (possibly Rafidis): first, that the appropriateness of asking which is meant indicates ambiguity and therefore common usage; second, that the exception is valid for both all and the last, so it is a homonym. The author denies both. Finally, there is a benefit (fa'ida): In the verse of qadhf (Quran 24:4), the exception 'except those who repent' is limited to the last clause (the following words) according to the Hanafis, so the repentant slanderer's testimony is still rejected. Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools apply the exception to all clauses, thus accepting the testimony after repentance.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithnā'): A linguistic operation that excludes something from the scope of a preceding statement, e.g., 'except'.
شرط (shart): A conditional clause (e.g., 'if') that is grammatically advanced in meaning and can apply to multiple preceding statements.
تعلق (ta'allaq): Attachment or applicability of one part of speech to another.
الجمل (al-jumal): Multiple independent sentences that are not connected by conjunction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, in the verse of qadhf (Quran 24:4), does the exception 'إلا الذين تابوا' apply to the clause 'وَأُوْلَيْكَ هُمُ الْفَاسِقُونَ' or to all preceding clauses?
A) It applies to all preceding clauses, so a repentant slanderer's testimony is accepted.
B) It applies only to the immediately preceding clause 'وأولئك هم الفاسقون', so the repentant slanderer is still not accepted as a witness.
C) It applies only to the first clause about flogging.
D) It does not apply at all because of abrogation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: an exception after multiple independent sentences attaches only to the last sentence due to its inherent delay and proximity, which provides preponderance over alternative interpretations.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Definition of Shart and Its Distinction from Sabab
Defining shart and responding to objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of shart, distinguish it from sabab, and apply the definition to resolve objections about juz' al-sabab and time.

Core Idea
A condition is necessary but not sufficient; a cause is both necessary and sufficient unless prevented.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut delves into the precise Hanafi definition of 'shart' (condition) in usul al-fiqh. Understanding this definition is crucial because it determines how conditions operate in legal reasoning: a condition makes the cause effective but does not itself produce the effect. The passage defends this definition against objections, refining our grasp of the relationship between conditions, causes, and their parts.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition of shart
Identify the core definition: 'al-shart huwa al-amr al-muta'alliq bi al-shay' la yujad bidunihi li-naw' hadha al-ta'allaq, wa la yalzam an yujad 'indahu'. Note the two parts: non-existence without it by type of relation, but existence does not necessitate.
The phrase 'li-naw' hadha al-ta'allaq' is key – it emphasizes the specific type of relation, not any absence.
2
Distinguish shart from sabab
Contrast with sabab: a cause entails its effect (istitba' al-wujud). A condition only enables; it does not bring about. The passage uses this to expose the objection that juz' al-sabab (part of the cause) might be considered a condition.
3
Address the juz' al-sabab objection
The objection: juz' al-sabab also fits the definition because the effect does not exist without it but may exist with it via another cause. The response: the definition considers the type of relation in one specific cause; if multiple causes exist, the part is not the condition for the effect absolutely.
Understand that the definition is tied to a single cause.
4
Resolve the time objection
Time is a condition for performance of prayer but a cause for obligation. The passage explains that one entity can have two different relations: causal for obligation, conditional for performance. This does not violate the definition.
This shows that shart and sabab are not mutually exclusive across different legal categories.
5
Examine the qabd example and multiplicity of conditions
Qabd (possession) is a condition for ownership in hiba but not in sale. The definition holds because qabd is a condition for the specific ownership from hiba, not for ownership in general. The passage then explains why conditions cannot multiply: the definition implies non-existence without each, so the true condition is the common factor.
This leads to the philosophical reasoning about unity of cause.

Source Text
