Specification of the Quran by the Quran: Takhsis vs. Naskh
Usul dispute on takhsis vs. naskh of Quran by Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on takhsis al-Kitab bi al-Kitab, distinguishing between specification (takhsis) and abrogation (naskh) based on chronological order and textual connection.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, a later specific verse not connected to the general abrogates, not specifies.

One of the key disputes between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools concerns whether a later specific Quranic verse can specify a general earlier verse without being connected to it. The Shafi'is allow it absolutely; the Hanafis insist that specification requires immediate connection or a qarīnah—otherwise, the later verse abrogates the earlier. This lesson unpacks the arguments and evidence, focusing on the pregnant women and the Women of the Book verses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the competing positions
State the absolute Shafi'i position and the conditional Hanafi position regarding takhsis of the Quran by the Quran.
Shafi'i: any later specific specifies. Hanafi: only if connected; otherwise naskh.
2
Examine the Shafi'i evidence
Look at the two Quranic examples given by the Shafi'is: the pregnant women verse (al-Talaq 4) and the chaste women of the Book verse (al-Ma'idah 5). Understand why they see these as specification.
3
Apply the Hanafi response
Analyze how the Hanafis reinterpret these examples as abrogation (naskh) by establishing that the alleged specific verses were revealed later, citing Companion testimony (Ibn Mas'ud) and the lack of contiguity.
The key is the chronological order and the absence of connection (mawṣūl).
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical difference: both schools reach the same ruling for the pregnant widow (delivery ends iddah) but differ on the legal reasoning and precedential value for other cases.
The dispute affects how new cases of conflicting general and specific texts are resolved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة (هل يجوز تخصيص الكتاب (بالكتاب أم لا (جوّزه كثيرون من علماء الأصول (مطلقاً) سواء كان العام مقدماً على الخاص أو بالعكس، وسواء كانا متلاصقين أم يكون أحدهما مقدماً أو مؤخراً وهو المختار عند الشافعية (ومنهم) القاضي الإمام أبو زيد وجمع منا هذا شيء عجاب فإن القاضي الإمام صرح في الأسرار» بأن التخصيص لا يكون متراخياً، وما يظن فيه التراخي فليس بياناً، بل رافعاً للحكم الثابت عن بعض الأفراد ومنعه بعض مطلقاً) متراخياً أحدهما عن الآخر وموصولاً كل منهما بصاحبه وفصل الحنفية العراقية والقاضي) أبو بكر (وإمام الحرمين) كلاهما من الشافعية وهو المختار ( بأن الخاص مخصص إن كان متأخراً وموصولاً بالعام ( وإلا) يكن موصولاً فالعام ناسخ) له إن كان متأخراً غير مقارن إلا أن تدل قرينة جزئية على بقاء الحكم الخاص المتقدم، فيخص العام حينئذ كما خص قوله تعالى : وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّمَا غَنِمْتُم مِّن شَيْءٍ فَأَنَّ لِلَّهِ مُسَهُ ﴾ [الأنفال : ٤١] بما سوى سلب المقتول مع كون الحكم بإعطاء السلب للقاتل مقدماً عليه كما مر (أو منسوخ بقدره إن كان مقدماً على الخاص الغير المقارن (ويبقى) هذا العام المنسوخ البعض قطعياً في الباقي لا كالعام له إذا خص منه البعض، والصواب حذف قوله : متأخراً، بل يقال : إن الخاص مخصص إن كان موصولاً (وإن جهل التاريخ) بين العام والخاص (تساقطا) إذا لم يظهر ترجيح أحدهما على الآخر (فيتوقف بقدره إلى دليل آخر كما هو شأن التعارض من إسقاط المتعارضين وطلب الدليل دونه، وإنما قيدنا بعدم ظهور الترجيح لأن صاحب الهداية قال : العام المتفق على صحته مقدم في العمل على الخاص المختلف، ولأن العمل بالرابح أصل متأصل في الباب (ويؤخر المحرم احتياطاً) فإنه لا شناعة في ترك المباح إنما الشناعة في فعل الحرام، ثم إن ما ذكر هو الذي يساعد عليه الدليل وينطبق عليه الفروع الفقهية فإنه عارض النهي عن الصلاة في الأوقات المكروهة قوله : (من أدرك ركعة من الفجر فقد أدرك الفجر ومن أدرك ركعة من العصر فقد أدرك العصر رواه الشيخان ولم يخصصوا العموم به بل أسقطوهما وعملوا بالقياس، فرجح في الفجر حديث النهي وفي العصر الحديث الثاني، وأيضاً : عارض حديث النهي المذكور حديث إباحة الصلاة وقت الاستواء بمكة وبيوم الجمعة، فما خصصوا العموم به بل عملوا بالمحرّم إلى غير ذلك، لكن ما ذكره مخالف لما قال صدر الشريعة وصاحب البديع أنه يحمل على المقارنة وتخصيص العام، وأيضاً ذكر في مبحث التعارض من أصول الإمام فخر الإسلام أن في صورة التعارض يجمع بحمل العام على الخاص وسيصرح به المصنف أيضاً، إلا أن يقال : الأصل أن لا يعمل بهما، لكن الأمر في نفسه أن حكم أحدهما ،ثابت، فلأجل الفتوى يحمل العام على الخاص، وهو أهون من حمل الخاص على المجاز البعيد لئلا تتعطل الحادثة فتأمل فيه، قال (المجوّزون (أولاً) لو لم يكن الخاص مخصصاً للعام الكتابي مطلقاً لما وقع، وقد (وقع كثيراً، منه قوله تعالى : ﴿وَأُوْلَتُ الْأَحْمَالِ أَجَلُهُنَّ أَن يَضَعْنَ حَمْلَهُنَّ ﴾ [الطلاق: ٤] (مخصص لقوله تعالى : وَالَّذِينَ يُتَوَفَّوْنَ مِنكُمْ وَيَذَرُونَ أَزْوَاجًا يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْرًا ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٣٤] فأخرج الحامل المتوفى عنها الزوج وليس بينهما مقارنة (ومنه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالْمُحْصَنَتُ مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُواْ الكتب [المائدة: ٥] مخصص لقوله تعالى ﴿وَلَا تَنكِحُوا الْمُشْرِكَتِ فأخرج الكتابية عن المشركات فإن الكتابية مشركة (للتثليث كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿لَقَدْ كَفَرَ الَّذِينَ قَالُوا إِنَّ اللَّهَ ثَالِثُ ثَلَاثَة [المائدة: ۷۳] نزلت في النصارى (وغيره) من اتخاذ أحبارهم ورهبانهم أرباباً من دون الله ، وقولهم عزير ابن الله والمسيح ابن الله وغير ذلك من حماقاتهم (قلنا) إن القول بالتخصيص باطل بل الكريمة (الأولى) وهي قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأُولَتُ الْأَعْمَالِ ﴾ [الطلاق: ٤] الخ (متأخرة عن الثانية، لقول ابن مسعود من شاء باهلته، أن سورة النساء القصرى نزلت بعد التي في سورة البقرة) كذا ذكره الإمام محمد في الأصل، كذا في التيسير»، وروى عبد الرزاق وابن أبي شيبة وأبو داود والنسائي وابن ماجه عن ابن مسعود أنه بلغه أن علياً يقول : تعتد آخر الأجلين فقال من شاء لاعنته أن الآية التي في سورة النساء القصرى نزلت بعد سورة البقرة بكذا وكذا شهراً وكل مطلقة أو متوفى عنها زوجها فأجلها أن تضع حملها، وأخرج عبد الرزاق وابن أبي شيبة عن ابن مسعود من شاء حالفته أن سورة النساء القصرى أنزلت بعد الأربعة أشهر وعشراً وَأَوَلَتُ الْأَحْمَالِ أَجَلُهُنَّ أَن يَضَعْنَ حَمْلَهُنَّ ﴾ [الطلاق: ٤] والـروايـتـان مـذكـورتـان فـي «الدرر المنثورة»، وإذا ثبت هذا فيكون نسخاً لا تخصيصاً فبطل استدلالهم، ثم القول بكون كريمة أولات الأحمال مخصصة لعله مخالف لإجماع الصحابة، فإن الصحابة اختلفوا في عدة الحامل المتوفى عنها زوجها فأمير المؤمنين علي وابن عباس قالا بأبعد الأجلين، وهذا نوع احتياط للتعارض والجهل بالناسخ، وليس من التخصيص في شيء، وابن مسعود وأبو هريرة قالا بالنسخ، وأما التخصيص فلم ينقل من أحد فتأمل فيه وكذا) والمحصنات) نزلت (بعد) كريمة و ( وَلَا تَنكِحُوا الْمُشْرِكَتِ ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۲۱] ذكره جماعة من المفسرين) فتكون ناسخة لها لا مخصصة، وروى البيهقي في سننه عن ابن عباس في قوله: ﴿وَلَا تَنكِحُوا الْمُشْرِكَتِ حَتَّى يُؤْمِنَ ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۲۱] قال : نسخت وأحل من المشركات نساء أهل الكتاب، وروى أبو داود، في ناسخه عن ابن عباس في قوله: ﴿وَلَا تَنكِحُوا الْمُشْرِكَتِ حَتَّى يُؤْمِنَّ وَلَاَمَةٌ مُؤْمِنَةٌ خَيْرٌ مِن مُّشْرِكَة [البقرة: ۲۲۱] قال : نسخ من ذلك نكاح أهل الكتاب أحلهن للمسلمين وحرم المسلمات على رجالهم، وما وقع في رواية البيهقي عنه رضي الله عنه لفظ استثنى الله من ذلك، فالمراد به النسخ ، إذ لا حقيقة للاستثناء، والمعنى أنه أخرج الله من ذلك التحريم الذي كان ثابتاً وهو
Issue: (Is specification of the Book by the Book permissible or not? (Many of the scholars of usul permitted it (absolutely), whether the general is prior to the specific or vice versa, and whether they are contiguous or one is prior or posterior. This is the chosen view of the Shafi'is. (Among them) is al-Qadi Imam Abu Zayd and a group of us. This is something astonishing, for al-Qadi Imam stated in al-Asrar that specification does not occur with a gap, and what is thought to be with a gap is not explanation, rather it is a remover of the established ruling from some individuals. And some prevented it absolutely) with a gap between them, and connected each with its companion. And the Iraqi Hanafis and al-Qadi Abu Bakr and Imam al-Haramayn (both from the Shafi'is, and it is the chosen view) differentiated: the specific is a specifier if it is later and connected to the general (and if it is not connected, then the general abrogates it if it is later and non-contiguous, unless a particular clue indicates the survival of the earlier specific ruling, then the general is specified, as His statement: 'And know that whatever you take as spoils, then for Allah is a fifth thereof' (al-Anfal 41) was specified by excluding the spoil of the slain while the ruling of giving the spoil to the killer was prior to it, as passed. (Or abrogated to its extent if it is prior to the non-contiguous specific (and this partially abrogated general remains decisive in the remainder, unlike a general if some is specified from it. And the correct is to omit the word 'later', rather it is said: the specific is a specifier if connected (and if the chronology is unknown) between the general and specific (they cancel each other) if no preference appears for one over the other (so they suspend to their extent until another proof, as is the case of conflict: dropping the conflicting proofs and seeking proof without them. And we only qualified by the absence of preference because the author of al-Hidayah said: the general agreed upon its authenticity is given precedence in practice over the specific that is disputed, and because acting with the preponderant is a well-established principle. (And the prohibited is delayed out of precaution) for there is no disgrace in leaving the permissible, but disgrace is in doing the prohibited. Then what he mentioned is what the evidence supports and the furu' al-fiqhiyyah conform to. For the prohibition of prayer in the disliked times conflicted with his statement: 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr has caught Fajr, and whoever catches one rak'ah of 'Asr has caught 'Asr' reported by the two Shaykhs. And they did not specify the generality with it, rather they dropped both and acted by qiyas. So in Fajr the hadith of prohibition was preponderant, and in 'Asr the second hadith. Also, the hadith of prohibition conflicted with the hadith permitting prayer at the time of midday in Makkah and on Friday. So they did not specify the generality with it, but rather acted by the prohibited, etc. However, what he mentioned is contrary to what Sadr al-Shari'ah and the author of al-Badi' said, that it is carried on contiguity and specification of the general. Also, it is mentioned in the discussion of conflict from the Usul of Imam Fakhr al-Islam that in the case of conflict, one should combine by carrying the general on the specific, and the author will also state it. Except that it is said: the principle is not to act by both, but the matter itself is that the ruling of one of them is established, so for the sake of fatwa, the general is carried on the specific, and that is easier than carrying the specific to a far-fetched metaphorical interpretation to avoid the incident being left without a ruling. So ponder on it. The permitters said: (First) if the specific were not a specifier of the general from the Book absolutely, it would not occur, and it has occurred many times. Among them is His statement: 'And those who are pregnant, their term is that they give birth to their burden' (al-Talaq 4) specifying His statement: 'And those who are taken in death among you and leave wives, they shall wait by themselves for four months and ten' (al-Baqarah 234). So it excludes the pregnant woman whose husband dies, and there is no contiguity between them. And among them is His statement: 'And chaste women from those who were given the Book' (al-Ma'idah 5) specifying His statement: 'And do not marry the polytheist women' (al-Baqarah 221). So it excludes the women of the Book from the polytheist women, for the woman of the Book is a polytheist due to trinitarianism as Allah said: 'Certainly, those who say Allah is the third of three have disbelieved' (al-Ma'idah 73) revealed about the Christians, and other things like taking their rabbis and monks as lords besides Allah, and their saying 'Uzayr is the son of Allah and the Messiah is the son of Allah, and other foolishness. (We said) that the claim of specification is false. Rather, the first verse, which is His statement: 'And those who are pregnant' (al-Talaq 4) etc., is later than the second, due to the statement of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Whoever wishes, I will imprecate [mutual curse] him that Surah al-Nisa' al-Qusra was revealed after that in Surah al-Baqarah.' This is what Imam Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl, and likewise in al-Taysir. And Abd al-Razzaq, Ibn Abi Shaybah, Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah narrated from Ibn Mas'ud that it reached him that 'Ali said: 'She observes the later of the two terms,' so he said: 'Whoever wishes, I will imprecate him that the verse in Surah al-Nisa' al-Qusra was revealed after Surah al-Baqarah by such-and-such months, and every divorced woman or woman whose husband dies, her term is that she gives birth to her pregnancy.' And Abd al-Razzaq and Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated from Ibn Mas'ud: 'Whoever wishes, I will assert by oath that Surah al-Nisa' al-Qusra was revealed after the four months and ten, and 'those who are pregnant, their term is that they give birth to their pregnancy' (al-Talaq 4).' Both narrations are mentioned in al-Durr al-Manthur. And if this is established, then it is abrogation, not specification, so their argument is invalid. Then the claim that the verse on pregnant women is a specifier is perhaps contrary to the consensus of the Companions, for the Companions differed on the waiting period of a pregnant woman whose husband dies: Amir al-Mu'minin 'Ali and Ibn 'Abbas said the later of the two terms, and this is a type of precaution due to conflict and ignorance of the abrogator, and it is nothing of specification; and Ibn Mas'ud and Abu Hurayrah said abrogation. As for specification, no one reported it. So ponder on it. And similarly, 'al-Muhsanat' (the chaste women from those given the Book) was revealed after the verse 'And do not marry the polytheist women' (al-Baqarah 221), as a group of commentators mentioned, so it is an abrogator of it, not a specifier. And al-Bayhaqi narrated in his Sunan from Ibn 'Abbas concerning His statement: 'And do not marry the polytheist women until they believe' (al-Baqarah 221) that he said: 'It was abrogated, and the women of the People of the Book were permitted from the polytheist women.' And Abu Dawud narrated in his Nasikh from Ibn 'Abbas concerning His statement: 'And do not marry the polytheist women until they believe, and a believing slave girl is better than a polytheist woman' (al-Baqarah 221) that he said: 'It abrogated from that the marriage of the People of the Book; He permitted them for the Muslims and prohibited Muslim women to their men.' And what occurred in the narration of al-Bayhaqi from him (may Allah be pleased with him) is the wording 'Allah excepted from that,' but what is meant by it is abrogation, for there is no reality of exception, and the meaning is that Allah removed from that prohibition which was established, and it is
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the usul al-fiqh issue: Can a general verse (ʿāmm) in the Quran be specified (takhṣīṣ) by another verse (khāṣṣ) from the Quran? The text presents different scholarly positions. Many scholars, particularly Shafiʿis, allow it unconditionally. Others, including some Ḥanafīs like the Iraqi school, hold that specification only occurs when the specific verse is connected (mawṣūl) to the general one; if it is later and separated, the general abrogates (naskh) the specific, or vice versa. The author argues that the examples given by the permitters (e.g., the pregnant women's waiting period verse specifying the general waiting period verse, and the verse allowing marriage to chaste women of the Book specifying the prohibition of marrying polytheists) are actually cases of naskh, not takhṣīṣ, based on the chronological order of revelation. The text cites statements from Ibn Masʿūd and other Companions indicating that the verse on pregnant women (Sūrat al-Ṭalāq 4) was revealed after the general waiting period verse (Sūrat al-Baqarah 234), making it abrogating (nāsikh) rather than specifying. Similarly, the verse on chaste women of the Book is later than the prohibition of marrying polytheists. The author also notes the disagreement among the Companions regarding the waiting period of a pregnant widow, with some taking the later term as a precaution, not as specification. The passage concludes with a discussion of how to handle conflicting evidence (taʿāruḍ) and the principle of preferring the prohibited out of caution.

Key Terms
التخصيص (al-takhṣīṣ): The specification of a general term (ʿāmm) by a specific term (khāṣṣ) or by a qarīnah, restricting its application.
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a previous ruling by a later ruling from the same source, such that the earlier ruling is no longer valid.
العام (al-ʿāmm): A term that encompasses all individuals of a category without restriction.
الخاص (al-khāṣṣ): A term that applies to a specific subset or individual, limiting the general.
موصول (mawṣūl): Connected; in this context, a specific verse that is immediately adjacent to or contextually linked to the general verse, without temporal separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position as presented in the passage, what is the condition for a later specific verse to specify an earlier general verse?
A) The specific verse must be from the same surah.
B) The specific verse must be connected (mawṣūl) to the general verse.
C) The general verse must have been revealed first.
D) The specific verse must be a clear exception.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a later specific verse that is not connected to the general abrogates (naskh), not specifies (takhṣīṣ).

The Three-Statements Argument: Limits of Takhsīṣ
Presenting a hypothetical scenario to argue that tarkhis is necessary to avoid absurdity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Mufassilun's argument for takhsīṣ using the three-statements example and identify when abrogation (naskh) becomes necessary to avoid absurdity.

Core Idea
When specification leads to absurdity, abrogation (naskh) resolves the conflict.

The Mufassilun (those who distinguish cases) propose that specification (takhsīṣ) can always reconcile seemingly conflicting general and specific texts. To test this, they present a hypothetical: three sequential statements that initially appear to create an absurd outcome if specification is applied absolutely. This lesson walks through the scenario, reveals the absurdity, and examines a counter-argument that clarifies why the Hanafi school insists on naskh in certain situations.

Guided Path
1
Understand the three-statements scenario
Review the three statements: (1) 'Do not honor the ignorant' (specific), (2) 'Honor people' (general), (3) 'Do not honor the scholars' (specific). Note their sequence.
The general statement (2) is sandwiched between two specific statements (1 and 3).
2
Apply specification absolutely
Assume that every general text can be specified by a subsequent or prior specific text. Here, statement (2) 'people' is first specified by (1) to exclude 'the ignorant', leaving 'scholars'. Then (3) prohibits honoring scholars, leaving nothing to honor.
This makes the middle command meaningless — it is void (laghw).
3
Recognize the absurdity
If specification always applies, the result is that the general command has no subject left. This is absurd because a valid command must have a possible subject.
The absurdity shows that specification cannot resolve every conflict.
4
Analyze the counter-argument
A Mufassil might object: they do not specify by the second statement in this exact case because after specification by (1), 'people' becomes equivalent to 'scholars', so (3) directly opposes (2) — it is a contradiction, not a specification. This shifts the conflict from a general-specific relationship to a direct clash.
The Hanafi response: this demonstrates that sometimes naskh (abrogation) is needed, not takhsīṣ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال (المفصلون أوّلاً أقول : إذا قيل في شهر لا تكرم الجهال ثم قيل (في) شهر (آخر) : أكرم الناس و) قيل (في) شهر (ثالث : لا تكرم العلماء لا يعد كلام الوسط لغواً، ولو قيل بالتخصيص مطلقاً) مقدماً كان العام أو مؤخراً لزم ذلك اللغو، لأنه إذا خصص من الناس الجهال لم يبق إلا العلماء وإذا خصت لم يبق شيء فلزم اللغو قطعاً، ويمكن المناقشة من قبلهم إنهم لا يخصصون في هذه الصورة بالثاني كيف وإذا خصص العام بالأول صار الناس بمعنى العلماء، فصار الأمر بالإكرام والنهي عنه وردا على شيء واحد والتخصيص إنما يكون في العام والخاص فلم يبق الوسط مع الآخر من قبيل معارضة الخاص للعام فتدبر
The detailers said, firstly: I say: If it is said in one month, 'Do not honor the ignorant,' then in another month, 'Honor people,' and in a third month, 'Do not honor the scholars,' the middle statement would not be considered void. But if one applies specification absolutely – whether the general comes first or later – that absurdity would necessarily follow, because if 'people' is specified by 'the ignorant,' none remain except the scholars, and if specified to none, nothing remains, so absurdity is necessary. It can be countered on their part that they do not specify in this case by the second; how? Since if the general is specified by the first, 'people' becomes synonymous with 'scholars,' so the command to honor and the prohibition apply to the same thing, and specification only occurs between general and specific. So the middle statement is no longer a case of specific opposing general. Reflect.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage presents the first argument of the Mufassilun (those who distinguish between cases). They give an example of three sequential statements: 'Do not honor the ignorant' (specific), 'Honor people' (general), 'Do not honor the scholars' (specific). If we consistently apply tarkhis (specification) to reconcile these, we get absurdity: 'people' is specified to mean 'scholars' by the first statement, then the third statement prohibits honoring scholars, leaving nothing. So the middle statement would be void. The author notes a possible counter-argument: The opponent may claim they do not specify in this particular case because the first specification makes 'people' equivalent to 'scholars', so the third statement directly opposes the middle, not as a specific general but as a conflicting specific. This shows that sometimes naskh is necessary.

Key Terms
اللغو (al-laghw): Void, meaningless speech. In usul, a statement that has no practical legal effect due to impossibility or contradiction.
التخصيص (al-takhsīṣ): Specification: limiting a general term to exclude some individuals. It is a branch of bayan (clarification).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the three-statements example ('Do not honor the ignorant', 'Honor people', 'Do not honor the scholars'), what is the absurdity that arises if one applies specification absolutely?
A) The middle statement becomes completely void.
B) The first and last statements contradict each other.
C) The second statement is repeated unnecessarily.
D) The third statement becomes ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
Absolute application of specification (takhsīṣ) can produce absurdity when three conflicting texts are involved, necessitating the use of abrogation (naskh) to resolve the conflict.

Can the Quran Specify Itself? The Hanafi Defense
Debate on whether Quran can specify another Quranic text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the arguments for and against takhsis of the Quran by the Quran and evaluate the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
The Quran can specify itself without redundancy because its clarification is the same as the Prophet's clarification.

This passage delves into a key usul dispute: can one Quranic verse specify another? Opponents argue that since the Quran is already a clarifier (mubayyin), specifying it would be redundant (tahsil al-hasil). The Hanafi school defends the possibility, citing examples from the Quran itself and arguing that the Quran's specification is a form of the Prophet's clarification. We will trace both sides and understand the practical implications for deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the central question: Is it permissible for one part of the Quran to specify (takhsis) another part?
This is an usul dispute between Hanafis and some early scholars.
2
Understand the opposing argument
Opponents argue that the Quran is described as 'mubayyin' (a clarifier) in verse 16:44. If the Quran specified itself, it would be explaining what is already clear, which is impossible (tahsil al-hasil).
Their proof relies on the verse: {وَلِتُبَيِّنَ لِلنَّاسِ مَا نُزِلَ إِلَيْهِمْ}
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond that the Quran is a clarifier through the Prophet. Takhsis by the Quran is itself a form of that clarification, not a separate act. Moreover, the Quran contains examples of takhsis, such as the specification of the general prohibition of marrying polytheists (2:221) by later verses.
The author points out that the opponents' proof is circular: it assumes the very impermissibility it tries to prove.
4
Examine the counter-refutation
The author further argues that even if we accept the verse as describing the Quran as an explanation of everything, that does not preclude takhsis; it means the Quran is an explanation in a general sense, not that every type of explanation is included.
The resolution: The Prophet is the ultimate clarifyer, using both Quran and Sunnah. Takhsis by the Quran is part of his clarification.
5
Conclude with the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: If takhsis by the Quran is allowed, a Hanafi jurist can directly use one Quranic verse to specify another without needing external evidence (like hadith). This affects istinbat methodology.
This strengthens the Hanafi position that the Quran is self-sufficient for its own interpretation.

And if added to it what was mentioned from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) regarding the abrogation of {Do not marry the polytheistic women} [Al-Baqarah:221], there would be no room for this specification. But you may use the prior ambiguity (the preventers of specification absolutely said: if the Book were specified, clarification would be necessary because specification is clarification and the Book is a clarifier due to His saying: {And to make clear to the people what was revealed to them} [An-Nahl:44] - it indicates that he (peace be upon him) is a clarifier of everything, so he is a clarifier and explaining the clarifier is redundant. I say: the proof would only be valid if this general was not what was revealed to them, specified by scriptural specifications, i.e., specification of some of the Book by other parts, so the proof is pending on the claim which is the impermissibility of scriptural specifications. If you say: specification is figurative, so there must be a motive, and it is not present, so the generality remains intact. I say: the motive is the existence of specification without doubt. And this proof is opposed by His saying in describing the Quran: {as an explanation of everything} [An-Nahl:44], and among its contents is the Book, so it is an explanation of it, thus specification is permissible, for it is an explanation of the general and it is also of everything. In it, the utmost that follows is that the Quran is an explanation of the Quran, and it does not follow that it is every type of explanation so that specification is permissible; rather it may be an explanation in another way, so reflect. So it is better to make it an objection to the premise of the proof, which is that explaining the clarifier is invalid, so we say it is invalid because the Quran is a clarifier from the Messenger (peace be upon him) and he is also a clarifier of the Quran by this verse. The most appropriate is to raise a deficiency that if your proof were valid, it would indicate the invalidity of the Quran explaining the Quran absolutely, which is invalid by this text. The solution is that everything from the Book and Sunnah came upon his tongue, so he is the clarifyer, sometimes by the Book and sometimes by the Sunnah, so it does not follow from the Messenger's clarification that he must not be a clarifyer by the Book, because it is possible that this clarification is the very clarification of the Messenger, so no impossible redundant attainment follows. So reflect.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is a debate about whether the Quran can be specified (takhsis) by another part of the Quran. Some opponents argued that if the Quran were subject to takhsis by itself, it would require the Quran to clarify itself, which is impossible because the Quran is already a clarifier. The author refutes this by pointing out that the Quran itself contains specification (e.g., the verse about not marrying polytheists being specified by Ibn Abbas's interpretation). He argues that the opponents' proof only works if the general text is not already specified by other parts of the Quran, but it is. The argument then shifts to a verse that describes the Quran as an explanation of everything, which would allow specification. The author concludes that the Quran can specify itself without redundancy because the clarification is the same as the Prophet's clarification.

Key Terms
تخصيص (takhsis): Specifying a general text to exclude some of its individuals.
مبين (mubayyin): That which makes something clear; the Quran is described as a clarifier.
تبيان (tibyan): Explanation; the Quran is described as 'tibyan li kulli shay'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Specification would require the Quran to be a clarifier, which it already is, leading to redundancy.
C) The Quran was revealed all at once, so no specification is possible.
D) Specification is only allowed by the Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defends takhsis of the Quran by the Quran, arguing that it is a natural part of the Quran's role as a clarifier and is evidenced by examples within the Quran itself.

Rule of Takhsis between Sunnah and Quran
Statement of permissibility and conditions for takhsis between Sunnah and Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on takhsis between the Sunnah and the Quran, identify the condition of contemporaneity, and distinguish takhsis from naskh.

Core Idea
If contemporaneous, specify; if not, the later abrogates the earlier.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on how general and specific texts from the Sunnah and Quran interact. You will learn the crucial distinction between specification (takhsis) and abrogation (naskh), and why the Shafi'is hold a stricter view regarding the Sunnah's ability to abrogate the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sources involved
Recognize that the rule involves a general (amm) text and a specific (khass) text. The sources can be the Quran and the mutawatir Sunnah.
Only mutawatir Sunnah is considered; ahad hadith are not equivalent to the Quran in certainty.
2
Understand the condition of contemporaneity
The Hanafi rule hinges on whether the two texts are 'muqtarinan' (contemporaneous). If both were revealed at the same time or without knowledge of which came first, specification applies.
If the precedence is known, the later text abrogates (naskh) the earlier, not specification.
3
Apply the rule
If contemporaneous, the general text is specified by the specific text. If not, the later abrogates the earlier.
This applies to mutual specification: Sunnah can specify Quran and vice versa.
4
Compare with Shafi'i position
The Shafi'is do not allow the Sunnah to abrogate the Quran at all, regardless of timing. They allow specification but not abrogation.
The Hanafi view sees the mutawatir Sunnah as equal in certainty to the Quran for abrogation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة (يجوز تخصيص السنة بالسنة وتخصيص السنة (المتواترة بالكتاب وبالعكس أي تخصيص المتواترة بالكتاب والخلاف فيهما كما تقدم والمختار عندنا أنه إذا كانا مقترنين فيخصص وإلا فينسخ المتقدم بالمتأخر، وخلاف الشافعية في انتساخ خاص الكتاب بعام السنة المتواترة، أو عامه بخاصها أشد فإنهم لا يجوزون انتساخ الكتاب بالسنة .
Issue: It is permissible to specify the Sunnah by the Sunnah, and to specify the Sunnah (mutawatir) by the Book and vice versa, i.e., specification of the mutawatir by the Book. The disagreement on these two is as previously mentioned. The chosen position with us is that if they are contemporaneous (muqtarinan), then specification applies; otherwise, the earlier is abrogated by the later. The Shafi'ites' disagreement on abrogation of a specific text of the Book by a general mutawatir Sunnah, or its general by its specific, is more severe: they do not permit abrogation of the Book by the Sunnah.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage sets out the Hanafi ruling on takhsis among revealed sources. The Sunnah can specify another Sunnah, and the mutawatir Sunnah and the Quran can specify each other. If the two texts are contemporaneous (i.e., both revealed at the same time or without a known time difference), then specification is applied. If one is later, the earlier is abrogated (naskh) by the later. The Shafi'ites are even stricter: they do not allow the Sunnah to abrogate the Quran, regardless of the strength of the Sunnah. This shows the Hanafi view on the mutual interaction of scriptural sources in deriving rulings.

Key Terms
مقترنين (muqtarinan): Two texts that are contemporaneous, i.e., revealed at the same time or without knowledge of precedence.
متواترة (mutawatirah): A hadith transmitted by so many narrators at each level that collusion on a lie is impossible.
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification: restricting the general meaning of a text to a subset of its instances based on another text.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation: the removal or replacement of a prior legal ruling by a later one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are both applied as general and specific.
B) The later revelation abrogates the earlier.
C) The Quran always prevails over hadith.
D) The earlier is considered abrogated regardless of order.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule: if two revealed texts are contemporaneous, the specific specifies the general; otherwise, the later abrogates the earlier.

Takhsis of Quran by Khabar Wahid: Certainty Overrides Probability
Hanafi ruling and evidence on specification using isolated reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the Quran cannot be specified by a khabar wahid, explain the proof based on qat'i vs zanni, and apply the rule to distinguish between valid and invalid specification.

Core Idea
Certainty cannot be overridden by probability: the Quran (qat'i) cannot be specified by a solitary report (zanni).

How do we handle apparent conflicts between a definitive text (the Quran) and a probable text (a solitary hadith)? The Hanafi school maintains that a definitive text remains untouched by a probable one, meaning a solitary hadith cannot restrict the general meaning of the Quran. This lesson unpacks that principle and its implications for Islamic legal methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the first sentence: what is the Hanafi position on specifying the Quran by a khabar wahid? Note that the same applies to mutawatir Sunnah.
The ruling is negative: 'la yajuz' (not permissible).
2
Understand the Proof
Why is it not permissible? Identify the two characteristics: the Quran is qat'i in both transmission (mutawatir) and indication (general is qat'i), while khabar wahid is zanni in transmission.
The proof is based on the epistemological hierarchy: qat'i overrides zanni.
3
Examine Opposing Views
The jumhur (majority) allow takhsis by khabar wahid. Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani (Shafi'i) hesitated. Contrast their reasoning with the Hanafi proof.
The difference stems from whether the general (amm) is considered qat'i or zanni in indication.
4
Note the Thamarah al-Khilaf
What practical difference does this make in legal rulings? Give an example: a solitary hadith that would restrict a general Quranic ruling is not accepted by Hanafis unless supported by other evidence.
Example: the verse 'Allah has permitted trade' (2:275) cannot be specified by a solitary hadith declaring a specific sale invalid.
5
Apply the Principle
Consider a scenario: a solitary hadith says 'No marriage without a guardian' while the Quran says 'Marry whom you please' (4:3). Apply the Hanafi rule: the general Quran remains unrestricted by the hadith.
Hanafis would not restrict the Quranic generality based solely on that hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة لا يجوز عند الحنفية تخصيص الكتاب بخبر الواحد) وكذا تخصيص السنة المتواترة بخبر الواحد (ما لم يخص بقطعي دلالة وثبوتاً وأجاز (الباقون من علماء الأصول (مطلقاً) سواء خص بقطعي قبله أم لا وتوقف القاضي أبو بكر من الشافعية (أي لا أدري أيجوز) التخصيص (أم لا ، لنا أنه أي الكتاب (قطعي من كل وجه لأن المتن متواتر، والعام قطعي الدلالة كما مر بأقوم حجة والخبر ظني) متناً، لأنه خبر الواحد فلا يخصه، وبعده) أي بعد
Issue: It is not permissible according to the Hanafis to specify the Book by a khabar wahid, nor to specify the mutawatir Sunnah by a khabar wahid, unless it is specified by something definitive in indication and transmission. The rest of the usul scholars permitted it absolutely, whether specified by a definitive text before it or not. Qadi Abu Bakr of the Shafi'ites hesitated (i.e., I do not know whether specification is permissible or not). Our proof: The Book is definitive from every aspect because its text is mutawatir, and the general is definitive in indication as earlier established with the strongest evidence, whereas the khabar is presumptive in text because it is a khabar wahid, so it does not specify it. And after it...
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position that the Quran and mutawatir Sunnah cannot be specified by a solitary report (khabar wahid) because the former are definitive (qat'i) in both transmission and indication, while the latter is only presumptive (zanni). Other schools, including most Shafi'is, allow it. Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani hesitated. The proof is that the Quran's text is mutawatir, giving certainty of its wording, and its general meaning is also certain (according to Hanafi usul, general is qat'i until specified). A khabar wahid only gives probability, so it cannot override certainty. This principle has practical implications: for example, the generality of the verse 'Allah has permitted trade' (2:275) cannot be specified by a solitary hadith declaring certain sales invalid unless that hadith is itself definitive or there is consensus. However, the text notes that if the khabar is contemporaneous, specification may be a form of clarification, not abrogation. This is the basis for the Hanafis' stricter requirement for accepting ahad hadith in the presence of Quranic generality.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar wahid): A report transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching mutawatir level; gives zann.
قطعي (qat'i): Definitive certainty; the Quran is qat'i in thubut (transmission) and dalala (indication) according to Hanafis for general texts.
ظني (zanni): Presumptive, probable; khabar wahid is zanni in transmission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis forbid specifying the Quran by a solitary hadith?
A) Because the Quran was revealed in Arabic and hadith is not.
B) Because the Quran is definitive (qat'i) while khabar wahid is presumptive (zanni).
C) Because the Quran was completed before any hadith.
D) Because the Prophet forbade using hadith to interpret the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that general Quranic texts are qat'i in indication means they cannot be specified by a zanni khabar wahid, preserving the Quran's epistemic supremacy.

Hanafi Response to Qadi on 'Amm al-Kitab and Khabar
Hanafi rebuttal of Qadi's tawaqquf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that 'amm al-kitab is qat'i in indication to resolve an apparent conflict with a khabar ahad by prioritizing combination (jamm') over suspension (tawaqquf).

Core Idea
General Quranic texts are definitive ('amm qat'i) in Hanafi usul; they can be specified by mashhur hadith without conflict.

This passage presents a classic dispute in usul al-fiqh: when a general Quranic verse and a specific hadith appear to conflict, should the jurist suspend judgment or give precedence? The Hanafi school argues that the general text is not speculative but definitive, and that specification (takhsis) by a well-known hadith (mashhur) is permissible, preferring combination over suspension. Understanding this argument is crucial for correctly deriving rulings from revealed sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two dalils and their epistemological aspects
The Quranic verse is qat'i in transmission (thubut) but its generality is claimed by Qadi to be zanni in indication (dalala). The hadith is zanni in transmission but qat'i in indication. Map these to understand the claimed conflict.
Hanafis reject that 'amm is zanni; they hold it is qat'i until specified.
2
Understand Qadi's argument for tawaqquf
Qadi argues that both dalils are 'definitive from one aspect and speculative from another', leading to a stalemate where no preponderance exists, thus requiring suspension.
Suspension means 'I do not know' in the sense of inability to prefer one over the other.
3
Analyze the first Hanafi rebuttal: denial of zanniyya of 'amm
Hanafis state that 'amm al-kitab is qat'i in indication (dalala) because the general text is clear and binding until a specific exclusion is proven. This removes the claimed speculation from the Quranic side.
This is a foundational Hanafi usul rule: 'al-amm yufidu al-qat'a'.
4
Analyze the second Hanafi rebuttal: combination is preferred
Even if conflict existed, Hanafis argue that combining both dalils by specifying the general with the specific is preferable to ignoring both. The hadith here is mashhur (well-known, acted upon by consensus), which gives it strength to specify the Quran.
The passage distinguishes between specification and abrogation; some cases are actually abrogation, not specification.
5
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
Take the inheritance verses (general: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children...' 4:11) and the hadith 'We prophets do not leave inheritance.' Hanafis specify the Quranic general with this hadith because it is mashhur and the specification is valid.
This shows the practical outcome: prophets' property is not inherited but given as charity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قبل (وإلا كان متواتراً) إما آية أو خبراً. وكلاهما مفقودان (فافهم) فيه أن الملازمة ممنوعة، بل يجوز أن تكون تلك الأخبار متواترة وبعد الاتفاق والإجماع على التخصيص ارتفع توفر الدواعي على النقل من البين فصارت آحاداً، وقد عرفت كون حديث لا نورث» قاطعاً، وقد عرفت أيضاً أن المخصص في الحديثين السابقين الكتاب وهو قاطع (قلنا) لا نسلم أن الأحاديث المذكورة آحاد بل تلك الأحاديث مشاهير لإجماعهم على العمل بها فبلغت قوة فیزاد بها على الكتاب وهي تقيد المطلق قال : ولعل المراد ما يعمه ونسخ البعض، فإن ههنا ليس تقييد المطلق (وهو نسخ عندنا وليس تخصيصاً، فيه نوع من الخفاء، فإنه ظاهر إن لم يكن الحكم سابقاً توريث مال النبي الله ثم رفع وصار صدقة كما يقتضيه سياق الحديث، وكذا لم يكن توريث القاتل، فإنه قد ورد في بعض الأخبار أن هذا الحكم من شريعة موسى بقي إلى الآن فلا ،نسخ، وهكذا توارث أهل الملتين لم يكن قط في شريعتنا وكذا لم يكن حل الجمع النساء المحرمة بعد نزول آية التحريم فالأولى أن يقال : إن الأخبار مشاهير، فيجوز بها التخصيص كنسخ البعض فتأمل (القاضي) قال كلاهما قطعي من وجه) إذ الكتاب قطعي متناً، والخبر قطعي دلالة ظنّي من وجه إذ عام الكتاب مظنون ،دلالة، وخاص الخبر مظنون متناً (فوقع التعارض) ولا ترجيح (فوجب التوقف أقول : لا يلزم من ذلك التوقف، بمعنى لا أدري بل أدري التوقف) وهذا إنما يرد لو أراد القاضي بقوله : لا أدري الجهل الذي يشترك فيه العامة، وهو بعيد بل المراد الجهل الذي لوجود التعارض وغيره من الموجبات التي ليس فيها حظ للعامة وهو لازم البتة فافهم وأجيب بالمنع أي بمنع كون عام الكتاب ظنياً من وجه، فإن العام قطعي عندنا وهو من قبل مشايخنا (والترجيح) أي أجيب بتسليم التعارض ومنع التوقف، لأن الجمع مرجح ، وهذا من قبل النافين فافهم.
Before: (Otherwise it would be mutawatir) either a verse or a report. Both are absent. (Understand) that the entailment is prevented; rather it is possible that those reports were mutawatir and after agreement and consensus on specification, the availability of motives for transmission ceased, so they became ahad. You have known that the hadith 'We do not inherit' is definitive, and you have also known that the specifier in the two previous hadiths is the Book, which is definitive. (We say) we do not concede that the mentioned hadiths are ahad; rather those hadiths are mashhur due to consensus on acting upon them, so they gained strength and are given precedence over the Book, and they restrict the absolute. He said: Perhaps what is meant is general and abrogation of some, for here there is no restriction of the absolute (and it is abrogation according to us, not specification; there is a kind of obscurity in it, for it is apparent if the ruling was not previously inheritance of the Prophet's property then it was raised and became charity as the context of the hadith requires; similarly, there was no inheritance for the killer, for it has been reported in some reports that this ruling from the law of Moses remained until now, so no abrogation; likewise, mutual inheritance of people of two religions never existed in our law; similarly, there was no permissibility of marrying prohibited women after revelation of the verse of prohibition. So it is better to say: The reports are mashhur, so specification is permissible by them like abrogation of some. So reflect. (Al-Qadi) said: Both are definitive from one aspect, since the Book is definitive in text, and the report is definitive in indication, speculative from one aspect, since the general of the Book is speculative in indication, and the specific of the report is speculative in text. (So conflict occurs) and no preponderance (so suspension is necessary). I say: That does not necessitate suspension, in the sense of 'I do not know'; rather I know suspension. This only applies if al-Qadi by his saying 'I do not know' meant ignorance shared by the common people, which is far-fetched; rather what is meant is the ignorance due to existence of conflict and other causes which the common people have no share in, and it is absolutely necessary. Understand. And it was answered by denial, i.e., denial that the general of the Book is speculative from one aspect, for the general is definitive according to us, and it is from our shaykhs. (And preponderance) i.e., it was answered by conceding conflict and denying suspension, because combination is preponderant, and this is from the negators. Understand.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi response to an argument attributed to al-Qadi (likely Qadi Abd al-Jabbar or similar) regarding the conflict between a general Quranic text and a khabar al-wahid. The opponent claims that the general text is definitive in transmission but speculative in indication, while the specific report is speculative in transmission but definitive in indication, leading to a stalemate requiring suspension (tawaqquf). The Hanafi rebuttal is two-fold: first, they deny that the general is speculative in indication, asserting that according to Hanafi usul, general texts ('amm) are definitive (qat'i) in the absence of specification. Second, they argue that even conceding conflict, suspension is not necessary because combination (jamm') by specifying the general is preferable to ignoring both. The text illustrates the Hanafi commitment to the definitive nature of 'amm and the permissibility of specifying the Quran by mashhur hadith, which have the strength of consensus. The passage also touches on the distinction between specification and abrogation, noting that some apparent specifications are actually abrogations.

Key Terms
عام (amm): A word that encompasses all individuals of its category without limitation.
قطع (qat'): Certainty in transmission or indication.
ظن (zann): Speculative; probable but not certain.
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification of a general term to exclude some of its individuals.
مشهور (mashhur): A hadith transmitted by at least three chains in each generation, below mutawatir but above ahad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Specification by Mafhum al-Mukhalafah: A Usul Dispute
Debate on whether mafhum al-mukhalafah can specify general texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the Hanafi position on using mafhum al-mukhalafah to specify a general text and evaluate the objections raised.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-mukhalafah can specify a general text if both are equally speculative (zanni).

This lesson examines a key usul al-fiqh dispute: can a general text be specified by a concept derived from its opposite condition? The Hanafi school permits this under certain conditions, while opponents argue the explicit is always stronger. We will work through the arguments using the famous water purity example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two textual sources
Locate the general hadith ('water is pure') and the conditional hadith ('when water reaches two qullas it does not carry impurity').
The general is a mantuq of generality; the conditional yields a mafhum.
2
Extract the mafhum al-mukhalafah
From the conditional hadith, derive the opposing implication: water less than two qullas does carry impurity.
This is the mafhum that contradicts the general.
3
Observe the apparent conflict
The general says all water is pure; the concept says some water is impure. They seem to contradict.
Conflict triggers the need for resolution.
4
Understand the Hanafi argument
Hanafis argue both texts are equally speculative (zanni), so they conflict. Combination by specification is preferred over discarding one.
Key principle: al-jam' awla min al-ihdar.
5
Recognize the counter-arguments
Opponents say the explicit is stronger; further objections question the equality of speculation and the role of specificity.
The Hashiyah criticizes the Hanafi response as preferring the weaker.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القائلون بالمفهوم المخالف خصوا به العموم وأما مفهوم الموافقة فعندهم يخصص مطلقاً ويفهم من إشارات كلام البعض أنه لا يخصص لأن العبارة أقوى إلا إذا خص بعبارة قاطعة أولاً والتحقيق أنه تخصيص مطلقاً إن كان جلياً، وإلا فكما سبق (كتخصيص خلق الماء طهوراً لا ينجسه إلا ما غير لونه أو طعمه أو ريحه) رواه الترمذي بغير الاستثناء، وقال صحيح، بمفهوم إذا بلغ الماء قلتين لم يحمل خبثاً) رواه أبو داود، لكن بتعريف الخبث ومفهومه إذا لم يبلغ الماء قلتين يحمل الخبث مخصص من عموم الماء، ما كان أقل من قلتين، وإنما خصوا العموم به لأنه ظني مثله فتعارضا، والجمع (أولى من الإهدار، فيجمع بتخصيص العام فإن قيل : لا نسلم المعارضة بين المفهوم والمنطوق (فإن المنطوق أقوى والمفهوم أضعف فيهدر المفهوم إن كان في مقابلة المنطوق، فإن اعتبار الرابح أصل متأصل في الباب، وما أجيب به من العام وإن كان أقوى من حيث كونه منطوقاً لكنه أضعف من جهة العموم والمفهوم وإن كان أضعف من جهة كونه مفهوماً لكنه أقوى من جهة الخصوص ففيه ما أورد عليه المصنف في «الحاشية»، أما أولاً : فلأنه لا دخل في المفهوم للعموم والخصوص، لأن المفهوم إنما يثبتونه لأنه لولاه لانتفت فائدة التخصيص، وفي هذا العام والخاص سواء انتهى، وفيه أن دلالة اللفظ على العموم أضعف من دلالته على الخصوص، فدلالة اللفظ على المفهوم الخاص تكون أقوى من جهة أنه خاص، والاستدلال بانتفاء الفائدة لا ينافي هذا، وأما ثانياً : فلأن غاية ما لزم منه وجود القوة من وجه في المفهوم من جهة الخصوص، لكن هذه القوة لا تبلغ قوة المنطوق، فلا مساواة في درجة الظنية أصلاً قلنا : مساواتهما ظناً) أي مساواة العام والمخصص في قدر الظنية بعد مساواتهما في أصل الظن (ليس شرطاً للتخصيص للإتفاق عليه) أي على التخصيص (بخبر الواحد للكتاب كذا في شرح المختصر . أقول : لا يخفى أنه) أي عدم اشتراط المساواة في قدر الظن (ترجيح المرجوح وهو خلاف البديهة) فإن قلت : فما تصنع للاتفاق على التخصيص بخبر الواحد عام الكتاب؟ قال : أما حديث التخصيص بحديث
Those who affirm mafhum al-mukhalafah have specified the general by it. As for mafhum al-muwafaqah, according to them it specifies absolutely. It is understood from the indications of some statements that it does not specify because the explicit statement is stronger, unless it is specified by a definitive statement first. The verification is that it specifies absolutely if it is clear, otherwise as before. (Like specifying the hadith 'Water is pure, nothing makes it impure except what changes its color, taste, or smell' narrated by al-Tirmidhi without the exception, and he said it is sahih, by the concept of 'when water reaches two qullas it does not carry impurity' narrated by Abu Dawud, but with definition of khabath, and its concept that if water does not reach two qullas it carries impurity, specifying the general of water, what is less than two qullas. They specified the general by it because it is speculative like it, so they conflict, and combining is preferable to discarding, so one combines by specifying the general. If it is said: We do not concede the conflict between the concept and the explicit statement, for the explicit is stronger and the concept is weaker, so the concept is discarded if it is in opposition to the explicit, for considering the stronger is a well-established principle in the chapter. And what was answered that the general, although stronger as an explicit statement, is weaker in terms of generality, and the concept, although weaker as a concept, is stronger in terms of specificity. There is what the author criticized in the Hashiyah. First: because the concept has no relation to generality and specificity, because they affirm the concept only because otherwise the benefit of specification would be lost, and in this the general and specific are equal. End. And there is that the indication of a word to generality is weaker than its indication to specificity, so the indication of the word to the specific concept is stronger because it is specific, and the inference from loss of benefit does not contradict this. Second: because the utmost that follows is the existence of strength in one aspect in the concept due to specificity, but this strength does not reach the strength of the explicit, so there is no equality in the degree of speculation at all. We said: Their speculation is equal, i.e., equality of the general and the specifier in the degree of speculation after their equality in the basis of speculation is not a condition for specification because of agreement on it, i.e., on specification, by khabar al-wahid of the Book. Likewise in Sharh al-Mukhtasar. I say: It is not hidden that it, i.e., not stipulating equality in degree of speculation, is a preference for the weaker over the stronger, which is contrary to intuition. For if you say: What do you do with the agreement on specification by khabar al-wahid of the general of the Book? He said: As for the hadith of specification by a hadith...
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage presents the debate on whether mafhum al-mukhalafah (a concept derived from a specific condition or characteristic) can specify a general text. Proponents of mafhum al-mukhalafah use it to specify general texts. The text discusses an example: the hadith 'Water is pure' is general, but another hadith 'When water reaches two qullas it does not carry impurity' yields a concept that less than two qullas does carry impurity, thus specifying the general. The objection raised is that mafhum is weaker than the explicit general statement, so it should be discarded. The Hanafi response is that both are speculative in equal degree, so specification is allowed. However, a counter-argument is that equality in degree of speculation is not required, as agreed upon in the case of khabar al-wahid specifying the Quran. The author (likely the commentator) rejects this by saying that not requiring equality amounts to preferring the weaker over the stronger, which is absurd. The passage ends with the opponent asking how to reconcile this with the consensus on specification by khabar al-wahid, but the text is cut off.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالف (mafhum al-mukhalafah): The opposing implication from a text; e.g., when a condition is mentioned, what is not conditioned is ruled differently.
مفهوم الموافقة (mafhum al-muwafaqah): The agreeing implication; a fortiori reasoning from a text.
منطوق (mantuq): The explicit wording of a text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the basis for using mafhum al-mukhalafah to specify a general text?
A) The mafhum is always stronger than the explicit general.
B) The mafhum is equally speculative as the general.
C) The mafhum is derived from the Quran.
D) The mafhum represents consensus.

Key Takeaway
Mafhum al-mukhalafah can specify a general text only when both are equally speculative and the concept is clear (jali), as demonstrated by the water purity example.

Specification of General Texts by Mafhum: Hanafi View
Discussing whether and how mafhum can specify general texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on using mafhum to specify general texts and evaluate the conditions under which mafhum al-muwafaqa and mafhum al-mukhalif can specify amm.

Core Idea
Mafhum can specify general texts if both are zanni, reconciling rather than nullifying.

The ability of implied meanings (mafhum) to specify general (amm) texts is a key issue in Hanafi usul. This lesson unpacks the debate, focusing on the conditions for specification, the role of conjecture (zann), and a practical example from hadith. By the end, you will have a clear framework for evaluating when a mafhum can override a general ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and positions
State the central question: can mafhum al-mukhalif and mafhum al-muwafaqa specify general texts? Note the Hanafi view (yes) and the opposing view (no, or with restrictions).
The text opens with 'مسألة القائلون بالمفهوم المخالف خصوا به العموم'.
2
Examine the Hanafi dalil
Analyze the hadith example: the general rule 'Water is pure' is specified by the mafhum of 'If water reaches two qullas, it carries no impurity'. Understand how the mafhum creates a particular ruling for water less than two qullas.
Both hadith are zanni al-thubut and al-dalala.
3
Understand the opposing argument
The opponent argues that explicit text (mantuq) is always stronger than implied, so mafhum should be disregarded when in conflict. Identify the principle of preferring the stronger.
لقولهم: 'المنطوق أقوى والمفهوم أضعف'.
4
Trace the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response: the general is weaker due to generality, the mafhum is stronger due to particularity. Both are zanni, so they are equal in conjecture, reconcilable by specification. Then address the criticism that equality in conjecture is not possible.
Key phrase: 'الجمع أولى من الإهدار'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical result: a general fiqh ruling (e.g., water is pure) can be specified by a mafhum (e.g., water less than two qullas is impure if changed). The Hanafi position is supported by the principle of preferring reconciliation.
The text concludes by leaning towards the Hanafi view, though with nuanced conditions.

Issue: Those who subscribe to the contradictory implication (mafhum al-mukhalif) have specified general texts with it. As for the harmonious implication (mafhum al-muwafaqa), according to them it specifies absolutely. It is understood from the indications of some people's speech that it does not specify because the explicit expression is stronger, unless specified by a definitive expression first. The verification is that it specifies absolutely if it is clear, otherwise as before (like specifying the hadith 'Water is pure, nothing makes it impure except what changes its color, taste, or smell' reported by al-Tirmidhi without the exception, and he declared it authentic, with the implication of the hadith 'If water reaches two qullas, it carries no impurity' reported by Abu Dawud, but with the definition of impurity; its implication is that if water has not reached two qullas, it carries impurity, specifying the general rule of water that is less than two qullas). They only specify the general with it because it is conjectural like it, so they conflict, and reconciliation is preferred to nullification, so reconcile by specifying the general. If it is said: We do not concede conflict between the implied and the explicit (for the explicit is stronger and the implied is weaker, so the implied is disregarded if in opposition to the explicit, because considering the stronger is an established principle in the chapter). And what was answered that the general, although stronger in terms of being explicit, is weaker in terms of generality, and the implied, although weaker in terms of being implied, is stronger in terms of particularity—there is an objection raised by the author in the Hashiyah. First: because the implied has nothing to do with generality and particularity, since they only affirm the implied because otherwise the benefit of specification would be lost, and in this the general and the particular are equal. And in it is that the indication of the word to generality is weaker than its indication to particularity, so the indication of the word to the particular implied is stronger in that it is particular, and reasoning by the loss of benefit does not negate this. Second: because the utmost that follows from it is the existence of strength from one aspect in the implied in terms of particularity, but this strength does not reach the strength of the explicit, so there is no equality in degree of conjecture at all. We said: their being equal in conjecture (i.e., equality of the general and the specific in amount of conjecture after their equality in original conjecture) is not a condition for specification due to agreement on it (i.e., on specification by a solitary report for the Book, as in Sharh al-Mukhtasar). I say: it is not hidden that it (i.e., not requiring equality in amount of conjecture) is preferring the preponderated, which is contrary to intuition. If you say: What do you do with the agreement on specification by a solitary report of a general text of the Book? He said: As for the hadith of specification by a solitary report of a general text of the Book, it does not apply to us because of what preceded of specification by the definitive; then the conjectural becomes balanced. But without precedent it is not permissible according to us, so there is no agreement. If you say: Suppose the general becomes weak by specification, but it does not reach the weakness of a solitary report. I say: No, and we have already shown that the indication of the specified general is equivalent to the indication of analogy or weaker, so how is it not weaker than a solitary report? And he said in al-Tahrir: The verification in the answer is that with the conjecture of indication in both (i.e., the general and the implied), the conjecture of particularity is strengthened due to its prevalence in the general. So in the general there is weakness from two aspects. And in it is apparent consideration, because the doubt in the indication of the general according to them is only from the aspect of the prevalence of particularity in it, and apart from this doubt there is no doubt in the general, so by this prevalence its indication becomes conjectural, probable of particularity. So by what thing is the conjecture of particularity strengthened? Also, what the author said refutes him: I say: The prevalence, if it leads to conjecture of particularity, only leads to a weak conjecture (i.e., a preponderated probability contrary to the linguistic use, not prevalence, i.e., prevalence of conjecture of particularity). This probability does not remove the explicit from being explicit, so it does not become like the implied in weakness. Do you not see the disagreement in the general regarding definitiveness and conjecture? (Agreement on the original indication of generality) and the disagreement in the implied regarding conjecture and its absence? So the implied is weaker than the general; many experts did not understand it, so one only conjectures particularity weakly, and conjecture avails nothing against the truth. Then I say: It is not far-fetched to say in the answer: The general according to them was conjectural due to the possibility of absolute specification arising from the prevalence of the occurrence of specification. When the specific specifier (which is the implied) was conjectured, its weakness intensified, so the possibility becomes conjectural, then the specifier is acted upon due to existence of equality. Ponder. And this too is not free from criticism, because we do not concede the existence of conjecture of the specifier; rather the generality of the general nullifies this conjecture because it is explicit. And this is because the weak disintegrates in the face of the strong. Understand. Alternatively, you may answer that the general, although explicit, those who hold the implied require halting to search for a specifier, and as long as the absence of a specifier is not preponderantly conjectured or certain, it remains like an ambiguous text, not benefiting anything. So when the specifier is conjectured, this is established due to the general being unsuitable for opposition, and the particularity becomes strong. Contemplate it, for it is only complete if the implied is particular. With even no pause in it.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion (mas'ala) on the usul al-fiqh issue of whether mafhum (implied meaning)—both mafhum al-mukhalif (contradictory implication) and mafhum al-muwafaqa (harmonious implication)—can be used to specify general (amm) texts. The author begins by stating that those who accept mafhum al-mukhalif use it to specify general texts, while mafhum al-muwafaqa is said to specify absolutely according to some, though others disagree. The preferred view (tahqiq) is that mafhum al-muwafaqa specifies absolutely if it is clear (jali). The discussion then presents an example from hadith: the general rule that water is pure and not impure except by change of properties is specified by the mafhum of another hadith that water reaching two qullas does not carry impurity, implying that water less than two qullas does carry impurity. The key argument is that since both the general and the mafhum are conjectural (zanni), they can be reconciled by specification rather than nullification. The opponent argues that explicit text (mantuq) is always stronger than implied, so the implied should be disregarded. The author responds by examining strengths: the general is weaker due to generality, while the mafhum is stronger due to particularity. The discussion continues with objections from the Hashiyah and responses, ultimately concluding that the conjecture of particularity can be strengthened, but the implied remains weaker. The passage ends with a suggestion that if the implied is particular, it can specify, but if general, there is no pause.

Key Terms
المفهوم المخالف (al-mafhum al-mukhalif): The implied meaning that contradicts the explicit wording when a condition or attribute is mentioned, e.g., 'if it reaches two qullas it does not carry impurity' implies that less than two qullas does carry impurity.
المفهوم الموافقة (al-mafhum al-muwafaqa): The harmonious implied meaning where the explicit ruling applies even more strongly to an unmentioned case (e.g., prohibition of saying 'uff' implies prohibition of hitting parents).
العموم (al-umum): A word that encompasses all individuals of its category, such as 'water' in the hadith covering all water types.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition for mafhum al-muwafaqa to specify a general text absolutely?
A) It must be reported by a mutawatir chain
B) It must be clear (jali) in its implication
C) It must contradict the explicit wording
D) It must be weaker than the general

Key Takeaway
Mafhum can specify general texts in Hanafi usul when both are zanni, provided the mafhum is particular and clear.

Strength of Specified Amm vs Mafhum: A Hanafi Usul Dispute
Debate on relative strength of specified general text vs concept

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the relative strength of a general text (amm) after specification (takhsis) compared to a concept (mafhum) and evaluate the counterarguments.

Core Idea
A specified general text remains stronger than a concept because its spoken wording (mantuq) preserves its authority.

In Hanafi usul, a general text (amm) is considered definitive until specified. But what happens after it is specified? Does it become as weak as a concept (mafhum) derived from implication? This passage from Sharh Muslim al-Thubut delves into this intricate debate, defending the Hanafi view that even after specification, the general text remains stronger than the concept. Understanding this hierarchy is crucial for resolving conflicts between textual evidences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
What is the dispute about? The relative strength of a specified amm compared to a mafhum. The passage argues that the specified amm is not as weak as some claim.
2
Understand the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position is that amm after takhsis is weaker than before but still stronger than mafhum. It is not weaker than khabar al-wahid.
The text states that the indication of a specified amm equals that of analogy or is weaker, but that does not make it as weak as mafhum.
3
Analyze the opposing argument
Some scholars argue that the predominance of specificity in the general makes it speculative, and thus it is no stronger than a mafhum. The author refutes this by pointing out that the doubt is only about the possibility of further specification, not about the basic indication.
The 'predominance of specificity' is not enough to reduce the amm to the level of mafhum.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The author uses a logical argument: the amm is a spoken expression (mantuq) whose basic indication is agreed upon, while the mafhum is not understood by many skilled jurists. Therefore, the amm retains its strength.
The concept is weaker because it is not universally accepted as a valid source of law.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: when a specified amm conflicts with a mafhum, the amm is given preference. Also, a khabar al-wahid can specify an amm but cannot specify a mafhum on its own.
This affects how jurists rank evidences in ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الواحد) عام الكتاب (فلا يرد علينا لما تقدم من التخصيص بالقاطع قصيره ظنياً فاعتدلا، وأما بدون تقدمه فلا يجوز عندنا فلا ،اتفاق فإن قلت : هب العام يصير ضعيفاً بالتخصيص لكن لا يبلغ ضعف خبر الواحد قلت كلا وقد بينا سابقاً أن دلالة العام المخصوص تعادل دلالة القياس أو أضعف منه، فكيف لا يكون أضعف من خبر الواحد (و) قال في «التحرير» التحقيق) في الجواب أن مع ظنية الدلالة فيهما أي العام والمفهوم (يقوى ظن الخصوص لغلبته في العام) ففي العام ضعف من وجهين وفيه نظر ظاهر، لأن الشبهة في دلالة العام عندهم ليست إلا من جهة غلبة الخصوص فيه وغير هذه الشبهة لا شبهة في العام فبهذه الغلبة تصير دلالته عندهم ظنية محتملة للخصوص، فبأي شيء يقوى ظن الخصوص، وأيضاً يردعليه ما قال المصنف (أقول : الغلبة لو أفضى إلى ظن الخصوص فإنما يفضي ظناً ضعيفاً) أي احتمالاً مرجوحاً على خلاف الوضع لا الغلبة أي غلبة ظن الخصوص، وهذا الاحتمال لا يخرج المنطوق عن المنطوقية، فلا يصير مثل المفهوم في الضعف ألا ترى الاختلاف في العام في القطع والظن) الاتفاق في أصل الدلالة على العموم (و) الاختلاف في المفهوم في الظن وعدمه) فالمفهوم ضعيف عن العام لم يفهمه كثير من المهرة فلا يظن الخصوص إلا ظناً ضعيفاً) والظن لا يغني من الحق شيئاً ثم أقول : لا يبعد أن يقال في الجواب العام عندهم كان مظنوناً لاحتمال المخصص المطلق الناشيء عن غلبة وقوع التخصيص فلما ظن المخصص) الخاص وهو المفهوم اشتد ضعفه الصيرورة الاحتمال مظنوناً فحينئذ يعمل المخصص لوجود المساواة فتأمل وهذا أيضاً غير حال عن المناقشة لأنا لا نسلم وجود ظن المخصص، بل يبطل عموم العام لكونه منطوقاً هذا الظن وهذا لأن الضعيف يضمحل عند القوي فافهم ولك أن تجيب بأن العام وإن كان منطوقاً لكن قائلو المفهوم يوجبون التوقف إلى البحث عن المخصص، فما لم يغلب على الظن أو لم يتيقن انتفاء المخصص يبقى مثل المجمل غير مفيد شيئاً، فإذا ظن المخصص ثبت هذا لعدم صلوح العام معارضة وقوي الخصوص فتدبر فيه، فإنه إنما يتم إذا كان المفهوم خاصاً مع حتى ، لا يتوقف فيه .
The general text of the Book is not rejected by us because of what previously passed of specification with a definitive [proof], so its indication becomes speculative and they become equal. But without such [definitive specification] it is not permissible according to us, so there is no agreement. If you say: The general [text] becomes weak by specification but it does not reach the weakness of a solitary report, I say: No, we have already explained that the indication of a specified general text equals the indication of analogy or is weaker than it, so how can it not be weaker than a solitary report? And he said in al-Tahrir: The verification in the answer is that with the speculative indication in both — the general and the concept — the presumption of specificity is strengthened due to its predominance in the general. So the general has weakness from two aspects, and there is apparent consideration in it, because the doubt in the indication of the general according to them is only from the aspect of the predominance of specificity in it, and besides this doubt there is no doubt in the general. So due to this predominance its indication according to them becomes speculative, admitting the possibility of specificity. By what thing is the presumption of specificity strengthened? Also, what the author said refutes him: I say: If the predominance leads to a presumption of specificity, it only leads to a weak presumption, i.e., an improbable probability contrary to the [linguistic] convention, not the predominance, i.e., the preponderance of the presumption of specificity. This probability does not remove the spoken expression from being a spoken expression, so it does not become like the concept in weakness. Do you not see the disagreement concerning the general regarding certainty and speculation? There is agreement in the basic indication of generality, and disagreement concerning the concept regarding speculation and its absence. So the concept is weaker than the general; many of the skilled did not understand it, so it does not presume specificity except a weak presumption. And presumption does not avail against the truth at all. Then I say: It is not far to say in answer: The general according to them was speculative due to the probability of an absolute specifier arising from the predominance of occurrence of specification. When the specific specifier — which is the concept — is presumed, its weakness intensifies due to the probability becoming speculative; then the specifier operates because of equality, so contemplate. This too is not free from discussion, for we do not concede the existence of a presumption of the specifier; rather, the generality of the general is invalidated because it is spoken expression — this presumption — and this is because the weak disappears before the strong, so understand. And you may answer that although the general is a spoken expression, the proponents of the concept necessitate suspension pending search for a specifier. So as long as it is not preponderant in presumption or the absence of a specifier is not certain, it remains like a general [ambiguous] term, not benefitting anything. So when the specifier is presumed, this is established due to the general not being fit for opposition and the specificity is strengthened. So ponder over it, for it is only complete if the concept is specific, such that it does not suspend [operation].
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute about the relative strength of a general text (amm) after specification (takhsis) compared to a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) and to the concept (mafhum). The author begins by stating that a general text from the Book is not rejected by us (Hanafis) when it has been specified by a definitive proof, because then its indication becomes speculative and equal to that of a solitary report. Without such specification, the general text retains its strength and cannot be disregarded. The discussion then addresses an objection: even if the general text is weakened by specification, it is still not as weak as a solitary report. The author rejects this, citing previous arguments that the indication of a specified general text equals that of analogy or is weaker. Then, reference is made to al-Tahrir, where it is claimed that both the general and the concept are speculative, and the presumption of specificity is strengthened in the general due to its predominance, so the general has two weaknesses. The author critiques this, pointing out that the only doubt concerning the general is from the predominance of specification, and that this does not make the general equal to the concept. The concept is weaker because many scholars do not accept it. Several arguments and counterarguments are presented, with the author ultimately defending the position that the general text, even after specification, is stronger than the concept. The discussion involves rational reasoning (talil) and is typical of Hanafi usul methodology.

Key Terms
عام (amm): A word that applies to all individuals of its category without restriction.
مفهوم (mafhum): The implied meaning derived from a text, as opposed to the explicit wording.
تخصيص (takhsis): The specification of a general term by excluding some of its individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a specified general text (amm) stronger than a concept (mafhum)?
A) Because the general text remains spoken (mantuq) and its basic indication of generality is agreed upon.
B) Because the general text can never be specified by a solitary report.
C) Because the concept is always definitive.
D) Because the general text becomes stronger after specification.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a general text after specification remains stronger than a concept because its spoken nature and agreed-upon indication of generality provide more authority than mere implication.
