Prophet's Action as Specifier of General Texts
Dispute over the Prophet's action as a specifier of general texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three scholarly positions on whether the Prophet's action specifies a general text and apply the Hanafi timing principle to determine the outcome in a given scenario.

Core Idea
The Prophet's action specifies a general text only when the command to follow is contemporaneous; timing decides between specification and abrogation.

A key question in usul al-fiqh is whether the Prophet's ﷺ actions can limit the generality of Quranic or hadith commands. This passage presents three views and a nuanced Hanafi resolution based on the timing of the evidence requiring emulation (dalil al-ta'assi) relative to the general text. Understanding this dispute is essential for correctly deriving rulings from the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Opinions
Extract the three positions mentioned: (1) the action specifies the general, (2) the action does not specify rather following is obligatory and it abrogates if later, (3) suspension until external evidence.
Note that each opinion has implications for whether the ummah must follow the action.
2
Analyze the Evidence of Emulation (Dalil al-Ta'assi)
The author cites Quranic verses (33:21, 3:31) and a hadith commanding following the Prophet. Understand that this evidence is itself a general command, and its interaction with the primary general text is the core issue.
3
Apply the Timing Principle
The author's truth: if dalil al-ta'assi is prior to the general text, it is abrogated; if contemporaneous, it specifies; if later, the general may serve as a qarina for specification if there is evidence of non-abrogation.
Consider why the second opinion fails in the first two scenarios.
4
Determine the Practical Consequence (Thamarah)
The difference affects whether an individual is obligated by a specific prophetic action that contradicts a general command. For example, the Prophet's ﷺ way of praying might specify the general command 'Pray'.
5
Locate the Author's Tarjih
The author favors the nuanced position based on timing, as he says 'al-haqq' at the end. Recognize this as the relied-upon view.
The author promises more detail in the discussion on Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقالة الثالثة في المبادىء اللغوية عموماً) نحو ﴿لَقَدْ كَانَ لَكُمْ فِي رَسُولِ اللَّهِ أَسْوَةٌ حَسَنَةٌ ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٢١] ونحو : ﴿ فَاتَّبِعُونِي يُحببكُمُ اللهُ ﴾ [آل عمران: ٣١] ونحو لو كان موسى حياً لما وسعه إلا اتباعي» (فقيل: يخصص بالأول) وهو العام فلا يلزم على الأمة الاقتداء به في الفعل، وقيل: لا يصير) الأول (مخصصاً، بل يجب الاتباع في الفعل، وعلى هذا يلزم أن يكون الفعل مع هذا الدليل ناسخاً للعام مع تقدمه عليه في بعض العمومات (وقيل : بالوقف) فلا يعمل حتى يقوم الدليل من خارج (للمخصص التخصيص أولى للجمع) وإن لم يخصص بطل العام بالكلية، وعلى تقدير كونه متأخراً ينبغي أن يكون ناسخاً فتأمل وللنافي الفعل أولى، فإنه مع دليل الاتباع أخص) والخاص أقوى من العام فيعمل به وفيه ما فيه لأنه إذا ضم مع دليل الاتباع يكون أخص، لكن وجوب الضم من أين لم لا يجوز أن يضم مع العام فيخص دليل الاتباع، والحق في هذه المسألة أنه إن كان دليل التأسي مقدماً على نزول العام والعمل بخلافه فدليل التأسي منسوخ فيه وإن كان مقارناً فيخص فلا وجه للقول الثاني في الصورتين وإن كان دليل التأسي مؤخراً فيحتمل الخلاف فإن المقدم يصلح قرينة التخصيص عند دلالة قرينة على عدم الانتساخ والله أعلم وسيأتي مفصلاً في السنة إن شاء الله تعالى.
The third topic: On Linguistic Principles Generally. For example: {Indeed in the Messenger of Allah you have a good example} [al-Ahzab:21] and {So follow me, Allah will love you} [Aal-e-Imran:31] and 'If Musa were alive, he would have no choice but to follow me.' It is said: it (the action) specifies the first (the general), so the ummah is not obligated to follow him in the action. And it is said: the first does not become a specifier, rather following the action is obligatory, and accordingly the action with this evidence would be abrogating the general if the action comes after it in some generals. And it is said: suspension, so it is not acted upon until evidence from outside appears. For the proponent of specification, specification is preferable for combination; if not specified, the general becomes entirely void. And if the action is later, it should be an abrogator, so ponder. And for the denier of the action, his view is preferable, for it along with the evidence of following is more specific, and the specific is stronger than the general, so it is acted upon. But there is something in it: because if it is combined with the evidence of following, it becomes more specific, but from where does the necessity of combination come? Why may it not be combined with the general so that the evidence of following becomes specified? The truth in this issue is: if the evidence of emulation is prior to the revelation of the general and action contrary to it, then the evidence of emulation is abrogated. If it is contemporaneous, it specifies, so there is no basis for the second opinion in both cases. If the evidence of emulation is later, then difference is possible, for the earlier can serve as a contextual indication of specification when there is evidence of non-abrogation. Allah knows best, and it will come in detail in the discussion on Sunnah, if Allah wills.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage opens the third topic of linguistic principles. The author considers whether an action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) can specify a general textual command. He cites verses and a hadith that command following the Prophet. Some scholars say the action specifies the general, so the general is not binding in that case. Others say the action does not specify; rather, following the action is obligatory, and if the action comes after the general text, it abrogates it. A third view suspends judgment until external evidence is found. The author analyzes the arguments: if the evidence of emulation (the command to follow) is prior to the general text, then the general abrogates the emulation command; if contemporaneous, the action specifies; if later, there is room for difference—the prior text can serve as a qarina for specification if there is evidence of no abrogation. This is a classic usul dispute on the interaction of the Prophet's practice with Quranic and hadith texts. The author promises further detail in the section on Sunnah.

Key Terms
مخصص (mukhassis): A specifier that limits the generality of a general text
دليل التأسي (dalîl al-ta’assî): The evidence that requires following the Prophet, i.e., the command to imitate

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, when is the Prophet's action considered a specifier of a general text rather than an abrogator?
A) When the action is prior to the general text
B) When the action is contemporaneous with the general text
C) When the action is later than the general text
D) The action always abrogates

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's action specifies a general text only when the evidence of emulation is contemporaneous; chronology determines whether the relationship is specification, abrogation, or nullification.

Taqrir: Specifier or Abrogator? The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Defining taqrir and debating its effect on general texts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on whether the Prophet's tacit approval (taqrir) specifies or abrogates a general text, and apply the distinction based on timing.

Core Idea
Tacit approval specifies if contemporaneous with the general, abrogates if later — a uniquely Hanafi timing distinction.

When the Prophet (peace be upon him) remained silent upon witnessing an action, did He approve it? And how does that silence interact with an earlier general command? The Shafi'i school treats such silence as a specifier in all cases, while the Hanafis split the ruling based on when the silence occurred relative to the general text. This lesson unpacks the arguments and the crucial role of timing.

Guided Path
1
Define taqrir and its conditions
Identify the definition of taqrir: silence upon seeing an action while able to forbid it. Note the condition that the Prophet must have known about the action and been able to prevent it.
The legal effect of taqrir is permission for the witnessed act.
2
State the Hanafi position on timing
If the silence (taqrir) occurs in the same session as the general text was revealed, it specifies that text. If it occurs after that session, it abrogates the general for that specific case.
3
State the Shafi'i position (absolute specification)
The Shafi'is hold that taqrir always specifies; it never abrogates, regardless of timing.
4
Analyze the proof and response
The Shafi'i rely on the principle that silence indicates permission and should harmonize with the general by specification. The Hanafi respond that if the silence occurs later, the general was already in effect, so abrogation is the only way to avoid contradiction.
5
Determine the practical thamarah
The dispute affects whether a later witnessed act of a Companion after a general verse is considered a specification (Shafi'i) or an abrogation (Hanafi) of that verse for similar future acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة (التقرير) هو السكوت عند رؤية فاعل يفعل الفعل مع القدرة على المنع (مخصص) لذلك الفاعل عند الشافعية (مطلق سواء كان مقارناً أو متأخراً ( وعند الحنفية إن كان العلم بالفعل (في مجلس ذكر العام فمخصص (وإلا) يكن في المجلس بل متأخر عنه (فنسخ لنا أن السكوت عند العلم (دليل الجواز (عادة لأن عادته الشريفة النهي عن المنكر، فهو كالنص على الجواز، فهو مخصص عند الشافعية مطلقاً، وعندنا إن تأخر فناسخ وإن قارن فمخصص (ثم إن ظهر علة مشتركة بين الفاعل وغيره (تعدى الحكم إلى غير الفاعل المشارك بالقياس أو بحكمي على الواحد حكمي على الجماعة وقد تكلم عليه شراح المنهاج»، وقد بينا سابقاً أن معناه ثابت، ثم إن تعدى الحكم بالقياس عند تأخر التقرير غير ظاهر فإنه يلزم حينئذ تعليل الناسخ ونسخ الحكم بالقياس إلا أن تكون العلة مفهومة لغة أو عرفاً، للشارع قطعاً إن جوز نسخ العبارة بالدلالة ( وإلا يظهر علة مشتركة فالمختار عدم التعدية لأن التعدية من غير جامع غير معقول (قال السبكي من الشافعية (المختار عندنا التعميم) مطلقاً (وإن لم يظهر الجامع ما لم يظهر ما يقتضي التخصيص بذلك الفاعل ( وذلك لقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم حكمي على الواحد الخ. قلنا ذلك الحديث (مخصوص إجماعاً بما علم فيه عدم الفارق) لاختلاف المكلفين في بعض الأحكام وههنا لم يعلم عدم الفارق، لأن الكلام فيما لا يعلم فيه الجامع (بل) علم أن عموم العام يمنع ثبوت حكم ذلك الفاعل في غيره من المكلفين (والا) يكن مخصوصاً بما علم فيه الجماع ويكون التقرير عاماً مطلقاً (كان التقرير نسخاً مطلقاً) إذ لم يبق تحت العام فرد في صورة وجود العلة أو عدمها فإن قلت: لعله يكون في بعض الأفراد علة مانعة عن ثبوت حكم التقرير قلت الكلام ليس في الأمر الخارج، بل في نفس التقرير والعموم كذا في «الحاشية».. لقائل أن يقول : إن تخصيص الحديث بما ذكرتم تخصيص من غير مخصص وما ذكرتم من اختلاف المكلفين، فإنما يقتضي التخصيص بما علم فيه فارق، فهو يلتزم النسخ إلا فيما علم فيه فارق فعند عموم الشريعة قرينة إرادة العموم من الواحد، وعلى هذا ينبغي أن يكون الخطاب لواحد من الأمة خطاباً للكل بهذا العموم كما نقل عن الحنابلة لكن شرعاً إلا لمانع (فافهم).
Issue: AI-Taqrir (tacit approval) is silence upon seeing an agent performing an action while having the ability to prevent it. It is a specifier for that agent according to the Shafi'is, absolutely, whether contemporaneous or later. According to the Hanafis, if the knowledge of the action occurs in the same session where the general was mentioned, it is a specifier; otherwise, if later, it is an abrogator for us, because silence in the presence of knowledge is an indication of permissibility (by custom), for his noble practice was to forbid evil, so it is like an explicit text on permissibility. So it is a specifier for the Shafi'is absolutely, and for us, if later, it abrogates; if contemporaneous, it specifies. Then, if there appears a common effective cause ('illa) between the agent and others, the ruling extends to other participants by analogy, or by the principle 'My ruling on one applies to the community'—the commentators on al-Minhaj have discussed this. We have previously established that its meaning is established. Then, extending the ruling by analogy when the taqrir is later is not apparent, because it would require providing an 'illa for the abrogator and abrogating the ruling by analogy, unless the 'illa is understood by language or custom, and the Lawgiver's permissibility of abrogating an explicit text by an indication is certain. If no common 'illa appears, the preferred view is non-extension, because extension without a commonality is irrational. AI-Subki (of the Shafi'is) said: our preferred view is generalization absolutely, even if the commonality is not apparent, unless there appears what necessitates specification to that agent, due to his statement 'My ruling on one is my ruling on the community.' We say: that hadith is specified by consensus to cases where the absence of difference is known, due to differences among obligated persons in some rulings. Here we do not know the absence of difference, because we are discussing what does not have a known commonality. Rather, it is known that the generality of the general prevents the establishment of that agent's ruling for other obligated persons. Otherwise, if it were specified to cases where commonality is known and the taqrir is absolutely general, then the taqrir would be absolute abrogation, since no individual would remain under the general regardless of the presence or absence of the 'illa. If you object: perhaps in some individuals there is a preventing cause for the establishment of the taqrir ruling. I say: the discussion is not about external matters, but about the taqrir itself and the general. This is in al-Hashiya. Someone may say: specifying the hadith as you have is specification without a specifier. What you mentioned about differences among obligated persons only necessitates specification where a difference is known, so it necessitates abrogation except where a difference is known. So, in light of the generality of the Shari'ah, there is a contextual indication of intending generality from 'one'. Accordingly, the address to one of the community should be an address to all by this generality, as transmitted from the Hanbalis, but according to the Shari'ah unless there is an obstacle. So understand.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This issue (مسألة) defines al-Taqrir (tacit approval) as the Prophet's silence upon seeing an action while able to forbid it. This silence indicates permission. The Shafi'is consider it a specifier for the actor in all cases, whether the silence occurs at the time of the general text or later. The Hanafis distinguish: if the action occurs in the same session where the general text was mentioned, the silence specifies; if after the session, it abrogates the general. The discussion then turns to whether the ruling of the tacitly approved action extends to others via analogy (qiyas). If there is a shared effective cause ('illa), it extends; if not, it does not. AI-Subki argues for generalization based on the hadith 'My ruling on one...', but the Hanafis respond that this hadith is specified by consensus to cases where no difference is known among the addressees. The author concludes that without a known commonality, the general prevents extension, and if we were to generalize, the taqrir would abrogate all individuals of the general, which is unreasonable.

Key Terms
التقرير (al-taqrīr): Silence of the Lawgiver upon witnessing an action while able to prevent it, indicating approval
مخصص (mukhassis): A specifier that limits the generality of a text
ناسخ (nāsikh): An abrogator that overrides a previous ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, when does the Prophet's tacit approval (taqrir) serve as an abrogator rather than a specifier?
A) When the approval occurs in the same session as the general text
B) When the approval occurs after the session in which the general text was mentioned
C) When the approval involves a different type of action
D) It never serves as an abrogator

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uniquely distinguishes taqrir as a specifier if contemporaneous with a general text and an abrogator if it occurs later, based on the need to avoid contradiction with the general.

Fi'l al-Sahabi as a Mukhassis: The Hanafi Argument
Dispute over Companion's action as specifier

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis consider a just Companion's action a specifier and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
A just Companion's contrary action reveals a hidden specifier, not rebellion.

This lesson explores a pivotal usul dispute: can the action of a Companion, known for his integrity, restrict a general Quranic or hadith command? The Hanafi school says yes—such an action is a strong contextual clue (qarina) that the general text has a specifier. The Shafi'i and Maliki schools say no—the general stands until a textual specification is found. Understanding this disagreement sharpens your ability to assess the weight of different types of evidence in istinbat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Read the opening phrase: 'Action of a just Companion... is a specifier according to the Hanafis and Hanbalis.' The issue is whether such an action can limit a general text.
2
State the two positions
Hanafis: It is a specifier. Shafi'is: The general must be followed; the Companion's action is not a proof.
Remember the school affiliation.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof: The Companion, being just and knowledgeable, would not act against a general without evidence. His action is like his saying 'this is specified.' It is a qarina, like consensus but weaker.
Note the distinction from interpretation (ta'wil).
4
Examine the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Shafi'is say interpretation of a narrator is not proof; how can action be? Hanafis respond: action is a qarina, not an interpretation. The narrator's ta'wil is one thing, his action is direct evidence.
Key distinction: action vs. interpretation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: If a later general command is found, and a Companion's action contradicts it, Hanafis will specify; Shafi'is will not. This affects how we derive rulings from the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة فعل الصحابي العادل العالم بخلاف العموم بعد العلم به (مخصص عند الحنفية والحنابلة فإن قلت : المشهور في كتب أكثر المشايخ أن تأويل الراوي ليس حجة، وقد صرح به الزيلعي في شرح الكنز في مواضع عديدة قلت : المراد هناك حمل الراوي الحديث أو الآية على أحد المحامل، كما في المشترك أو الخفي، وأما عمله على خلاف الظاهر فهو قرينة إرادته باتفاق مشايخنا، وسيتضح الفرق في بحث السنة إن شاء الله تعالى فافهم؛ ثم القول بالتخصيص مشكل بل المطابق لقواعدهم على تقدير كون فعله المخالف للعام حجة أن يحمل على الأعم من النسخ والتخصيص (خلافاً للشافعية والمالكية فيعمل بعموم العام ويترك اقتداء الصحابي، وهذا مشكل على رأيهم من التوقف في العام قبل البحث عن المخصص، فإنه إذا وجد عمل الصحابي خلاف العموم احتمل عند العقل وجدان المخصص، فإن من القطعيات أن عمله لا يكون إلا عن حجة شرعية في زعمه، لأن العمل من غير حجة معصية قد عصمهم أن يتوقف فيه حتى يعلم فساد حجته فتأمل لنا أنه) أي عمل الصحابي (دليل الدليل على التخصيص، لأنه بعد علمه لا يترك العمل بالعام إلا بدليل يدل على التخصيص، ولما كان عارفاً باللغة لا يخطىء فصار هذا العمل بمنزلة قوله : هذا العموم مخصوص، فيخص به كالإجماع، ثم هذا إنما يدل على أن المعمول الخصوص، وأما أن العام مخصوص فلا يدل عليه بخصوصه بل يحتمل أن يكون منسوخ البعض ، ولهذا زاد في «التحرير» وقال : فيحمل على التخصيص، لأنه أهون من النسخ، فتأمل فيه فإنه موضع تأمل (قيل) إنه دليل لكن (ظناً لا قطعاً) والظن لا يكفي بخلاف الإجماع، لأنه دليل الدليل قطعاً، وبخلاف عمله خلاف النص المفسر، فإنه لا مساغ للتأويل فيه قطعاً من مقطوع العدالة، فتعين النسخ (أقول لا يجب القطع) في المخصص كمفهوم خبر الواحد هذا يتم إلزاماً ولا يتم على أصولنا، لأن العام قطعي إلاّ إذا خصص الدعوى بالعام المخصوص البعض، فإن قلت : هذا الظن يجوز أن يكون ضعيفاً من العام المخصوص فلا يصلح قلت كلا فإن حجة الصحابي إما قرينة جزئية مخصصة أو كلام مخصص أو ناسخ أو قياس، وهذا العام أضعف من الكل كما مر مراراً، فإن قلت: فحينئذ يلزم تقليد المجتهد للصحابي قال : (ولا يلزم تقليد المجتهد لأنه أي التخصيص (عن دليل) مخصص (مخصوص) دال عليه عمله وإن دل اجمالاً على المخصص حقيقة، قيل) في رده
Issue: The action of a just Companion who knows the general text and acts contrary to it after knowing it is a specifier according to the Hanafis and Hanbalis. If you say: the famous view in the books of most scholars is that the interpretation of a narrator is not a proof, and al-Zayla'i stated this in his commentary on al-Kanz in numerous places. I say: the meaning there is that the narrator's interpretation of a hadith or verse is to carry it on one of its possible meanings, as in a homonym or ambiguous term. As for his action contrary to the apparent meaning, it is a contextual indication (qarina) of his intended meaning according to the agreement of our scholars. The difference will become clear in the discussion of Sunnah, if Allah wills, so understand. Then the claim of specification is problematic; rather, in accordance with their principles, if his action contrary to the general is considered a proof, it should be interpreted as having the more general possibility of abrogation and specification (contrary to the Shafi'is and Malikis). They act upon the general and discard following the Companion. This is problematic from their perspective of suspending judgment on the general before searching for a specifier. For if the Companion's action contrary to the general is found, the intellect entertains the possibility of finding a specifier, for it is a certainty that his action is not without a legal proof in his view, because acting without proof is a sin from which they are protected. So one should suspend judgment until his proof is found to be invalid. Ponder. Our proof is that his action is an evidence of the evidence for specification, because after knowing the general, he does not abandon acting on it except with evidence indicating specification. And since he is a language expert who does not err, this action becomes like his saying 'this general is specified', and thus it specifies like consensus. However, this only indicates that the acted-upon is specific; it does not specifically indicate that the general is specified, but it could be that some part was abrogated. For this reason, the author of al-Tahrir added: 'It is interpreted as specification because it is less severe than abrogation.' Ponder, for it is a point of reflection. It is said: it is a proof, but speculative, not certain. Conjecture is insufficient, unlike consensus which is a proof of proof with certainty, and unlike his action contrary to an explicit text (nass mufassar), where there is no room for interpretation due to certainty of integrity, so abrogation is determined. I say: certainty is not required in the specifier, like the concept of a solitary report (mafhum khabar al-wahid). This is an argument of obligation but not according to our principles, because the general is certain unless the claim is specified by the partially specified general. If you say: this speculation may be weak from the specified general and thus is not valid. I say: no, for the Companion's proof is either a specific partial contextual indication, or a specific text, or an abrogator, or an analogy, and this general is weaker than all, as has been repeated. If you say: then this would require the mujtahid to imitate the Companion. He said: imitation of the mujtahid is not required, because the specification is based on a specifier evidence that his action indicates. Even if it indicates the specifier in general, it is real. It is said in refutation...
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This issue (مسألة) addresses whether the action of a just Companion, who is aware of a general text and acts contrary to it, serves as a specifier of that general. The Hanafis and Hanbalis hold that it does. They argue by analogy: just as the Companion's interpretation (ta'wil) of a text is not binding, his action is different—it is a qarina (contextual indication) that he knows of a specifier. The Shafi'is and Malikis reject this, holding that the general must be followed and the Companion's action is not a valid specifier. The author defends the Hanafi view: since the Companion is upright and knowledgeable, his action cannot be based on mere opinion; he must have evidence. Therefore, his action is like his stating that the general is specified. However, the evidence is speculative (zanni) not certain, but this is sufficient because the general itself, after specification, is not certain. The objection that this leads to taqlid (blind imitation) of the Companion is rejected: the mujtahid does not follow the Companion blindly but uses his action as an indicator of a specifier, which he then investigates. The danger of abrogation is avoided by preferring specification as the lighter option.

Key Terms
فعل الصحابي (fi'l al-sahabī): The action of a Companion that is known to contradict a general text
مخصص (mukhassis): A specifier that limits the application of a general text

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, why is the action of a just Companion considered a specifier of a general text?
A) Because the Companion's interpretation is considered a proof
B) Because the Companion's action, given his knowledge and integrity, indicates the existence of a specifier
C) Because the Companion's action abrogates the general
D) Because the Companion is infallible

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants evidentiary weight to the practice of the Companions, considering their actions as contextual clues that can specify general texts, a position rooted in their trust in the Companions' integrity and linguistic acuity.

Companion Action as Specifier: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Debate on companion practice as a specifier for general texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi argument for why a companion's contrary action specifies a general text (amm) and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A companion's practice contrary to a general text is a probable proof for specification, not abrogation.

This passage delves into a foundational usul dispute: can the action of a just and knowledgeable companion, when it contradicts the apparent meaning of a general Quranic or hadith text, serve as a specifier (mukhassis) that restricts the general ruling? The Hanafis and Hanbalis argue yes, while the Shafi'is and Malikis hold that the general remains untouched. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to evaluate evidence hierarchy and the role of companion practice in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on companion action
The Hanafi school considers a just companion's action contrary to a general text as a proof of specification (dalil al-dalil ala al-takhsis). Because the companion is knowledgeable and just, his action implies he had evidence for specification.
This is a probabilistic (zanni) proof, not certain.
2
Identify the first Shafi'i/Maliki objection
The opposing school argues that the general text itself is a proof (hujja), while the companion's action is not a proof, so there is no conflict and thus no specification.
They deny the probative value of the action altogether.
3
Trace the Hanafi rebuttal to the first objection
Hanafis respond that the companion's action is indeed a proof because it indicates a specifier. The claim that it is not a proof is rejected (mamnu').
The action becomes like a statement: 'this general is specified'.
4
Examine the second objection and Hanafi response
The opponents ask: if the action is a specifier, why would another companion oppose it? Hanafis answer that when another companion opposes, the probabilities cancel each other, leaving the general intact.
The principle: 'al-zann yudfa' bi al-zann' (probability is repelled by probability).
5
Note the preference for specification over abrogation
Hanafis interpret the action as specification rather than abrogation because specification is easier (ahwan) and preserves the general's authority where possible.
This reflects the legal principle of minimizing change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة فعل الصحابي العادل العالم بخلاف العموم بعد العلم به (مخصص عند الحنفية والحنابلة فإن قلت : المشهور في كتب أكثر المشايخ أن تأويل الراوي ليس حجة، وقد صرح به الزيلعي في شرح الكنز في مواضع عديدة قلت : المراد هناك حمل الراوي الحديث أو الآية على أحد المحامل، كما في المشترك أو الخفي، وأما عمله على خلاف الظاهر فهو قرينة إرادته باتفاق مشايخنا، وسيتضح الفرق في بحث السنة إن شاء الله تعالى فافهم؛ ثم أن يكون ضعيفاً من العام المخصوص فلا يصلح قلت كلا فإن حجة الصحابي إما قرينة جزئية مخصصة أو كلام مخصص أو ناسخ أو قياس، وهذا العام أضعف من الكل كما مر مراراً، فإن قلت: فحينئذ يلزم تقليد المجتهد للصحابي (لا يكفي) لعمل المجتهد ما لم تحصل معرفته بعينه وإذا لم يكف لم يبق إلا التقليد (أقول) هذا (منقوض بالإجماع فإنه لا يتوقف تخصيصه على معرفة المخصص بعينه وما ذكر القائل من عدم كفاية الاعتقاد الإجمالي دعوى من غير حجة فلا تسمع (فتأمل) فيه الشافعية والمالكية (قالوا: أولاً: العموم حجة، وفعله ليس بحجة فلا تعارض فلا تخصيص (قلنا) عدم حجية فعله (ممنوع) كيف وفعله لما كان دالاً على المخصص وجب اعتباره (و) قالوا :(ثانياً : لو صح) فعله مخصصاً لم يجز مخالفة صحابي آخر (له لأنها مخالفة حجة واجبة العمل (وقد جاز) خلاف الآخر إياه اتفاقاً، قلنا لا تسلم الملازمة وفعله إنما كان واجب العمل ما دام ظن دلالته على المخصص باقياً. وعند مخالفة صحابي آخر لم يبق كيف وهو دليل العدم) أي عدم المخصص لأن الظاهر أنه لو كان لعلمه وعمل بمقتضاه ، لأن المخصص يكون ملاصقاً (والظن) يدفع (بالظن) فتساقطا وبقي العام كما كان (تأمل) لعل وجهه أنه إن جاز الخطأ في زعم المخصص مخصصاً، فلا يكفي علمه الإجمالي فتأمل فيه .
Issue: The action of a just and knowledgeable companion contrary to the general (text) after knowing it is a specifier according to the Hanafis and Hanbalis. If you say: The well-known in the books of most scholars is that the interpretation of the narrator is not a proof, and al-Zayla'i has stated this in Sharh al-Kanz in many places. I say: What is meant there is the narrator's interpretation of the hadith or verse according to one of the interpretations, as in the common or hidden (text). As for his action contrary to the apparent meaning, it is a contextual indication of his intent according to the consensus of our scholars, and the difference will become clear in the discussion of the Sunnah, God willing. So understand. Then the statement of specification is problematic; rather, according to their principles, if his action contrary to the general is considered a proof, it should be interpreted as the more general of abrogation and specification. Contrary to the Shafi'is and Malikis, who act upon the general of the general and abandon following the companion. This is problematic according to their view of suspending judgment on the general before searching for a specifier. For if a companion's action contrary to the general is found, reason would consider the existence of a specifier. Because it is certain that his action is only based on a legal proof in his opinion, since acting without proof is a sin which they are protected from. So one must suspend judgment until the invalidity of his proof is known. Reflect. For us, i.e., the action of the companion is a proof of the proof for specification, because after knowing (the general), he does not abandon acting on the general except due to a proof indicating specification. And since he is knowledgeable in the language and does not err, this action becomes like his saying 'this general is specified,' so it specifies like consensus. Then this only indicates that what is acted upon is particular; as for that the general is specified, it does not indicate it specifically, but may be that some part is abrogated. Therefore, in al-Tahrir it added: and it is interpreted as specification because it is easier than abrogation. Reflect on it, for it is a place of reflection. It was said that it is a proof but only probabilistically, not certainly, and probability is not sufficient unlike consensus, because it is a proof of the proof certainly, and unlike his action contrary to the clearly explicit text (nass mufassar), because there is no room for interpretation therein certainly due to his certain justice, so abrogation is determined. I say: Certainty is not required in the specifier like the implication of a solitary report; this is an argument to refute (them) and does not stand according to our principles, because the general is certain unless the claim is specified by a partially specified general. If you say: This probability may be weak from the partially specified general, so it is not suitable. I say: No, for the companion's proof is either a partial contextual indication specifying (the general), or a specifying statement, or an abrogator, or analogy, and this general is weaker than all (of these) as has been repeatedly mentioned. If you say: Then this entails the mujtahid following the companion (taqlid). He said: And it does not entail taqlid of the mujtahid because the specification (is based on) a proof, a specific specifier indicated by his action, although it indicates the specifier in an absolute sense, it was said in its rebuttal: The truth is that the belief that there is a specifying proof in general while the belief is general is not sufficient for the mujtahid's action unless he has specific knowledge of it. If it is not sufficient, nothing remains but taqlid. I say: This is refuted by consensus, because its specification does not depend on knowing the specifier specifically, and what the proponent mentioned about the insufficiency of general belief is a claim without proof, so it is not heard. Reflect on it. The Shafi'is and Malikis said: First: The general is a proof, and his action is not a proof, so there is no contradiction, hence no specification. We say: The lack of probative value of his action is denied. How so? For when his action indicates a specifier, it must be considered. And they said: Second, if his action were valid as a specifier, it would not be permissible for another companion to oppose him, because it is opposing a proof that must be acted upon, yet opposition to him by another has occurred by consensus. We say: We do not accept the entailment; his action is only obligatory to act upon as long as the probability of its indicating a specifier remains. When another companion opposes, it no longer remains, for it is an indication of absence, i.e., absence of a specifier, because the apparent is that if there were a specifier, he would have known it and acted according to it, since the specifier would be adjacent. And probability is repelled by probability, so they cancel each other and the general remains as it was. Reflect. Perhaps its reasoning is that if error is possible in considering (the action) as a specifier, then his general knowledge is not sufficient. Reflect on it.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul dispute about whether a companion's action that contradicts a general text (ʻāmm) acts as a specifier (mukhassis) for that text. The Hanafis and Hanbalis hold that it does, while the Shafiʻis and Malikis reject it. The author presents the Hanafi argument: a just, knowledgeable companion would not abandon the general without evidence of specification; thus his action functions like stating the specification, akin to consensus (ijmāʻ). The objection that this is merely probabilistic (zann) not certain is countered by noting that certainty is not required—similar to how a solitary hadith (khabar wāhid) can specify. The Shafiʻi/Maliki counterarguments are addressed: (1) that the companion's action is not a proof, (2) that if it were, opposing companions would be forbidden, yet such opposition occurs. The Hanafi response is that the proof stands only while the probability of specification remains; when another companion opposes, the probabilities cancel, leaving the general intact. The discussion highlights the Hanafi preference for specification over abrogation (naskh) as it is 'easier'. The translator's note: 'taqlid' here means following another's opinion without evidence.

Key Terms
فعل الصحابي (fiʻl al-ṣaḥābī): Action of a companion that contradicts the apparent meaning of a general text; used as evidence for specification.
مخصص (mukhassɪs): Something that specifies (makes particular) a general ruling; here, the companion's action is considered a mukhassɪs.
عام (ʿāmm): A term that covers all individuals of its category without restriction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, when a companion acts contrary to a general text, what does that action indicate?
A) The text is abrogated
B) The text is specified
C) The companion erred
D) The text is abandoned

Key Takeaway
A companion's practice contrary to a general text is a probable proof for specification, not abrogation, and it is considered a valid indicator only when no opposing companion practice exists.

Does Singling Out an Individual from a General Specify It?
Rule on specification by singling out a general individual

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on singling out individuals from general rulings and apply it to hadith examples.

Core Idea
Mentioning a specific example does not limit a general rule unless a clear opposed concept exists.

A common fallacy in understanding general Quranic and hadith texts is assuming that when a specific individual is mentioned alongside a general ruling, the ruling is restricted to that individual. The Hanafi school firmly rejects this notion. In this lesson, we examine the key usul principle: 'إفراد فرد من العام بحكمه لا يخصصه' — singling out one individual from the general with its ruling does not specify it. We will unpack the evidence, including the famous hadith about tanning hides, and the debate with Abu Thawr. By the end, you will be able to identify when a citation truly specifies a general ruling and when it remains merely an example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its condition
Read the statement: 'لا يخصصه إلا إذا كان له مفهوم مخالف' — it does not specify unless it has an opposed implication. Understand that the default is non-specification; the exception is when a mafhum mukhalafa is present.
The rule applies to any general text (amm) where an individual from the class is singled out with the same ruling.
2
Examine the hadith example
Consider the two hadith: (1) 'Any hide that is tanned becomes pure' (general), and (2) 'Its tanning is its purification' regarding the sheep of Maimuna (specific). The Hanafi position holds that the specific mention does not restrict the general ruling to only sheep hides.
The general ruling applies to all hides; the specific mention is just an example.
3
Understand the opposing view (Abu Thawr)
Abu Thawr argues that the specific mention creates a mafhum mukhalafa: because the Prophet specified 'sheep', the ruling applies only to animals whose meat is eaten (or only sheep). This is based on the concept of condition/attribute.
Abu Thawr is not from the four main schools; his view is considered weak.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
Hanafis reject mafhum al-mukhalafa as a proof (dalil) altogether. Even if accepted, this would require accepting mafhum al-laqab (concept of a title), which is rejected by all proponents of concept. Therefore, the specific mention does not specify.
The rebuttal is twofold: denial of the concept, and its impossibility in this case.
5
Apply the rule to new scenarios
Given a general Quranic verse like 'وَالْمُطَلَّقَاتُ يَتَرَبَّصْنَ بِأَنفُسِهِنَّ ثَلَاثَةَ قُرُوءٍ' (divorced women wait three periods), and a specific mention of a certain type of divorcee, the general rule remains unless an opposed concept is present.
Practice applying the rule to other usul texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة إفراد فرد من العام بحكمه أي بحكم العام الموافق له (لا يخصصه إلا إذا كان له مفهوم) مخالف (عند (قائليه كإفراد فرد موصوف بصفة أو معلق بشرط، كما في حديث القلتين مثاله : أيما إهاب دبغ فقد طهر» رواه أحمد (مع (قوله صلوات الله وسلامه عليه وآله وأصحابه (في شاة) أم المؤمنين (ميمونة) رضي الله عنها (دباغها طهورها») قد أنكر المخرّجون هذا اللفظ في شاة أم المؤمنين بل في قربة كما رواه أحمد سلمة أن رسول الله صلى الله عن عليه وآله وسلم جاء في غزوة تبوك على أهل بيت فإذا قربة معلقة فسال الماء فقالوا له : يا رسول الله إنها ميتة فقال : دباغها طهورها والذي في شاة أم المؤمنين ميمونة ما رواه الشيخان : هلا أخذتم إهابها فدبغتموه فانتفعتم فقالوا إنها ميتة فقال: «إنما حرم أكلها» (خلافاً لأبي ثور فيختص الإهاب عنده بالشاه) في رواية أو بما يؤكل لحمه) في رواية أخرى لعل وجهه اعتبار المفهوم الموافق فيخرج ما وراءه (لنا) أنه لا تعارض) وهو ظاهر ولا تخصيص بدون التعارض أبو ثور وأتباعه (قالوا له أي للفرد المفرد من العام (مفهوم) مخالف يعارضه والمفهوم يخصص العموم قلنا لا نسلم المفهوم المخالف فإنا ننكره رأساً و(لو سلم) ثبوت المفهوم ( فهو ) أي اعتبار المفهوم ههنا (فرع) ثبوت مفهوم اللقب وهو ردّ) عند القائلين بالمفهوم أيضاً، وما قيل يجوز أن يكون إفراد بعض الأفراد موجباً لمفهوم العدد إذ نزاع أبي ثور يعم الكل فلا يتمشى هذا الجواب هناك، فليس بشيء، لأن تلك المواضع متفقة التخصيص عند القائلين بالمفهوم فلا يحتاجون إلى الجواب، وما قيل إن الكلام أن نفس الإفراد مخصص أم لا، فيرد عليه أن دليل أبي ثور لا ينطبق حينئذ فتأمل.
Issue: Singling out one individual from the general with its ruling, i.e., with the ruling of the general that corresponds to it, does not specify it unless it has an opposed implication (concept), according to its proponents. Like singling out an individual described by an attribute or conditional, as in the hadith of the two wells (qultatayn): for example, 'Any hide that is tanned becomes pure' narrated by Ahmad with his statement (peace and blessings be upon him and his companions) regarding the sheep of the Mother of the Believers Maimuna (may God be pleased with her): 'Its tanning is its purification.' The hadith critics have denied this wording regarding the sheep of the Mother of the Believers; rather, it is about a water-skin as narrated by Ahmad ibn Salamah: The Messenger of God (peace and blessings be upon him) came during the expedition of Tabuk to a household and found a water-skin hanging, so water leaked. They said: O Messenger of God, it is dead meat. He said: 'Its tanning is its purification.' And what is reported about the sheep of Maimuna is what the two shaykhs narrated: 'Why did you not take its hide, tan it, and benefit from it?' They said: It is dead meat. He said: 'Only eating it is forbidden.' Contrary to Abu Thawr, who holds that the hide is restricted to sheep, in one narration, or to what is eaten meat, in another narration. Perhaps his reason is considering the concurrent implication, so what is beyond is excluded. Our proof: There is no contradiction, and that is apparent; there is no specification without contradiction. Abu Thawr and his followers said to him, i.e., to the singled-out individual from the general: It has an opposed implication that contradicts, and the implication specifies the general. We say: We do not accept the opposed implication, for we deny it entirely. And if the existence of the implication is granted, then considering it here is subsidiary to establishing the implication of the title (laqab), which is rejected even by proponents of the implication. And what is said that singling out some individuals may necessitate an implication of number, since the dispute of Abu Thawr encompasses all, so this answer cannot apply there, is nothing, because those places are agreed upon specification by proponents of implication, so they need no answer. And what is said that the discussion is whether the mere singling out is a specifier or not, then it is replied that the proof of Abu Thawr does not apply then. Reflect.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage states a usul rule: mentioning a specific individual from a general category does not limit the general ruling unless the mention carries an opposed implication (concept of a restrictive adjective or condition). The Hanafi position is that mere mention is not a specifier. The author uses the example of the tanning of hides: the general rule 'any hide tanned is pure' is not specified by the specific mention of a sheep's hide or a water-skin in hadith. Abu Thawr argued that the specific mention indicates specification (e.g., only sheep hide is meant). The Hanafi response is that they reject the concept of opposed implication (mufaham al-mukhalafa) as a proof, and even if accepted, the specification from singling out an individual would require the concept of the title (laqab), which is rejected. The discussion shows the Hanafi principle that general words remain general unless a clear specifier is found, and mere examples do not restrict.

Key Terms
إفراد فرد من العام (ifrād fard min al-ʿāmm): Mentioning one specific individual from a general category along with the same ruling as the general.
مفهوم مخالف (mafhūm mukhalafa): An implication from a text that contradicts the general implication, derived from a restrictive clause (condition, attribute, etc.).
مفهوم اللقب (mafhūm al-laqab): An implication from the mention of a specific title or name (e.g., 'Zayd') that restricts a ruling to that named individual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule, when does singling out one individual from a general ruling specify that general?
A) Always
B) Never
C) Only if it has an opposed implication (concept)
D) Only if the individual is a companion

Key Takeaway
A general ruling remains general unless a clear opposed implication (mafhum mukhalafa) is proven; mere mention of an example does not restrict it.

Adequacy of General Belief in a Specifier
Dispute on whether general belief in a specifier suffices for the mujtahid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position on whether a mujtahid's general belief in a specifier is sufficient and identify the key arguments in the dispute.

Core Idea
General belief in a specifier is insufficient; the mujtahid must know the specific specifier, otherwise only taqlid remains.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut presents a nuanced usul dispute: when a mujtahid encounters a general text and has a general belief that there exists a specifier but does not know it specifically, can he act on the general text? The author argues that general belief is not enough, and the only alternative is taqlid. The text then presents objections based on ijma and the actions of the Prophet and Companions. By understanding this dispute, you will sharpen your ability to assess the role of presumption and evidence in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial claim
The author states that general belief in a specifier is insufficient for the mujtahid's action; he must have specific knowledge. Note the consequence: if insufficient, only taqlid remains.
The claim is that i'tiqad ijmali is not enough.
2
Analyze the objection using ijma
An objector points out that ijma itself is a proof that specification does not require knowing the specific specifier. This challenges the author's claim. Consider how ijma is used as a counterexample.
Ijma on a ruling does not require us to know the specific evidence for that ruling.
3
Examine the Shafi'i/Maliki arguments
Two arguments are presented: first, the general is a proof but the Prophet's action is not a proof, so no conflict; second, if the action were a specifier, opposing another Companion would be prohibited, yet it occurred. Understand each point.
These arguments aim to show that a specifier does not need to be known specifically.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi responses
The Hanafi responses deny the premises: the Prophet's action is a proof because it indicates the specifier, and the action is binding as long as the presumption of indication remains. When a Companion opposes, the presumption is rebutted.
The key concept is that presumptions can cancel each other out.
5
Reflect on the final 'tأمل'
The author ends with reflection (tأمل), suggesting that if error is possible in claiming a specifier, then general knowledge is insufficient. This leaves the issue open for deeper thought.
The lesson is not definitively closed; it invites further consideration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحق أن الاعتقاد بأن ههنا دليلا مخصصاً (إجمالاً) حال كون الاعتقاد مجملاً (لا يكفي) لعمل المجتهد ما لم تحصل معرفته بعينه وإذا لم يكف لم يبق إلا التقليد (أقول) هذا (منقوض بالإجماع فإنه لا يتوقف تخصيصه على معرفة المخصص بعينه وما ذكر القائل من عدم كفاية الاعتقاد الإجمالي دعوى من غير حجة فلا تسمع (فتأمل) فيه الشافعية والمالكية (قالوا: أولاً: العموم حجة، وفعله ليس بحجة فلا تعارض فلا تخصيص (قلنا) عدم حجية فعله (ممنوع) كيف وفعله لما كان دالاً على المخصص وجب اعتباره (و) قالوا :(ثانياً : لو صح) فعله مخصصاً لم يجز مخالفة صحابي آخر (له لأنها مخالفة حجة واجبة العمل (وقد جاز) خلاف الآخر إياه اتفاقاً، قلنا لا نسلم الملازمة وفعله إنما كان واجب العمل ما دام ظن دلالته على المخصص باقياً. وعند مخالفة صحابي آخر لم يبق كيف وهو دليل العدم) أي عدم المخصص لأن الظاهر أنه لو كان لعلمه وعمل بمقتضاه ، لأن المخصص يكون ملاصقاً (والظن) يدفع (بالظن) فتساقطا وبقي العام كما كان (تأمل) لعل وجهه أنه إن جاز الخطأ في زعم المخصص مخصصاً، فلا يكفي علمه الإجمالي فتأمل فيه .
The truth is that the belief that there exists a specifying evidence (in general) while the belief is general (is not sufficient) for the action of the mujtahid until he obtains specific knowledge of it. And if it is not sufficient, nothing remains but taqlid. I say: This is refuted by ijma, because specification does not depend on knowledge of the specific specifier. And what the speaker mentioned regarding the insufficiency of general belief is a claim without proof, so it is not heard. Consider: The Shafi'is and Malikis said: First: The general is a proof, and his action is not a proof, so there is no conflict and no specification. We say: The non-authoritativeness of his action is denied. How so? Since his action indicates the specifier, it must be considered. And they said: Secondly: If his action were valid as a specifier, then opposing another Companion would not be permissible because it would be opposing a binding proof. Yet opposition to him has occurred by agreement. We say: We do not accept the entailment. His action was only binding as long as the presumption of its indication of the specifier remained. When another Companion opposed, it did not remain, because it is evidence of absence — i.e., absence of the specifier — because the apparent is that if there were one, he would have known and acted accordingly, since the specifier would be attached. And presumption is repelled by presumption, so they cancel out and the general remains as it was. Consider: Perhaps its aspect is that if error is possible in claiming something as a specifier, then his general knowledge is not sufficient. So consider it.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute concerning the adequacy of a mujtahid's general belief in the existence of a specifier for a general text. The author begins by stating that mere general belief is insufficient; the mujtahid must have specific knowledge of the specifier. He then presents an objection: this claim is refuted by ijma (consensus), since specification in ijma does not require knowledge of the specific specifier. The Shafi'is and Malikis then raise two arguments: first, that the general is a proof but the Prophet's action is not a proof (so no conflict), but the author denies that the action is not a proof, arguing that it indicates the specifier. Second, they argue that if the action were a specifier, one could not oppose another Companion, but opposition has occurred; the author responds by saying that the action was binding only as long as the presumption of indication remained, and when another Companion opposed, that presumption was rebutted. In the end, presumptions cancel out, leaving the general as is. The author then reflects that if error is possible in the claim of specification, general knowledge is not sufficient.

Key Terms
اعتقاد إجمالي (i'tiqād ijmālī): A general belief in the existence of a specifier without specific knowledge of its identity.
مخصص (mukhaṣṣiṣ): Evidence that specifies a general ruling, restricting its application.
تقليد (taqlīd): Following another's opinion without evidence; the alternative if the mujtahid cannot act on general belief.
إجماع (ijmāʿ): Consensus of scholars; used here as a proof that specification does not require specific knowledge of the specifier.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a mujtahid's general belief in the existence of a specifier?
A) It suffices for action.
B) It is insufficient without specific knowledge.
C) It is prohibited.
D) It is recommended.

Key Takeaway
A mujtahid cannot act on a general text if he only has a general belief that a specifier exists; he must either know the specifier specifically or resort to taqlid.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Rule of Singling Out an Individual (Ifrad) and Its Effect on Specification
Dispute on whether mentioning an individual with the same ruling as the general specifies the general

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on ifrad and apply it to distinguish when mentioning an individual specifies the general or not.

Core Idea
Mentioning an individual with the same ruling as the general does not specify unless a contrary implication exists.

This passage addresses a subtle usul issue: when a general command is followed by a specific mention of an individual with the same ruling, does that single out the individual and restrict the general? The author presents the Hanafi position that such singling out (ifrad) does not cause specification (takhsis) unless the individual carries a contrary implication (mafhum mukhalif). He defends this against Abu Thawr, who argues that the specific mention creates a conflict that requires specification. Understanding this rule sharpens your ability to interpret general texts and avoid over-specification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim and counterclaim
First, identify the two opposing positions: the Hanafi view (ifrad does not specify) and Abu Thawr's view (ifrad does specify via contrary implication).
Both sides agree on the case: a general term is followed by a specific individual with the same ruling.
2
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The Hanafi argument rests on the absence of conflict (ta'arud). Since the individual's ruling matches the general, there is no contradiction that would necessitate specification.
The general remains operative over all its individuals.
3
Analyze Abu Thawr's argument and the Hanafi response
Abu Thawr claims the individual has a contrary implication that conflicts with the general. The Hanafi response denies the validity of contrary implication (mafhum mukhalif) entirely, or if conceded, shows it is a branch of mafhum al-laqab, which is rejected.
The debate hinges on the authority of mafhum mukhalif and its sub-types.
4
Apply the rule to a practical example
Consider the hadith: 'Any skin that is tanned is purified' (general). Then the Prophet said about the goat of Maymunah: 'Its tanning is its purification.' According to Hanafis, the general ruling applies to all skins, not just that goat, because the specific mention does not create a contrary implication.
This example is directly cited in the passage.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: under the Hanafi view, the general ruling applies universally; under Abu Thawr's view, it is restricted to the specified individual (or similar ones).
This shows why the rule matters for fatwa and interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
إفراد فرد من العام بحكمه أي بحكم العام الموافق له (لا يخصصه إلا إذا كان له مفهوم) مخالف (عند (قائليه كإفراد فرد موصوف بصفة أو معلق بشرط، كما في حديث القلتين مثاله : أيما إهاب دبغ فقد طهر» رواه أحمد (مع (قوله صلوات الله وسلامه عليه وآله وأصحابه (في شاة) أم المؤمنين (ميمونة) رضي الله عنها (دباغها طهورها») قد أنكر المخرّجون هذا اللفظ في شاة أم المؤمنين بل في قربة كما رواه أحمد سلمة أن رسول الله صلى الله عن عليه وآله وسلم جاء في غزوة تبوك على أهل بيت فإذا قربة معلقة فسال الماء فقالوا له : يا رسول الله إنها ميتة فقال : دباغها طهورها والذي في شاة أم المؤمنين ميمونة ما رواه الشيخان : هلا أخذتم إهابها فدبغتموه فانتفعتم فقالوا إنها ميتة فقال: «إنما حرم أكلها» (خلافاً لأبي ثور فيختص الإهاب عنده بالشاه) في رواية أو بما يؤكل لحمه) في رواية أخرى لعل وجهه اعتبار المفهوم الموافق فيخرج ما وراءه (لنا) أنه لا تعارض) وهو ظاهر ولا تخصيص بدون التعارض أبو ثور وأتباعه (قالوا له أي للفرد المفرد من العام (مفهوم) مخالف يعارضه والمفهوم يخصص العموم قلنا لا نسلم المفهوم المخالف فإنا ننكره رأساً و(لو سلم) ثبوت المفهوم ( فهو ) أي اعتبار المفهوم ههنا (فرع) ثبوت مفهوم اللقب وهو ردّ) عند القائلين بالمفهوم أيضاً، وما قيل يجوز أن يكون إفراد بعض الأفراد موجباً لمفهوم العدد إذ نزاع أبي ثور يعم الكل فلا يتمشى هذا الجواب هناك، فليس بشيء، لأن تلك المواضع متفقة التخصيص عند القائلين بالمفهوم فلا يحتاجون إلى الجواب، وما قيل إن الكلام أن نفس الإفراد مخصص أم لا، فيرد عليه أن دليل أبي ثور لا ينطبق حينئذ فتأمل.
Issue: Singling out an individual from the general with its ruling, i.e., with the ruling of the general that agrees with it, does not specify it unless it has a contrary implication according to its proponents, such as singling out an individual described by an attribute or qualified by a condition, as in the hadith of the two qullas. Example: 'Any skin that is tanned is purified' narrated by Ahmad, along with his saying (peace be upon him and his family and companions) regarding the goat of the Mother of the Believers Maymunah (may Allah be pleased with her): 'Its tanning is its purification.' The hadith scholars have denied this wording regarding the goat of the Mother of the Believers; rather, it is about a water skin as narrated by Ahmad from Salamah that the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him and his family) came in the expedition of Tabuk to a household and found a hanging water skin, and water dripped, so they said: O Messenger of Allah, it is carrion. He said: 'Its tanning is its purification.' And what is about the goat of the Mother of the Believers Maymunah is what the two shaykhs narrated: 'Why did you not take its skin and tan it and benefit from it?' They said: It is carrion. He said: 'Only its eating is forbidden.' Contrary to Abu Thawr, who specifies 'ihab' to the goat in one narration, or to what is eaten meat in another narration. Perhaps his aspect is considering the coincident implication, so what is beyond is excluded. For us: there is no conflict, and there is no specification without conflict. Abu Thawr and his followers said: For him, i.e., the individual singled out from the general, there is a contrary implication that conflicts with it, and the implication specifies the general. We say: We do not accept the contrary implication, for we deny it entirely. And if the implication is conceded, then considering it here is a branch of establishing the implication of the title, which is rejected also among proponents of implication. And what is said that singling out some individuals may necessitate an implication of number, since the dispute of Abu Thawr covers all, so this answer does not apply there, is nothing, because those places agree on specification according to proponents of implication, so they do not need an answer. And what is said that the issue is whether the singling out itself specifies or not, then it is countered that Abu Thawr's evidence does not apply then. So consider.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage addresses a usul rule: whether singling out an individual from a general category and mentioning it with the same ruling as the general constitutes specification (takhsis) of the general. The author uses the example of the hadith 'Any skin that is tanned is purified' and the specific mention of the goat of Maymunah with 'Its tanning is its purification.' He clarifies that the hadith scholars consider the wording about the goat problematic; the correct narration is about a water skin. The dispute is with Abu Thawr, who holds that the term 'ihab' (skin) in the first hadith is specified to the goat (or to animals whose meat is eaten) based on the concept of coincident implication (mafhum muwafiq). The Hanafi position (lana) is that there is no conflict requiring specification; the general remains general. The author refutes Abu Thawr's reliance on contrary implication (mafhum mukhalif) by denying it entirely, or if conceded, by arguing that the implication here is a branch of the implication of the title (mafhum al-laqab), which is generally rejected even by proponents of implication. The passage ends with reflection on the weakness of Abu Thawr's evidence.

Key Terms
إفراد (ifrād): Singling out an individual from the general category by mentioning it specifically.
مفهوم مخالف (mafhūm mukhalif): A contrary implication; a derived meaning that opposes the apparent meaning of the text.
مفهوم موافق (mafhūm muwāfiq): A coincident implication; a meaning that agrees with the apparent meaning.
تخصيص (takhṣīṣ): Specification of a general term, restricting its application to some individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, when does singling out an individual from a general term with its ruling specify the general?
A) Always.
B) When the individual has a contrary implication.
C) Never.
D) When the individual is described by an attribute.

Key Takeaway
Mentioning an individual with the same ruling as the general does not automatically specify the general; specification requires a conflict, typically from a contrary implication.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Does a Pronoun Referring to Some Individuals Specify the General? The Hanafi Waqf Position
Dispute on whether a pronoun referring to some individuals of a general term specifies the general

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions on whether a pronoun referring to some individuals of a general term constitutes specification, and identify the Hanafi preferred view of waqf.

Core Idea
When a pronoun refers to only some individuals of a general term, the correct position is to stop (waqf) because both general and pronoun are equally susceptible to metaphor.

This lesson examines a classic usul al-fiqh problem: if a general term is used (e.g., 'divorced women') and a subsequent pronoun (e.g., 'their husbands') applies to only a subset, does that specify the general? The passage presents three views: specification, non-specification, and the stop position. The author argues for the stop (waqf) position, which is preferred by many later Hanafi usulis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue and the Three Positions
Recognize the usul question: Does a pronoun that refers to some individuals of a general term constitute takhsis? Note the three positions: (1) specification, (2) non-specification, (3) waqf. Identify which scholars hold each view.
The majority of Hanafis and Shafi'is hold non-specification; the author champions waqf.
2
Examine the Quranic Example
Analyze the example from Q. 2:228: 'divorced women' (general) and 'their husbands' (pronoun). Understand that the pronoun refers only to revocably divorced women, but the general includes both revocably and irrevocably divorced.
The author also discusses the possibility of abrogation (naskh) affecting the interpretation.
3
Analyze the Specification Argument
Consider the view that the pronoun specifies the general: the pronoun indicates the intended meaning, so the general is restricted to the pronoun's reference. Note the scholars who hold this (Abu al-Husayn al-Mu'tazili, Imam al-Haramayn, etc.).
This view treats the pronoun as evidence for takhsis.
4
Analyze the Non-Specification Argument
Examine the view that the pronoun is metaphorical (majaz) and the general remains real (haqiqah). The majority argue that the pronoun's departure from the general does not necessitate specifying the general; rather, the pronoun is used metaphorically.
This view preserves the general's scope.
5
Understand the Waqf Position and Its Justification
Appreciate the author's preference for waqf: because both the general and the pronoun can be metaphorical (one of them must be metaphorical, but we cannot determine which), there is no preponderance. Therefore, we suspend judgment.
The author provides a detailed linguistic argument: if we specify the general, the pronoun is real but the general becomes metaphorical; if we keep the general real, the pronoun is metaphorical – both are equally possible.

Issue: The return of a pronoun to some individuals of the general is not a specifier according to the majority of Hanafis and Shafi'is. Al-Amidi chose an example: His saying (the Most High): 'And divorced women shall wait for three menstrual cycles' (Quran 2:228) along with His saying: 'And their husbands are more entitled to take them back' (Quran 2:228). The first verse includes both revocably and irrevocably divorced women, while the pronoun in the second is only for revocably divorced women. Abu al-Husayn al-Mu'tazili and Imam al-Haramayn said it is specification. It is said that most Hanafis, some Shafi'is, and some Mu'tazilis hold this, as in 'al-Taysir', and attributed to Imam al-Shafi'i as well. And he said in 'al-Tahrir': It is the most likely. And it was said: stop (waqf), and this is the chosen view in 'al-Mahsul'. Know that there is consideration in the example of the two verses, for the pronoun in the second refers to all divorced women, even if divorced thrice; and taking back was permissible in every divorce, then abrogated by the law of irrevocable divorce. The evidence is what Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and al-Bayhaqi narrated from Ibn Abbas about the verse up to His saying 'and their husbands are more entitled to take them back', that a man, if he divorced his wife, was more entitled to take her back even if he divorced her thrice; then that was abrogated by His saying: 'Divorce is twice, then retention with kindness or release with goodness' (Quran 2:229). Then on this basis, His saying 'and their husbands' etc. is partly abrogated; thus the right to take back remains beyond the abrogator. Abrogation is only regarding more than two and khul'. It follows that what is beyond them are returning divorced women, so not one is non-mali irrevocably. The husband's disposal is not considered without the Lawgiver's consideration. Thus, Imam al-Shafi'i's (may Allah have mercy on him) statement that kinayah (allusive divorce) is not irrevocable is established, unless it is said that khul' is legislated as irrevocable and it is only irrevocability with financial compensation, so by its coincident implication, it indicates the validity of irrevocability without compensation. So that verse was abrogated concerning single irrevocable divorce. But this is if allowing abrogation of wording by implication. Allah knows best His rulings. I say: And it (i.e., the stop) is the more similar to the truth, because the pronoun refers to the wording by virtue of its intended meaning, which is apparent. For if the general is specified and the pronoun refers to the remainder, the pronoun is used in its real sense, because it refers to the intended meaning of the general word, even if the general is metaphorical. And if it is not specified and refers to some, the pronoun becomes metaphorical while the general is real. So specification in the first does not necessitate specification in the second, because it remains real, i.e., referring to the intended meaning; similarly, specification in the second does not necessitate it in the first. Only one of the two metaphors is necessary without determination. So there is no preponderance for either, so stop is necessary. And what is said that the apparent (zahir) is stronger than the pronoun, so metaphor in the pronoun is easier, is countered by the fact that the pronoun is more specific (a'raf) because it indicates that it is it. So the two preponderances are equal, so stop is necessary. Reflect. And this is not sufficient, for being more specific does not entail less metaphor; rather, the apparent is stronger, and metaphor in it is slight compared to the pronoun, because mere mention of the antecedent implicitly and by estimation suffices for the pronoun, and fame may stand in place of mention. These are metaphors, so the pronoun is more deserving of metaphor, and the general remains on its generality. The majority said: The second (i.e., the pronoun) is metaphorical entirely because it is specified, and that does not entail metaphor in the first, so it remains on its generality. In it is that the pronoun's contradicting the antecedent is a cause for metaphor by agreement, because it is placed for the antecedent. So if it contradicts, it is metaphorical. However, contradiction can be conceived in two ways: one is that...
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage discusses a classic usul problem: If a general term is used and then a pronoun (e.g., 'their husbands') refers to only some individuals of that general term (e.g., revocably divorced women only), does that constitute specification of the general? The majority of Hanafis and Shafi'is say no; it is not a specifier. Others, like Abu al-Husayn al-Mu'tazili and Imam al-Haramayn, say it does specify. A third position is to refrain from a ruling (waqf), which is chosen by the author. He then engages in a detailed analysis of the Quranic example (Quran 2:228) and argues that the pronoun actually refers to all divorced women when revealed, but later abrogation changed the ruling. He concludes that the stop (waqf) is the more similar to the truth because of the mutual possibility of metaphor in the general or the pronoun. He then reports the majority's argument that the pronoun is metaphorical but the general remains real, and responds by noting that metaphor in the pronoun is more plausible.

Key Terms
ضمير (ḍamīr): A pronoun that refers back to an antecedent; in this context, it may refer to some individuals of a general term.
عام (ʿāmm): A general term that encompasses all individuals within its scope.
تخصيص (takhṣīṣ): Specification; restricting the application of a general term to some of its individuals.
مجاز (majāz): Metaphorical usage; using a word in a sense other than its original meaning.
حقيقة (ḥaqīqah): Literal or real meaning; the original meaning of a word.
وقف (waqf): The position of suspending judgment; refraining from declaring either specification or non-specification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the most appropriate ruling when a pronoun refers to some individuals of a general term?
A) The general is specified.
B) The general remains on its generality.
C) One should stop (waqf) and not rule either way.
D) The pronoun is interpreted metaphorically.

Key Takeaway
When a pronoun refers to some individuals of a general term, the Hanafi usul position is not to rush to specification; waqf is preferable because both the general and the pronoun can be metaphorical.

Return of Pronoun to Some Individuals of the General: Is It a Specifier?
Usul dispute on pronoun specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three positions on whether pronoun return to some individuals of a general term constitutes takhsis, and evaluate the arguments for each.

Core Idea
A pronoun returning to some of a general term does not necessarily specify the general—the majority view; but arguments lead to suspension.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut addresses a classic usul dispute: when a pronoun refers to part of what a general term covers, does that make the general term specific? The dispute involves Hanafis, Shafi'is, and Mu'tazilis. We will examine the arguments and the conclusion that suspension (tawaqquf) is most plausible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue
Recognize the core question: does a pronoun returning to only some individuals of an 'amm count as a mukhassis (specifier) for that 'amm?
The issue is whether the pronoun's limited reference forces a reinterpretation of the general term.
2
State the Three Positions
List: (1) Majority of Hanafis and Shafi'is: it is not a specifier. (2) Abu al-Husayn al-Mu'tazili and Imam al-Haramayn: it is a specifier. (3) Suspension (tawaqquf): no preference between the two.
The author cites al-Mahsul and al-Tahrir for the suspension view.
3
Analyze the Key Evidence
Examine the Quranic example (al-Baqarah 2:228) and the naskh discussion. The first verse is general for all divorced women; the pronoun in the second refers to revocable divorces. Determine whether this shows takhsis.
The author notes a potential problem: the example may be affected by abrogation, so it might not be a pure case.
4
Examine the Core Logical Argument
Understand the majority argument: the pronoun is metaphorical (majaz) when returning to some, but the general remains real (haqiqah). The opponents argue that pronoun requires unity with the antecedent, so specification of the general is needed.
The author counters that the only necessary consequence is metaphor in one of them, not specific takhsis of the general.
5
Evaluate the Author's Conclusion
The author finds the arguments equally strong, leading to suspension (tawaqquf). He critiques the objection that the apparent is stronger, showing that definiteness does not outweigh the frequency of metaphor in pronouns.
The suspension position is considered 'ashbah bi'l-haqq' (closest to truth).
