الضمير راجع عليه في الظاهر ففيه أن الضمير أعرف فإنه يفيد دلالة) أنه هو) فاستوى الترجيحان فوجب التوقف فتدبر) وهذا غير واف فإن الأعرفية لا توجب قلة التجوز، بل الظاهر أقوى يتجوز فيه قليلاً بالنسبة إلى المضمر فإنه يكفي فيه ذكر المرجع ضمناً وتقديراً، وقد تقام الشهرة مقام الذكر، وهذه تجوزات، فالضمير أحرى بالتجوز، ويبقى العام على عمومه الجمهور (قالوا الثاني) أي الضمير (مجاز) البتة (لأنه مخصوص ولا يلزم منه التجوز في الأوّل) فيبقى على عمومه (وفيه أن مخالفة الضمير للمرجع سبب للتجوز اتفاقاً لأنه موضوع بإزاء المرجع، فإذا خالف جاز عنه (لكن) المخالفة تتصور على وجهين: أحدهما: أن يراد به غير ما أريد بالمرجع) وإن كان مجازاً فيه وثانيهما أن يراد به غير ما وضع له المرجع وإن لم يكن) الموضوع له (مراداً وبناء كلامكم أيها المستدلون (على الثاني) أي على كون سبب التجوز المخالفة الثانية، فإن المجازية في الضمير لازم البتة على هذا التقدير، لأنه غير راجع إلى العموم الموضوع له المرجع والظاهر) هو (الأول) أي كون سبب التجوز مخالفة المراد، وعلى هذا لزوم المجازية فيه ممنوع، بل إذا خص العام يبقى الضمير حقيقة لرجوعه إلى المراد بالمرجع فتدبر، إمام الحرمين ومن تابعه قالوا) حقيقة الضمير تقتضي الاتحاد بينه وبين المرجع (فيلزم من خصوصه مع عموم المرجع المخالفة بينهما هذا خلف (أقول) في الجواب (اللازم) مما ذكروا مجازية أحدهما من العام أو الضمير لا على التعيين (لا تخصيص العام على الخصوص) لأن غاية ما لزم من المخالفة مجازية الضمير مع بقاء العام على الحقيقة، ومن التخصيص كونه حقيقة والعام مجازاً ولا أولوية فافهم (وأما الجواب كما في شرح المختصر بأنه) أي الضمير ( كإعادة الظاهر) ولا يلزم من التجوز في الثاني التجوز في الأول، ولا يعد هذا مخالفة، فكذا الضمير لا يعد مخالفاً، إذا رجع إلى البعض (فلا يخفى ما فيه لا لما في شرح الشرح من أنه يمنع ذلك أي كونه كإعادة الظاهر لأنه مقابلة المنع بالمنع، كذا في «الحاشية» (بل لما في شرح التخصيص من أن ظاهر الضمير إعادة) بعينه، فبرجوعه إلى البعض تلزم المخالفة قطعاً (دون الظاهر) فإنه ليس بإعادة فلا مخالفة فتدبر، ولك أن تجيب بأنا سلمنا المخالفة وغاية ما لزم منه مجازيته ولا عائبة لأن مجازية أحدهما متعين، والضمير يكثر فيه التجوز من الظاهر فيتحمل، ويبقى الظاهر على الحقيقة ولك أن تقرر كلام شارح المختصر بأن مقصوده أنه كإعادة الظاهر في أنه عين الأول ،حقيقة ولا يكون التجوز فيه قرينة التجوز في الأول فكذا الضمير فافهم.
Issue: The return of a pronoun to some individuals of a general term is not a specifier according to the majority of Hanafis and Shafi'is, and al-Amidi chose (like) His saying: 'Divorced women shall wait three menstrual periods...' with His saying: 'And their husbands have more right to take them back...' For the first verse includes both revocable and irrevocable divorces, and the pronoun in the second is only for revocable ones. Abu al-Husayn al-Mu'tazili and Imam al-Haramayn said it is a specification. It is said that this is the view of most Hanafis and some Shafi'is and some Mu'tazilis. Similarly in al-Taysir, and attributed to al-Shafi'i also. And it is said in al-Tahrir that it is the most appropriate, and it is said: suspension is the chosen view in al-Mahsul. Know that there is a problem with the example from the two verses: the pronoun in the second refers to all divorced women even if divorced three times, and taking back was permissible in every divorce then abrogated by the legislation of irrevocable divorce. The evidence is what Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and al-Bayhaqi narrated from Ibn Abbas: 'Divorced women shall wait three menstrual periods...' until His saying: 'And their husbands have more right to take them back...' That is because the man used to, when he divorced his wife, have more right to take her back even if he divorced her three times. Then that was abrogated by His saying: 'Divorce is twice; then retention in kindness or release with goodness.' Then accordingly His saying 'And their husbands...' is partially abrogated, so the right to take back remains beyond what is abrogated, and abrogation is only beyond two and khul', so the divorced women beyond them are taken back, so no single irrevocable divorce without compensation. The husband's action is not considered without the Lawgiver's consideration. So then the saying of al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) that kinayahs are not irrevocable is established, unless it is said that khul' is legislated as irrevocable and it is only irrevocability with financial compensation, so its congruent implication indicates the validity of irrevocability without compensation, so that verse is abrogated in the case of one irrevocable divorce. But this if abrogation of wording by implication is allowed. And Allah knows best His rulings. I say: it (suspension) is the most similar to truth because the pronoun refers to the wording based on its intended meaning, and that is apparent. For if the general is specified and the pronoun returns to the remainder, the pronoun is in its reality because it refers to the intended meaning of the general word, even if the general is metaphorical. And if it is not specified and refers to some, the pronoun becomes metaphorical and the general real. So specification in the first does not necessitate specification in the second because it remains real, which is reference to the intended meaning. And similarly the reverse, just as specification in the second does not necessitate it in the first, so one of the two metaphors is only necessary without specification. So there is no preference for one over the other, so suspension is necessary. And what is said that the apparent is stronger than the pronoun, and the metaphor in the pronoun returns upon the apparent, then in that the pronoun is more definite because it indicates 'it is it', so the two preferences are equal, so suspension is necessary. Ponder. But this is insufficient because definiteness does not cause less metaphor; rather the apparent is stronger and is used metaphorically only a little compared to the pronoun, because for the pronoun, mere implicit mention of the antecedent suffices, and notoriety may stand in place of mention, and these are metaphors. So the pronoun is more deserving of metaphor, and the general remains on its generality. The majority said the second (the pronoun) is metaphorical definitely because it is specified, and that does not necessitate metaphor in the first, so it remains on its generality. But in that, the opposition of the pronoun to the antecedent is a cause for metaphor unanimously because it is placed for the antecedent; when it opposes, it diverts from it. But opposition can be conceived in two ways: one is that it intends other than what the antecedent intended, even if metaphorical in it; the second is that it intends other than what the antecedent was placed for, even if that which it was placed for is not intended. And the construction of your argument, O inferrers, is on the second, i.e., that the cause of metaphor is the second opposition, so metaphor in the pronoun is definitely necessary on this estimation because it does not refer to the generality placed for the antecedent and the apparent is the first, i.e., the cause of metaphor is opposition of intention. On this, the necessity of metaphor in it is denied. Rather, if the general is specified, the pronoun remains real because it refers to what is intended by the antecedent. So ponder. Imam al-Haramayn and those who followed him said: the reality of the pronoun requires unity between it and the antecedent; so from its particularity with the generality of the antecedent, opposition between them follows, which is a contradiction. I say in reply: the necessary consequence of what they mentioned is metaphor in one of them, the general or the pronoun, without specification, not specification of the general in particular. Because the utmost that follows from opposition is metaphor in the pronoun with the general remaining real, and from specification it is real and the general metaphorical, and no priority. So understand. As for the answer as in Sharh al-Mukhtasar that it (the pronoun) is like repeating the apparent, and metaphor in the second does not necessitate metaphor in the first, and this is not considered opposition, so likewise the pronoun is not considered opposing when it refers to some. It is not hidden what is in it, not because of what is in Sharh al-Sharh that it prevents that, i.e., it being like repeating the apparent because it is a confrontation of denial with denial, as in al-Hashiyah. Rather because of what is in Sharh al-Takhsis that the apparent of the pronoun is repetition exactly, so by its return to some, opposition necessarily follows, unlike the apparent because it is not repetition, so no opposition. Ponder. And you may answer that we accept opposition, and the utmost that follows from it is its metaphor, and there is no blame because metaphor of one of them is specified, and the pronoun has much metaphor from the apparent so it can bear it, and the apparent remains on reality. And you may formulate the speech of the author of Sharh al-Mukhtasar as that his intent is that it is like repeating the apparent in that it is the same as the first in reality, and there is no metaphor in it as a qarinah for metaphor in the first, so likewise the pronoun. So understand.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul al-fiqh issue: does the return of a pronoun to some individuals of a general term constitute takhsis (specification) of that general term? The passage surveys three positions: 1) The majority of Hanafis and Shafi'is (the jumhur) hold that it does not specify; 2) Abu al-Husayn al-Mu'tazili and Imam al-Haramayn (and some attribute to al-Shafi'i and most Hanafis) hold that it does specify; 3) A third position of tawaqquf (suspension) is reported from al-Mahsul and considered the most appropriate by the author of al-Tahrir. The author, after a detailed analysis of the Quranic example (2:228) and discussions about naskh, concludes that tawaqquf is the most similar to truth (ashbah bi'l-haqq). The passage delves into arguments regarding whether the pronoun or the general term is more likely to be majaz (metaphorical). The jumhur argue that the pronoun must be majaz if it refers to some, but that does not affect the general. Opponents argue that the pronoun requires unity with the antecedent, so if the pronoun is particular, the general must be specified. The author counters that the necessary consequence is only that one of them is majaz, not that the general is specified specifically. He also critiques the argument that the pronoun is like repeating the apparent (i'ada al-zahir), showing that the pronoun actually implies exact repetition, so opposition is necessitated. The commentary by the author (from the text of Fawatih al-Rahmut) leans towards tawaqquf due to the equal weight of arguments.

Key Terms
ضمير (damir): اللفظ الدال على المذكور سابقاً بذاته أو بصفاته
عام (amm): اللفظ المستغرق لجميع أفراد ما يصلح له
مخصص (mukhassis): ما يخرج بعض أفراد العام عن الحكم
مجاز (majaz): استعمال اللفظ في غير ما وضع له لعلاقة مع قرينة مانعة من إرادة الحقيقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of the majority (al-jumhur) of Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the return of a pronoun to some individuals of a general term?
A) It is a specifier (mukhassis) for the general.
B) It is not a specifier; the general remains general.
C) It is definitely a specifier only for the pronoun part.
D) The matter requires suspension (tawaqquf).

Key Takeaway
The return of a pronoun to some individuals of a general term does not specify the general according to the majority; the strongest conclusion is suspension due to equal arguments.

The Pronoun After Specification: Literal or Metaphorical?
Resolving the status of a pronoun reverting to a specified general term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that a pronoun referring to a specified general term remains literal and evaluate the opposing argument of Imam al-Haramayn.

Core Idea
A pronoun after specification remains literal because it refers to the intended meaning, not the original generality.

This lesson tackles a subtle usul al-fiqh debate: when a general term (عام) is specified (مخصص) to a subset, how should we interpret a pronoun (ضمير) that refers back to that term? Is it literal (حقيقة) or metaphorical (مجاز)? The Hanafi position, championed by early masters, insists on literalness by focusing on the intended meaning (المراد). We will explore the reasoning, the objection from Imam al-Haramayn, and the Hanafi response, culminating in the preferred view that preserves the literal sense of the general text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Clearly state the issue: when a general term is specified to a part, what is the status of a pronoun that reverts to that term? Is it used literally or metaphorically?
This is a linguistic usul question with direct implications for legal interpretation.
2
State the Hanafi position and its basis
The Hanafi school holds that the pronoun remains literal because it refers to the intended meaning (المراد) of the referent, not its original comprehensive scope. The specification does not force metaphor.
The key is to distinguish between the original meaning (الموضوع له) and the intended meaning (المراد).
3
Present the opposing view of Imam al-Haramayn
Imam al-Haramayn argues that literalness requires identity (اتحاد) between pronoun and referent. Since the referent is general and the pronoun specific, a contradiction arises, necessitating metaphor.
This view prioritizes the formal requirement of unity over the intended reference.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The text responds that the dilemma forces metaphor in either the general or the pronoun, but there is no inherent preference. However, pronouns bear metaphor more easily than general terms, so it is better to keep the general literal.
This is a practical preference (ترجيح) based on linguistic tolerance, not a logical necessity.
5
Examine the critique of the repetition analogy
A counter-argument from Sharh al-Mukhtasar compares the pronoun to repeating the explicit noun (إعادة الظاهر), where metaphor in the second does not affect the first. The text critiques this because a pronoun inherently implies identity with its antecedent, unlike an explicit noun.
This shows the nuanced difference between pronouns and explicit repetitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقالة الثالثة في المبادىء اللغوية يراد به غير ما أريد بالمرجع) وإن كان مجازاً فيه وثانيهما أن يراد به غير ما وضع له المرجع وإن لم يكن) الموضوع له (مراداً وبناء كلامكم أيها المستدلون (على الثاني) أي على كون سبب التجوز المخالفة الثانية، فإن المجازية في الضمير لازم البتة على هذا التقدير، لأنه غير راجع إلى العموم الموضوع له المرجع والظاهر) هو (الأول) أي كون سبب التجوز مخالفة المراد، وعلى هذا لزوم المجازية فيه ممنوع، بل إذا خص العام يبقى الضمير حقيقة لرجوعه إلى المراد بالمرجع فتدبر، إمام الحرمين ومن تابعه قالوا) حقيقة الضمير تقتضي الاتحاد بينه وبين المرجع (فيلزم من خصوصه مع عموم المرجع المخالفة بينهما هذا خلف (أقول) في الجواب (اللازم) مما ذكروا مجازية أحدهما من العام أو الضمير لا على التعيين (لا تخصيص العام على الخصوص) لأن غاية ما لزم من المخالفة مجازية الضمير مع بقاء العام على الحقيقة، ومن التخصيص كونه حقيقة والعام مجازاً ولا أولوية فافهم (وأما الجواب كما في شرح المختصر بأنه) أي الضمير ( كإعادة الظاهر) ولا يلزم من التجوز في الثاني التجوز في الأول، ولا يعد هذا مخالفة، فكذا الضمير لا يعد مخالفاً، إذا رجع إلى البعض (فلا يخفى ما فيه لا لما في شرح الشرح من أنه يمنع ذلك أي كونه كإعادة الظاهر لأنه مقابلة المنع بالمنع، كذا في «الحاشية» (بل لما في شرح التخصيص من أن ظاهر الضمير إعادة) بعينه، فبرجوعه إلى البعض تلزم المخالفة قطعاً (دون الظاهر) فإنه ليس بإعادة فلا مخالفة فتدبر، ولك أن تجيب بأنا سلمنا المخالفة وغاية ما لزم منه مجازيته ولا عائبة لأن مجازية أحدهما متعين، والضمير يكثر فيه التجوز من الظاهر فيتحمل، ويبقى الظاهر على الحقيقة ولك أن تقرر كلام شارح المختصر بأن مقصوده أنه كإعادة الظاهر في أنه عين الأول ،حقيقة ولا يكون التجوز فيه قرينة للتجوز في الأول فكذا الضمير فافهم.
The third article on linguistic principles: It is intended by it other than what was intended by the referent, even if it is metaphorical in it. Secondly, that it is intended by it other than what the referent was placed for, even if the thing placed for is not intended. And your statement, O you who adduce evidence, is based on the second, i.e., that the cause of metaphor is the second discrepancy. Then metaphorical usage in the pronoun is necessarily required on this estimation, because it does not refer to the generality for which the referent was placed. But the apparent view is the first, i.e., that the cause of metaphor is discrepancy in the intended meaning. On this, the necessity of metaphor in it is denied. Rather, when the general is specified, the pronoun remains literal because of its reference to what is intended by the referent, so reflect. Imam al-Haramayn and those who followed him said: The literal meaning of the pronoun requires unity between it and the referent, so its specificity with generality of the referent entails discrepancy between them; this is a contradiction. I say in response: The necessary consequence from what they mentioned is metaphorical usage of one of them, the general or the pronoun, not specifically determined, not specification of the general to the specific. Because the utmost entailed by the discrepancy is metaphorical usage of the pronoun while the general remains literal, and from specification it would be literal and the general metaphorical, and there is no preference, so understand. As for the answer as in Sharh al-Mukhtasar, that the pronoun is like repeating the explicit noun, and metaphorical usage in the second does not entail metaphorical usage in the first, nor is this considered a discrepancy, so too the pronoun is not considered discrepant when it refers to a part. It is not hidden what is in it, not because of what is in Sharh al-Sharh that it prevents that, i.e., its being like repeating the explicit noun, because it is answering prevention with prevention as in al-Hashiya, but because of what is in Sharh al-Takhsis that the apparent meaning of the pronoun is a repetition itself, so by its reference to a part discrepancy necessarily follows, unlike the explicit noun, for it is not a repetition so no discrepancy, so reflect. And you may answer: we acknowledge the discrepancy, and the utmost it entails is its metaphoricity, and it is no defect because metaphoricity of one of them is determined, and the pronoun frequently admits metaphor more than the explicit noun, so it bears it, and the explicit noun remains literal. And you may formulate the statement of the commentator of al-Mukhtasar that his intent is that it is like repeating the explicit noun in that it is identical to the first in truth, and metaphor in it is not a قرينة (indication) for metaphor in the first, so too the pronoun, so understand.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage delves into a nuanced usul dispute about the status of a pronoun (ضمير) that refers back to a general term (عام) which has been partially specified (مخصوص). The core issue: after specification, does the pronoun, used for a part of the general term, remain literal (حقيقة) or become metaphorical (مجاز)? The Hanafi position, as presented, argues that the pronoun remains literal because it refers to the intended meaning of the referent (المراد بالمرجع), not the original comprehensive scope. The opposing view, attributed to Imam al-Haramayn, holds that the pronoun's literalness requires identity with the referent; since the referent is general and the pronoun is specific, a conflict arises, necessitating metaphor. The author responds by noting that the dilemma forces metaphor in either the general or the pronoun, but there is no preference. He then examines a counter-argument from Sharh al-Mukhtasar, which compares the pronoun to repeating the explicit noun (إعادة الظاهر) — the explicit noun can be used figuratively without affecting its original literal use, so the pronoun similarly does not become metaphorical when referring to a part. This is critiqued because a pronoun inherently implies identity with its antecedent in a way that an explicit noun does not. Ultimately, the Hanafi view prevails by emphasizing that metaphors are more tolerable in pronouns than in general terms, so it is better to keep the general literal and allow the pronoun to be metaphorical if necessary. The discussion highlights the Hanafi tendency to preserve the literal meaning of general texts (عموم) whenever possible.

Key Terms
الضمير (al-damir): A pronoun that refers back to a preceding word (المرجع).
المرجع (al-marja'): The antecedent or referent to which the pronoun is supposed to return.
التخصيص (al-takhsis): The specification of a general term to a part of its possible referents.
المجاز (al-majaz): Metaphorical or figurative usage, i.e., using a word in a sense other than its original placement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position explained in this passage, a pronoun (ضمير) that reverts to a part of a specified general term is:
A) Always metaphorical
B) Always literal because it refers to the intended meaning of the referent
C) Considered an explicit repetition of the noun
D) Neither literal nor metaphorical, but suspended

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a pronoun after specification is literal because it refers to the intended meaning, preserving the literal interpretation of the general text.

Specifying the General by Qiyas: The Hanafi Position
Detailed dispute on whether qiyas can specify an ‘amm text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on specification of a general by qiyas and evaluate the different scholarly positions.

Core Idea
Qiyas can specify a partially specified general because such a general is weaker than qiyas.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut is a rigorous exploration of a key usul al-fiqh dispute: can qiyas (analogy) specify a general text? The Hanafi school holds a nuanced position: qiyas can specify a general that has already been partially specified, but not an unspecified one. We will unpack this, contrast it with other schools, and analyze the proofs and counterarguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the Hanafi position
The core issue: Can qiyas specify a general text when they conflict? State the Hanafi position clearly: yes, but only if the general is already partially specified (makhsus al-ba'd).
This distinction is crucial.
2
Contrast with other schools
List the positions of Ibn Sharih, Ibn al-Hajib, al-Jubba'i, al-Qadi, Imam al-Haramayn, and al-Ghazali. Understand what conditions they impose or reject.
Note the range from absolute preference of the general to conditional acceptance.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof: A partially specified general depends on a contingent specifier, making it weaker. Qiyas does not require prior search for a specifier, so it is stronger. Hence the stronger (qiyas) should take precedence.
This is based on the relative strength of evidence.
4
Examine the key objection and response
Objection: Qiyas involves many conjectural elements, so it is weaker than a general text. The Hanafi response: The specified general is actually weaker, and specification is combination, not invalidation. Also, examples like khabar wahid specifying the Qur'an show that weaker proofs can specify.
The counterexample is debated: some say both are conjectural.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: In practice, a Hanafi jurist can use qiyas to narrow a partially specified general, while a Shafi'i may restrict this to evident qiyas or deny it altogether.
This affects real istinbat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما نحن فيه، وبهذا يندفع ما قيل أن عمل الصحابي خلاف العام، إنما يكون مخصصاً لكون حجته مخصصة، ويحتمل أن يكون حجته القياس، فثبت تخصيص القياس ابتداء، وجه الدفع أن عدالة الصحابي مرشدة إلى أنه لا يرتكب العمل بخلاف النص القاطع إلا بعد قطعية التخصيص بقرينة حالية أو مقالية لا بقياسه ورأيه فتدبر، ثم ههنا إشكال آخر هو أن هذا إنما يتم إذا كان النص الأصل مقارناً للعام على رأينا وهو غير لازم بل يجوز تخصيص المخصوص البعض ثانياً من غير ملاحظة مقارنته الأصل العام، والجواب أن هناك عمل بأرجح الدليلين عند المعارضة، فإن القياس أرجح في الدلالة من العام المخصوص كما تقدم وقد عارضه فيعمل به ويترك العام بقدره، وهو المعنى من التخصيص لا أن هذا القياس أو أصله قرينة على أن المراد به البعض وكيف يصلح قرينة ما لا يعلم وجوده عند الخطاب فتدبر (وقال ابن شريح) من الشافعية (إن كان القياس (جلياً) يخصص، وإلا لا (وقيل: إن كان أصله مخرجاً من ذلك العموم) جاز تخصيصه وإلا لا (وقيل) يخصص (إن كان أصله مخصصاً) للعام (أو ثبت العلة بنص من الكتاب أو السنة (أو إجماع أو ظهر قرينة جزئية) على ترجيح القياس (وإلا) يكن شيء من هذه الأشياء فالعمل بعموم الخبر ) واجب واختاره ابن الحاجب) من المالكية (والجبائي) من المعتزلة (يقدم العام مطلقاً سواء كان مخصوصاً من قبل أو لا، ولا يرى صحة تعليل المخصص أيضاً والقاضي والإمام (توقفا في العمل إلى أن المعارضة والكلام فيه فإنه لا تعادل والتعارض فرعه ولهذا يقدم الترجيح على الجمع التعارض فتدبر، والحق أن يقال دلالة القياس ،راجحة، أما عندنا فلأن الكلام في مخصوص البعض، وقد تقدم أن دلالته أضعف من القياس وغير المخصوص لا يجوز تخصيصه أصلاً، وأما عند غيرنا فلأن العمل به قبل البحث عن المخصص لا يجوز عندهم بخلاف القياس فإن العمل به لا يتوقف على البحث بالمعارض، فهو أقوى من العام فافهم، هكذا ينبغي أن يفهم هذا المقام (فاندفع ما قيل في رد تخصيص غير منصوص العلة العلة المستنبطة إما راجحة) على العام أو مساوية) له (أو مرجوحة) عنه (فالتخصيص على احتمال هو راجحية العلة (دون احتمالين آخرين والواحد) نصف (الاثنين والراجح الأغلب فالراجح العدم) للتخصيص لكونه على احتمالين وجه الاندفاع أنا لا نسلم أن التخصيص على احتمال واحد، فإن رجحان أن يكون على احتمال المساواة أيضاً، بل على المرجوحية أيضاً، ويرد عليه ما مر من أن تجويز تخصيص الأقوى بالأضعف مكابرة، ورجحان الجمع إنما هو عند التعادل، فالحق في الجواب ما قد مر أن القياس راجح على العام المخصوص عندنا، وعلى العام مطلقاً عند غيرنا فتدبر (على أنه يوجب بطلان التخصيص :(أقول : وأيضاً الاعتبار في الأغلبية (الغلبة (الأفراد فما يكون أفراده أغلب فهو أرجح (لا لغلبة الاحتمال (والثاني أي غلبة الاحتمال (لا يستلزم الأول أي غلبة الأفراد كالإمكان مع الوجوب والامتناع فإن أفراد مخرجاً (نزلت منزلة نص خاص معارض للعام (فيخصص بها للجمع بينهما، وكذا إذا كانت قرينة مرجحة للقياس، لأن العمل بالراجح واجب، وهذا لا يرد في التخصيص ابتداء على رأينا، لأنه وإن كان بمنزلة نص خاص لكنه بمنزلة سديد، لأن عدم الظفر بالدليل لا يدل على عدمه في الواقع ولا على عدم المدلول فيه (أقول : على أن الجمع) بين الدليلين حين التعارض (هو الدليل مطلقاً سواء كان كذلك أم لم يكن (فإن القياس دليل مطلقاً سواء كان علته مستنبطة أو منصوصة، فيجب الجمع بينه وبين العام، وقد تقدم ما فيه رداً وأحكاماً واحتج الجبائي أولاً بأن القياس أضعف من الخبر لأن القياس يتوقف على أمور كثيرة من حكم الأصل، وعلته ووجودها في الفرع وخلوها عن المعارض والكل مظنونة فيها شبهة بخلاف الخبر، فإن الظن فيه في شيئين السند والدلالة (فلو خص به) الخبر (لزم إبطال الأقوى بالأضعف) وهو خلاف المعقول (والجواب أن كلاً من المقدمتين) من ضعف القياس، ولزوم إبطال الأقوى بالأضعف (ممنوع) أما الأول فلما سيجيء في السنة إن شاء الله تعالى، كيف وقد بينا سابقاً أن ضعف العام المخصوص لأجل توقف إفادته على حكم المخصص المقارن لتعليله المورث للشبهة فهو أضعف من فتعادلا، وإن ادعى القوة
Regarding our discussion: this refutes what was said that the action of a Companion contrary to a general text is a specification because his evidence is specific, and it is possible that his evidence is qiyas, so specification by qiyas is established initially. The refutation is that the Companion's justice guides that he does not commit an action contrary to a definitive text except after the definitiveness of specification by a contextual or verbal clue, not by his qiyas and opinion. Then there is another problem: this only works if the original text is concurrent with the general text in our view, but it is not necessary; rather it is permissible to specify a partially specified [general] a second time without regard to its comparison to the original general text. The answer is that there is acting on the preponderant of the two proofs at the time of conflict, for qiyas is stronger in evidence than a partially specified general as previously stated, and it conflicts, so it is acted upon and the general is left to its extent. This is the meaning of specification, not that this qiyas or its original is a context clue that only part is intended, and how can something unknown at the time of speech be a context clue? So reflect. (Ibn Sharih) of the Shafi'is said: if the qiyas is (evident) it specifies, otherwise no. (It was said: if its original is derived from that general) its specification is permissible, otherwise no. (It was said: it specifies) (if its original is specified) for the general (or the cause is established by a text from the Book or Sunnah, or consensus, or a partial indication appears) for preponderance of qiyas (otherwise) if there is none of these, then acting on the general of the hadith is (obligatory). Ibn al-Hajib of the Malikis (chose this). (Al-Jubba'i) of the Mu'tazila says: (the general is preferred absolutely, whether it has been previously specified or not, and he does not consider the validity of the explanation of the specifier. (Al-Qadi and Imam) (suspended judgment until preponderance appears). (Imam Hujjat al-Islam al-Ghazali) takes the preponderant of the two conjectures: if preponderance is in the qiyas, he specifies by it; if in the general, he leaves it; if they are equal, then suspension. (We are bound) because the shared conjectural nature is established, and (the variance) in conjecture in strength and weakness is not an impediment to specification. (Preponderance: combining the two proofs is better than ignoring; specification even if weak is preponderated because it entails combination as previously in specification by implication). Therein is an indication to refute what might be imagined that the general, though conjectural, yields a higher conjecture than qiyas. Then this refutation is nothing, for preference of the strong over the weak is a firmly established and self-evident principle, perhaps agreed upon. As for the preponderance of combination, it does not give strength to specification, for after the establishment of conflict, the discussion is about it; there is no equivalence and conflict is its branch, hence preponderance is given priority over combination in conflict. So reflect. (The truth is to say: evidence of qiyas is preponderant. As for us, because we are discussing a partially specified general, and its evidence has been stated to be weaker than qiyas; an unspecified [general] cannot be specified at all. As for others, because acting on it [the general] before searching for a specifier is not permissible in their view, unlike qiyas, for acting on it does not depend on searching for a conflicting evidence, so it is stronger than the general. Understand, thus this station should be understood.) (Thus what was said in refutation of specifying [by qiyas with] non-textual cause is refuted: the inferred cause is either preponderant) over the general, or (equal) to it, (or weaker) than it. (So specification is on one probability: the preponderance of the cause) (without the other two probabilities, and one is) half (of two, and the preponderant is the majority, so the preponderant is non-existence) of specification because it is on two probabilities. The refutation: we do not concede that specification is on one probability, for preponderance can also be on equality, even on inferiority. It is also refuted by what passed that allowing specification of the strong by the weak is absurd, and preponderance of combination is only at equivalence. So the truth in the answer is what passed: qiyas is preponderant over the specified general according to us, and over the general absolutely according to others. So reflect. (Moreover, this requires nullification of specification absolutely, whether by qiyas, text, or other indication, because specification for every specifier is either preponderant, equal, or weak, etc. It is not far to say: probability does not conflict with certainty, for specification exists contrary to specification by qiyas with inferred cause. So consider.) (I say: also consideration is in majority) (of individuals, so what has more individuals is more preponderant) (not by preponderance of probability. (The second, i.e., preponderance of probability) (does not entail the first, i.e., majority of individuals, like possibility with obligation and impossibility; indeed individuals of the first are more than the latter two, despite them being probabilities. So it is possible that individuals of the preponderant cause are more, and preponderance is for specification. Understand.) (Ibn al-Hajib argued that qiyas, if it is such – i.e., with textual cause, or agreed upon, or its original is derived – (descends to the status of a specific text opposing the general), so specification is by it to combine them. Likewise if there is an indication preponderating the qiyas, because acting on the preponderant is obligatory. This does not apply to initial specification according to us, because though it is like a specific text, it is like conjectural evidence, while the general is definitive, so qiyas vanishes in its presence. Understand. It is not hidden that this does not indicate non-specification by other qiyas. (He argued that by the absence of evidence for permissibility of specification) by others, and whatever lacks evidence must be negated. (It is unsound, because failure to find evidence does not indicate its non-existence in reality, nor the non-existence of its signification.) (I say: combination) between two proofs at conflict (is the proof absolutely, whether it is like that or not). (Indeed qiyas is a proof absolutely, whether its cause is inferred or textual, so combination between it and the general is obligatory, and what passed contains refutations and rulings.) (Al-Jubba'i argued first that qiyas is weaker than hadith because qiyas depends on many matters: the ruling of the original, its cause, its existence in the branch, and its freedom from counter-evidence – all are conjectural with doubt – unlike hadith, for the conjecture in it is in two things: the chain and the evidence. (So if the hadith is specified by it, it would necessitate invalidating the strong by the weak), which is contrary to reason. (The answer: both premises) – weakness of qiyas and the necessity of invalidating the strong by the weak – (are denied). As for the first, as will come in the discussion of Sunnah, God willing. Moreover, we have previously shown that the weakness of the specified general is due to its dependence on the ruling of the specifier concurrent with it, its explanation causing doubt, so it is weaker than the ruling established by explanation, and the unspecified [general] is definitely stronger, no doubt, and cannot be specified by it. As for others, it is not acted upon except after searching for a specifier, unlike qiyas. So reflect. As for the second: specification is not invalidation but combination. If invalidation is meant generally, then it is prevented from being invalid. Therein it is said that this is meant and the denial is absurd, because to bring about the strong by the weak is contrary to reason, and combination is only if conflict is established, and the weak does not conflict with the strong. So reflect. (And) the (third) answer – he said third because the first resolves into two answers – (is invalidated by specification of khabar wahid to the Qur'an, for it is stronger than it, and) specification (of the concept by the expressed text. As for the invalidation by specification of khabar wahid, it is not valid, because khabar is conjectural in establishment and the general of the Qur'an is conjectural in evidence, so they are balanced, even if strength is claimed.)
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut is a detailed discussion of a core usul issue: whether qiyas (analogy) can specify a general text ('amm) when they appear to conflict. The author is expanding on the matn of Musallam al-Thubut. The discussion is structured around multiple scholarly positions and the Hanafi response.

The author begins by recapping a previously settled point: the action of a Companion contrary to a general text is not automatically taken as specification by qiyas, because the Companion's justice ensures they only act against a definitive text if there is a clear contextual or verbal clue, not by mere analogy. Then a new problem is raised: if the original text that the qiyas relies on is not concurrent with the general text, how can specification occur? The answer is that when proofs conflict, we act on the preponderant; and qiyas is stronger in evidence than a partially specified general ('amm makhsus al-ba'd). The author emphasizes that this is not because qiyas serves as a contextual clue, but because it outweighs the general in strength.

Next, the author lists various views from other schools and scholars:
- Ibn Sharih (Shafi'i): Only 'jali' (evident) qiyas specifies.
- Some: Only if the original of the qiyas is derived from that general text.
- Some: Specifies if its original is itself specified, or if the cause is textually proven, or if there is a specific indication for preponderance.
- Ibn al-Hajib (Maliki) and al-Jubba'i (Mu'tazili): The general is always preferred, regardless of prior specification.
- Al-Qadi and Imam al-Haramayn: Suspend judgment until preponderance is evident.
- Al-Ghazali: Take the preponderant; if equal, suspend.

The author then presents the Hanafi position (al-haqq an yuqal): Qiyas is preponderant. For Hanafis, this applies only to a general that has already been partially specified (makhsus al-ba'd), because such a general is weaker than qiyas. An unspecified general cannot be specified by qiyas at all. For other schools (like Shafi'is), qiyas is also preponderant because they do not act on a general before searching for a specifier, whereas they do act on qiyas without such search.

The passage then refutes an objection: if a qiyas with an inferred cause is one of three possibilities (preponderant, equal, weak), then specification is only one probability, making it unlikely. The refutation is that specification can also be on equality or even weakness, and that preponderance of combination only applies when proofs are equal, whereas here qiyas is stronger. So the correct answer is the one already given: qiyas is preponderant over the specified general (according to us) and over the general absolutely (according to others).

The author then addresses a possible objection that this argument would lead to the nullification of all specification (whether by text or other means) because every specifier can be categorized as preponderant, equal, or weak. The response is that probability (al-mazanna) does not conflict with certainty (al-mi'anna), and the existence of actual specification is different from specification by qiyas with inferred cause.

In a section marked 'Aqulu' (I say), the author adds that the real consideration is the majority of instances (ghalabat al-afrad), not the majority of probability. A cause that applies to more individuals is more preponderant, and this can support specification.

Ibn al-Hajib's argument is then examined: qiyas with textual cause or consensus descends to the status of a specific text opposing the general, so it can specify to combine them. The author notes that this does not apply to initial specification (takhsis ibtida') because the general is definitive while qiyas is conjectural, so qiyas vanishes. However, this does not prove that other qiyas cannot specify.

The passage concludes with al-Jubba'i's argument that qiyas is weaker than hadith because it involves many conjectural elements. The Hanafi response: (1) the premises are denied; the specified general is actually weaker due to its reliance on a specifier; (2) specification is not invalidation but combination; (3) the argument is undermined by the fact that khabar wahid (single-narrator report) can specify the Qur'an, and that a concept can specify an explicit statement, both of which involve a weaker proof specifying a stronger one. However, the author notes this counterexample is not valid because khabar wahid and the general of the Qur'an are both conjectural in different ways and thus balanced.

Throughout, the author maintains the Hanafi position that while qiyas cannot specify an unspecified general, it can specify one that has been partially specified, and this is based on the relative strength of evidence.

Key Terms
تخصيص (takhsis): The act of limiting a general statement to some of its individuals by a separate evidence.
عام مخصوص (‘amm makhsus): A general text that has been partially specified, leaving some of its individuals operative.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a shared cause.
علة (‘illa): The operative cause that justifies a legal ruling and provides the basis for qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position as detailed in this passage, which of the following statements is true regarding specification by qiyas?
A) Qiyas can specify any general text, regardless of whether it has been previously specified.
B) Qiyas can specify a general text only if the cause is textual or agreed upon.
C) Qiyas can specify a general text only if the general has been partially specified before (makhsus al-ba'd).
D) Qiyas can never specify a general text because the general is always stronger.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a partially specified general ('amm makhsus) is weaker than qiyas, allowing further specification by qiyas, while an unspecified general remains stronger and cannot be overridden.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
Can Qiyas Specify a General Text? The Hanafi Position on Takhsis al-Amm bi al-Qiyas
Dispute on whether qiyas can specify general texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on takhsis al-amm bi al-qiyas and evaluate the arguments of the opponents, particularly those of Ibn al-Hajib and al-Jubba'i.

Core Idea
A strong qiyas can specify a weak general text, but not a definitive one.

In this lesson we delve into a classic usul dispute: whether analogical reasoning (qiyas) can restrict the scope of a general textual command. The Hanafi school carves out a nuanced position: while a general text before any specification is definitive and cannot be overridden by qiyas, once it has been specified (becoming 'amm makhsus), it loses its strength, and a strong qiyas—one with a textually stated cause or clear contextual support—can then further specify it. We will follow the arguments of the opponents and the Hanafi responses as presented in Fawatih al-Rahamut.

Guided Path
1
State the precise Hanafi position
What is the ruling on takhsis by qiyas? When is it allowed and when not? The key is the strength of the general text: if the general is still definitive (qat'i), qiyas cannot specify; if it is already weakened (by a previous specifier), a strong qiyas may specify.
2
Examine Ibn al-Hajib's argument
He argues that qiyas with a textually stated cause is like a specific text, so it should specify the general. The Hanafi author responds that such qiyas is still speculative (zanni al-dalalah) while the general before any specification is definitive (qat'i), so it cannot specify initially.
3
Analyze al-Jubba'i's first argument
He claims qiyas is weaker than khabar because qiyas involves many speculative elements. The Hanafi response: the specified general (amm makhsus) is even weaker than qiyas due to its dependence on a specifier, so using qiyas to specify it does not violate any principle.
4
Analyze al-Jubba'i's second argument
He cites the hadith of Mu'adh to show that khabar is prioritized over qiyas. The Hanafi response: the hadith only establishes a hierarchy of sources (Book, then Sunnah, then ra'y); it does not forbid specification by qiyas. Moreover, the Sunnah can specify the Book, so specification by qiyas is not inherently prohibited.
5
Analyze al-Jubba'i's third argument
He argues that qiyas is proven by ijma', but there is no ijma' when qiyas opposes a general text because there is ikhtilaf. The Hanafi response: ijma' is not the only proof for qiyas; qiyas is established by other evidences. Even if ijma' were the only proof, the disagreement is about application, not the validity of qiyas itself.

التخصيص مطلقاً سواء كان بالقياس أو النص أو قرينة أخرى، لأن التخصيص لكل مخصص، إما راجح أو مساو أم مرجوح الخ. ولا يبعد أن يقال المظنة لا تعارض المئنة فإن التخصيص واقع بخلاف التخصيص بالقياس المستنبط العلة فتأمل :(أقول : وأيضاً الاعتبار في الأغلبية (الغلبة (الأفراد فما يكون أفراده أغلب فهو أرجح (لا لغلبة الاحتمال (والثاني أي غلبة الاحتمال (لا يستلزم الأول أي غلبة الأفراد كالإمكان مع الوجوب والامتناع فإن أفراد الأول أكثر من الأخيرين مع كونهما احتمالين، فيجوز أن يكون أفراد العلة الراجحة أكثر ويكون الترجيح للتخصيص فافهم ، وتمسك ابن الحاجب بأن القياسات إذا كانت كذلك أي منصوص العلة أو مجمعاً دليل مطلقاً سواء كان علته مستنبطة أو منصوصة، فيجب الجمع بينه وبين العام، وقد تقدم ما فيه رداً وأحكاماً واحتج الجبائي أولاً بأن القياس أضعف من الخبر لأن القياس يتوقف على أمور كثيرة من حكم الأصل، وعلته ووجودها في الفرع وخلوها عن المعارض والكل مظنونة فيها شبهة بخلاف الخبر، فإن الظن فيه في شيئين السند والدلالة (فلو خص به) الخبر (لزم إبطال الأقوى بالأضعف) وهو خلاف المعقول (والجواب أن كلاً من المقدمتين) من ضعف القياس، ولزوم إبطال الأقوى بالأضعف (ممنوع) أما الأول فلما سيجيء في السنة إن شاء الله تعالى، كيف وقد بينا سابقاً أن ضعف العام المخصوص لأجل توقف إفادته على حكم المخصص المقارن لتعليله المورث للشبهة فهو أضعف من الحكم الثابت بالتعليل وغير المخصوص أقوى البتة لا شك فيه ولا يجوز تخصيصه ،به وأما عند غيرنا فهو لا يعمل به إلا بعد البحث عن المخصص، بخلاف القياس فتأمل، وأما الثاني : فلأن التخصيص ليس إبطالاً بل جمعاً، وإن أريد بالإبطال ما يعمه فيمنع بطلانه، وفيه أنه أريد هذا والمنع مكابرة، لأن تغير الأقوى بالأضعف خلاف المعقول، والجمع ليس إلا إذا ثبت التعارض والأضعف لا يعارض الأقوى فتدبر (و) الجواب (ثالثاً) وإنما قال ثالثاً لأن الأول منحل إلى جوابين (منقوض بتخصيص خبر الواحد للكتاب فإنه أقوى منه (و) تخصيص (المفهوم للمنطوق أما النقض بتخصيص خبر الواحد فغير وارد، لأن الخبر ظني الثبوت وعام الكتاب ظني الدلالة فتعادلا، وإن ادعى القوة
 في ظن عام الكتاب على خاص الخبر فلا بد من البيان، وأما النقض بالمفهوم فوارد، وقد مر العذر فتذكر (و) احتج الجبائي (ثانياً بحديث (معاذ وهو ما روى أحمد وأبو داود والترمذي عنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لما بعثه إلى اليمن قاضياً قال له : «كيف تقضي إذا لك أمر فقال أقضي بما في كتاب الله ، فقال : فإن لم يكن في كتاب الله؟ قال : فبسنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ، قال : فإن لم يكن في سنة رسول الله؟ قال : اجتهد برأيي ولا آلو قال فضرب في صدري فقال : الحمد لله الذي وفق رسول رسول الله لما يرضى به رسول الله» (وهو) حديث (صحيح) وفي التيسير قال الترمذي غريب، وإسناده عندي ليس بمتصل، قال البخاري لا يصح لكن شهرته وتلقي الأمة له بالقبول لا يقعده عن الحجية ووثقه الباقلاني والطبري، وأشار إلى وجه الاستدلال بقوله: (فإنه قدم الخبر على القياس وصوبه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، والجواب أخر السنة عن الكتاب مع جواز تخصيصها له بالاتفاق) فالحجة منقوضة به وأيضاً : لا يدل على امتناع التخصيص به عند التعارض فإنه إذا جوز التخصيص به فلم يوجد في الحكم في السنة عند وجود القياس المخصص المعارض (و) احتج الجبائي (ثالثاً : دليل القياس إنما هو الإجماع ولا إجماع عند المخالفة أي عند مخالفة القياس عام الكتاب أو السنة (للمخالفة) أي لوجود خلاف الأئمة فيما بينهم وإذا انتفى الإجماع انتفى دليل حجية القياس فلا يصح معارضاً للعام فلا يخصص (والجواب) لا نسلم أن دليل القياس الإجماع فقط، بل قد ثبت بغيره) أي بغير الإجماع كما سيلوح لك في القياس (وإذا ثبت به أي لو سلم ثبوته به ثبتت أحكامه ضرورة، ومنها الجمع) عند التعارض فالخلاف فيه (كأنه خلاف الإجماع لأن الإجماع على الملزوم إجماع على اللازم، والخلاف في اللازم خلاف في الملزوم. هذا إنما يتم لو سلم الخصم التعارض بين القياس والخبر العام حتى يكون الجمع يرجعان إلى النص، وهو حكمي على الواحد حكمي على الجماعة فالتخصيص) بالقياس (إنما هو به، وإذا ترجح ظن التخصيص بقرينة المقام يجب العمل به للإجماع على اتباع الراجح) وصار التخصيص راجحاً وفيه أن الرجوع إلى ذلك النص جارٍ في جميع الأقيسة) فإن العلة المشتركة موجودة في كل قياس فيتناوله النص، ويلزم أن يجوز التخصيص بكل قياس (وهو خلاف مذهبه فإنه لا يجوز بالمستنبط إلا إذا أعانته قرينة جزئية إلا أن يقال : إن The Third Article on Linguistic Principles. It has passed that permitting the specification of the stronger by the weaker is obstinacy, and preference of combination is only when equal. So the truth in the answer is what has passed: that qiyas is preponderant over the specified general according to us, and over the general absolutely according to others, so ponder. (That it necessitates the invalidity of specification absolutely, whether by qiyas or text or other contextual clue, because specification for every specifier is either preponderant, equal, or weaker... And it is not unlikely that it is said: the indicative circumstance does not contradict the certain occurrence, for specification is actual unlike specification by qiyas that derives the cause, so reflect. I say: Also consideration is in majority of individuals, so what has more individuals is more preponderant, not due to probability dominance. The second (probability dominance) does not entail the first (dominance of individuals), like possibility with obligation and impossibility, for individuals of the first are more than the latter two even though they are probabilities. So it is possible that individuals of the preponderant cause are more, and preference is for specification, so understand. And Ibn al-Hajib argued that if analogies are like that, i.e., with a textually stated cause or consensus upon it, or its original is derived, they are treated as a specific text opposing the general, so they specify it for combination, and similarly if there is a contextual clue preponderating the analogy, because acting upon the preponderant is obligatory. This does not apply to initial specification in our view, because although it is like a specific text, it is like a speculative text while the general is definitive, so the analogy collapses in its face, so understand. And it is not hidden that it does not prove lack of specification by other analogies. He attributed that to lack of evidence for permissibility of specification by others, and whatever lacks evidence must be negated. This is not sound, because lack of evidence does not prove non-existence in reality nor non-existence of the meaning. I say: Rather, combination between two proofs when there is contradiction is the proof absolutely, whether it is like that or not, for qiyas is a proof absolutely whether its cause is derived or textually stated, so combination between it and the general is obligatory, and what preceded contains a reply and rulings. And al-Jubba'i argued first that qiyas is weaker than the report because qiyas depends on many things: the original ruling, its cause, its existence in the branch, absence of counter-evidence, all are speculative with doubt, unlike the report where conjecture is in two things: chain and meaning. So if the report were specified by it, it would necessitate annulling the stronger by the weaker, which is irrational. The answer: Both premises (weakness of qiyas and necessity of annulling stronger by weaker) are denied. As for the first, it will come in the section on Sunnah, and we have previously shown that the weakness of the specified general is because its benefit depends on the ruling of the accompanying specifier due to its cause that causes doubt, so it is weaker than the ruling established by causation, and the unspecific is definitely stronger, no doubt, and it is not permissible to specify it by it. As for others, they do not act upon it except after searching for the specifier, unlike qiyas, so reflect. As for the second, because specification is not annulment but combination; if by annulment is meant including that, then it is prevented from being false. But it is said that this is meant and the denial is obstinacy, because changing the stronger by the weaker is irrational, and combination is only when contradiction is established, and the weaker does not contradict the stronger, so ponder. And third answer: (He said third because the first resolves into two answers) is refuted by specification of the Book by a khabar wahid, for it is stronger than it, and specification of the mafhum by the mantiq. As for the refutation by specification of the Book by khabar wahid, it is not valid, because the khabar is speculative in thubut and the general of the Book is speculative in dalalah, so they are equal; and if he claims strength in the speculation of the general of the Book over the specific khabar, then explanation is needed. As for the refutation by mafhum, it is valid, and the excuse has passed, so remember. And al-Jubba'i argued secondly by the hadith of Mu'adh: Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi narrated from him that the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him and his family and companions) when he sent him to Yemen as a judge, said to him: 'How will you judge when a case comes to you?' He said: 'I will judge by what is in the Book of Allah.' He said: 'If it is not in the Book of Allah?' He said: 'By the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'If it is not in the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'I will exert my opinion and not fall short.' He said: He struck my chest and said: 'Praise be to Allah who has guided the messenger of the Messenger of Allah to what pleases the Messenger of Allah.' It is a sahih hadith. In al-Taysir, al-Tirmidhi said it is gharib, and its chain in my view is not connected. Al-Bukhari said it is not sahih, but its fame and the ummah's acceptance of it does not prevent it from being authoritative. Al-Baqillani and al-Tabari authenticated it. He indicated the aspect of inference by his saying: 'For he prioritized the report over qiyas and the Prophet approved him.' The answer: He delayed the Sunnah from the Book despite the permissibility of its specification by it by consensus, so the proof is refuted by it. Also: It does not prove the impossibility of specification by it at the time of contradiction, for if he permitted specification by it, then there is no ruling in the Sunnah when there is a conflicting specifying qiyas. And al-Jubba'i argued thirdly: The proof of qiyas is only ijma', and there is no ijma' at the time of opposition (i.e., when qiyas opposes the general of the Book or Sunnah) because of the opposition (i.e., due to the existence of disagreement among the imams among themselves). If ijma' is negated, the proof of the validity of qiyas is negated, so it cannot oppose the general, so it does not specify. The answer: We do not accept that the proof of qiyas is only ijma', rather it is established by others (i.e., other than ijma') as will become clear in qiyas. If it is established by it (assuming it is established by it), then its rulings are necessarily established, including combination at the time of contradiction. So the disagreement about it is like disagreement about ijma' itself, because ijma' on the necessary entails ijma' on the necessary consequence, and disagreement on the consequence is disagreement on the antecedent. This would only hold if the opponent conceded contradiction between qiyas and the general report so that combination is among its consequences. It is better to say: The disagreement is recent and the ijma' on the proof is the ijma' of the Companions, and it is not transmitted that they rejected qiyas due to opposition to the specified general, so reflect. And it was answered in al-Mukhtasar: That the cause established by text or ijma' and the specifier of the original refer back to the text, and it is a general ruling over the individual just as it is over the group, so specification by qiyas is only by it. If the probability of specification is preponderated by a contextual clue, it is necessary to act upon it due to ijma' on following the preponderant, and thus specification becomes preponderant. In it: That reference to that text applies to all analogies, because the common cause exists in every qiyas, so the text covers it, and it would entail that specification is permissible by every qiyas, which is against his school, for he does not permit specification by derived cause unless supported by a particular contextual clue, unless it is said that the mentioned text is understood to refer to what has a obvious commonality, so ponder. It was said: Also, the consequence of the mentioned text is general (i.e., the ruling applies only to the obligated individuals), so referring to the qiyas of one obligated person to another is correct, but not the qiyas of an act to another, and the issue is more general and applies to all analogies, unless specified by that, which involves clear artificiality. I say: If it is said that the mentioned text indicates by the concept of agreement that the ruling of equivalents and similars is one, for the understood ratio in the mentioned text is that one obligated person is like another in

Commentary
This passage is a detailed dispute from Hanafi usul al-fiqh concerning whether qiyas (analogical deduction) can be used to specify (takhsis) a general text (amm). The author, commenting on earlier works, presents arguments from Ibn al-Hajib and al-Jubba'i and responds from the Hanafi perspective. The central Hanafi position is that a strong qiyas—especially one with a textually stated cause or supported by contextual clues—can preponderate over a weak general text, because the general text when specified becomes weaker. The passage first addresses the notion that it is absurd to prefer the weaker over the stronger, but the author argues that the specified general is in fact weak due to its dependence on a specifier. Then Ibn al-Hajib's argument is discussed: when a qiyas has a clear cause or consensus, it is like a specific text. However, the Hanafis maintain that even such qiyas is speculative in dalalah while the general before specification is definitive, so the qiyas cannot specify initially; but after specification, the general becomes speculative. Al-Jubba'i raises three objections: (1) qiyas is weaker than khabar (report) because qiyas involves more speculative elements; the reply: the specified general is even weaker, and the khabar is only speculative in thubut, so they can be equal. (2) The hadith of Mu'adh shows prioritization of khabar over qiyas; the reply: the hadith itself shows that the Sunnah can specify the Book, so it does not forbid specification by qiyas in principle. (3) The proof of qiyas is ijma', but there is ikhtilaf when qiyas opposes the general; reply: ijma' is not the sole proof, and the disagreement is about the application of qiyas, not its validity. The passage ends with a discussion of a response from al-Mukhtasar, emphasizing that a qiyas with a textually established cause essentially refers back to that text, but this would allow specification by any qiyas, which is not the Hanafi view unless the analogy is clear (jali). The author adds that the reference to 'one individual like another' does not cover qiyas of actions, but the issue is broader.

Key Terms
تخصيص (takhsis): The act of specifying a general term (amm) to exclude some of its individuals.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction: applying a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a common effective cause (illa).
عام مخصوص (amm makhsus): A general text that has been specified by a specifier, thus losing its general application.
مظنة (mazinnah): A probable indication or circumstance that suggests a ruling but does not guarantee it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response to al-Jubba'i's first argument, why is it not a case of invalidating the stronger by the weaker?
A) Because the general is weaker than the qiyas after specification
B) Because qiyas is stronger than the general
C) Because the stronger is not being invalidated
D) Because both are equal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits specification by a strong qiyas only when the general text is already weak due to prior specification.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
intermediate
12 min
Dispute on Takhsis al-Kitab bi al-Qiyas: Hadith of Mu'adh and Ijma' Argument
Response to al-Jubbai's arguments against takhsis by qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on takhsis al-kitab bi al-qiyas and evaluate the counter-arguments from the hadith of Mu'adh and the ijma' argument.

Core Idea
The hadith of Mu'adh orders sources, it does not forbid qiyas from specifying a general text.

This passage explores a critical usul dispute: can qiyas specify a general Quranic or Sunnah text? Al-Jubbai argues no, using the hadith of Mu'adh and an ijma' argument. The Hanafi school responds with a nuanced analysis of the hadith and the nature of qiyas. By the end, you will understand how the Hanafis defend the use of qiyas as a specifying tool.

Guided Path
1
State the contested issue
What is the exact point of disagreement? The issue is whether qiyas (analogical reasoning) can specify the application of a general text ('amm) from the Quran or Sunnah.
2
Identify al-Jubbai's first argument (the hadith of Mu'adh)
Al-Jubbai claims that the Prophet's approval of Mu'adh's methodology—judging by the Book, then Sunnah, then qiyas—proves that qiyas cannot be used when a general text exists. The hadith is cited and its authenticity debated.
The hadith is a had ahad, but widely accepted by the ummah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the hadith argument
The Hanafis respond that the hadith only establishes the order of sources, not the impossibility of specification by qiyas. The Sunnah can specify the Book by consensus, so the order does not preclude specification by qiyas when textual evidence conflicts.
The key point: the hadith is about priority of sources, not about the permissibility of specification.
4
Identify al-Jubbai's second argument (ijma' dependency)
Al-Jubbai argues that the authority of qiyas rests solely on ijma' (consensus). If there is disagreement (ikhtilaf) among scholars regarding a qiyas that contradicts a general text, then ijma' is absent, and qiyas loses its authority.
Al-Jubbai's claim: no ijma' when qiyas opposes a general text.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and deeper discussion
The Hanafis deny that qiyas depends only on ijma'; it is established by other evidences. Even if based on ijma', conflict does not negate the authority of qiyas; reconciliation is required. The discussion further explores the role of the 'illa (effective cause) and contextual indicators in making qiyas preponderant for specification.
The text also addresses the objection that specification by qiyas would apply to all analogies, but Hanafis restrict it to cases with clear 'illa or contextual support.

في ظن عام الكتاب على خاص الخبر فلا بد من البيان، وأما النقض بالمفهوم فوارد، وقد مر العذر فتذكر (و) احتج الجبائي (ثانياً بحديث (معاذ وهو ما روى أحمد وأبو داود والترمذي عنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لما بعثه إلى اليمن قاضياً قال له : «كيف تقضي إذا لك أمر فقال أقضي بما في كتاب الله ، فقال : فإن لم يكن في كتاب الله؟ قال : فبسنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم ، قال : فإن لم يكن في سنة رسول الله؟ قال : اجتهد برأيي ولا آلو قال فضرب في صدري فقال : الحمد لله الذي وفق رسول رسول الله لما يرضى به رسول الله» (وهو) حديث (صحيح) وفي التيسير قال الترمذي غريب، وإسناده عندي ليس بمتصل، قال البخاري لا يصح لكن شهرته وتلقي الأمة له بالقبول لا يقعده عن الحجية ووثقه الباقلاني والطبري، وأشار إلى وجه الاستدلال بقوله: (فإنه قدم الخبر على القياس وصوبه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم، والجواب أخر السنة عن الكتاب مع جواز تخصيصها له بالاتفاق) فالحجة منقوضة به وأيضاً : لا يدل على امتناع التخصيص به عند التعارض فإنه إذا جوز التخصيص به فلم يوجد في الحكم في السنة عند وجود القياس المخصص المعارض (و) احتج الجبائي (ثالثاً : دليل القياس إنما هو الإجماع ولا إجماع عند المخالفة أي عند مخالفة القياس عام الكتاب أو السنة (للمخالفة) أي لوجود خلاف الأئمة فيما بينهم وإذا انتفى الإجماع انتفى دليل حجية القياس فلا يصح معارضاً للعام فلا يخصص (والجواب) لا نسلم أن دليل القياس الإجماع فقط، بل قد ثبت بغيره) أي بغير الإجماع كما سيلوح لك في القياس (وإذا ثبت به أي لو سلم ثبوته به ثبتت أحكامه ضرورة، ومنها الجمع) عند التعارض فالخلاف فيه (كأنه خلاف الإجماع لأن الإجماع على الملزوم إجماع على اللازم، والخلاف في اللازم خلاف في الملزوم. هذا إنما يتم لو سلم الخصم التعارض بين القياس والخبر العام حتى يكون الجمع من لوازمه، فالأولى أن يقال : الخلاف حادث والإجماع على الحجة إجماع الصحابة، ولم ينقل عندهم رد القياس بمخالفة العام المخصوص فتأمل فيه (وأجيب في «المختصر بأن ثابت العلة) بالنص أو الإجماع ومخصص الأصل يرجعان إلى النص، وهو حكمي على الواحد حكمي على الجماعة فالتخصيص) بالقياس (إنما هو به، وإذا ترجح ظن التخصيص بقرينة المقام يجب العمل به للإجماع على اتباع الراجح) وصار التخصيص راجحاً وفيه أن الرجوع إلى ذلك النص جارٍ في جميع الأقيسة) فإن العلة المشتركة موجودة في كل قياس فيتناوله النص، ويلزم أن يجوز التخصيص بكل قياس (وهو خلاف مذهبه فإنه لا يجوز بالمستنبط إلا إذا أعانته قرينة جزئية إلا أن يقال : إن النص المذكور محمول على ما يكون الجامع فيه جلياً فتدبر (قيل وأيضاً يرد عليه (اللازم) من النص المذكور (العموم) للحكم بالنسبة إلى المكلفين فقط فإنما يصح رجوع قياس مكلف على آخر لا قياس الفعل على الفعل (والمسألة أعم) وجارية في جميع الأقيسة (إلا أن يخصص بذلك وفيه تكلف) صريح (أقول : لو قيل (دل) النص المذكور بمفهوم الموافقة، على أن حكم النظائر والأشباه واحد فإنه يفهم المناط في النص المذكور هو كون أحد المكلفين مثل الآخر في الجامع المقتضى للحكم فكذلك في كل مثلين وإن لم يكونا من المكلفين (لم يبعد عن الصواب (فتأمل).
Regarding the assumption that a general text of the Book is specific to a particular report, there must be clarification. As for the objection based on [textual] implication, it is problematic, and the excuse has already been mentioned, so remember. (And) al-Jubbai argued (secondly) with the hadith of Mu‘adh, which is that Ahmad, Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi narrated from him that when the Prophet ﷺ sent him to Yemen as a judge, he said to him: 'How will you judge when a case is presented to you?' He said: 'I will judge by what is in the Book of Allah.' He said: 'And if it is not in the Book of Allah?' He said: 'Then by the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ.' He said: 'And if it is not in the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah?' He said: 'I will exercise my own opinion and will not fail.' He said: 'Then he struck me on my chest and said: Praise be to Allah who has guided the messenger of the Messenger of Allah to what pleases the Messenger of Allah.' (It is) a (sound) hadith. In al-Taysir, al-Tirmidhi said: 'Noble, but its chain in my view is not continuous.' Al-Bukhari said: 'It is not authentic.' But its widespread acceptance and the ummah's reception of it does not prevent it from being authoritative, and al-Baqillani and al-Tabari authenticated it. He pointed to the aspect of inference by his statement: (Indeed, he prioritized the report over qiyas, and the Prophet ﷺ approved him. The response: He delayed the Sunnah after the Book despite the permissibility of specifying the Book by it by consensus.) So the proof is undermined. Also: It does not prove the impossibility of specification by qiyas when there is conflict, because if specification by qiyas is permitted, then the ruling in the Sunnah is not found when a conflicting specific qiyas exists. (And) al-Jubbai argued (thirdly: The proof of qiyas is only consensus, and there is no consensus when there is opposition, i.e., when qiyas contradicts a general text of the Book or the Sunnah (due to opposition), i.e., due to the existence of disagreement among the imams. When consensus is negated, the proof for the authority of qiyas is negated, so it cannot oppose a general text, so it does not specify. (The response:) We do not concede that the proof of qiyas is consensus alone; rather, it has been established by other means (i.e., other than consensus) as will become clear to you in the chapter on qiyas. (And if it is established by it [i.e., if we concede its establishment by consensus], then its rulings are necessarily established, including reconciliation) when there is conflict. So disagreement about it (is like disagreement about consensus, because consensus on the necessary implies consensus on the necessary entailment, and disagreement on the necessary entailment is disagreement on the necessary.) This would only hold if the opponent concedes the conflict between qiyas and the general report, so that reconciliation is among its entailments. It is more appropriate to say: The disagreement is incidental, and the consensus on the authority is the consensus of the Companions, and it is not transmitted that they rejected qiyas due to opposition to a specific general text, so reflect. (And it was answered in al-Mukhtasar: The established cause [by text or consensus] and the specifier of the original revert to the text, and it is a ruling on the one which is a ruling on the group. So specification by qiyas is only through it. And if the assumption of specification is preponderant due to contextual evidence, acting upon it is obligatory due to consensus on following the preponderant.) And the specification becomes preponderant. But therein is that returning to that text applies to all analogies, because the common cause exists in every qiyas, so the text encompasses it, and it would necessitate permitting specification by every qiyas, which is contrary to his school, for he does not permit it with extracted [causes] unless a partial contextual indicator supports it. Unless it is said that the mentioned text is taken to be where the commonality is evident, so reflect. (It was said: Also, it is objected against him that the necessary entailment from the mentioned text is the generality of the ruling only with respect to the legally responsible individuals; thus, it is only valid to refer the qiyas of one responsible person to another, not the qiyas of an act to an act, and the issue is more general and applies to all analogies, unless it is specified to that; but that involves manifest burden.) I say: If it were said (the mentioned text indicates, by the implication of the correspondence, that the ruling of analogous and similar things is one; for it understands that the point of relevance in the mentioned text is that one responsible person is like another in the commonality necessitating the ruling; so likewise in every two similars, even if they are not from the responsible persons, it would not be far from correctness, so reflect.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute (ikhtilaf) between the Hanafis and al-Jubbai (a Mu'tazili) regarding whether qiyas can specify a general text from the Quran or Sunnah. The text first addresses a preliminary objection about the assumption that a general text of the Book can be taken as specific to a particular khabar, then moves to al-Jubbai's second argument: the hadith of Mu'adh. Al-Jubbai claims that the Prophet's approval of Mu'adh's methodology demonstrates that khabar is prioritized over qiyas, implying that qiyas cannot specify a general text. The Hanafi response is that this hadith only shows the sequence of sources (Book, then Sunnah, then qiyas), but it does not negate the possibility that a general text can be specified by qiyas when there is no conflicting textual evidence. Moreover, the hadith's authenticity is debated, but its acceptance by the ummah makes it authoritative. Al-Jubbai's third argument is that the proof of qiyas is solely ijma', and since there is disagreement (ikhtilaf) about the ruling when qiyas opposes a general text, the ijma' is negated, so qiyas cannot be used. The Hanafi response denies that qiyas is based only on ijma'; it is established by other evidences. Furthermore, if qiyas is valid, its rulings must be followed, and when there is conflict, reconciliation is necessary. The Hanafi position is that qiyas can specify a general text under certain conditions, such as when the 'illa is established by text or consensus. The author then analyzes the issue deeply, discussing the concept of the 'illa and the need for a contextual indicator, and concludes with his own suggestion that the text can be understood through the implication of correspondence. The Hanafi school holds that qiyas is a valid source for specification, and the hadith of Mu'adh does not contradict this.

Key Terms
عام ('amm): A general term that covers all individuals of its category without restriction.
خاص (khass): A specific term that indicates a particular individual or subset.
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification; the act of limiting a general term to a subset of its referents.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning; extending a known ruling to a new case based on a common cause ('illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, why does the hadith of Mu'adh not prove that qiyas cannot specify a general text?
A) Because the hadith is weak and cannot be used as evidence.
B) Because the hadith only shows the order of sources, not the impossibility of specification.
C) Because the hadith explicitly allows qiyas to specify general texts.
D) Because the hadith is about something else entirely.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that qiyas can specify a general text when the 'illa is clear and contextual indicators support it, and the hadith of Mu'adh does not negate this.

The Second Case: Both Absolute and Restricted Negative – Hanafi Rule and the Negated Indefinite Dispute
Discussion of the rule when an absolute and a restricted command are both negative in the same ruling with same cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when absolute and restricted commands are both negative in the same ruling and cause, they are both acted upon without contradiction, and you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi position that a negated indefinite (al-nakira al-manfiyya) is not necessarily a text for generality.

Core Idea
When absolute and restricted prohibitions share the same cause, both are applied by consensus — no conflict exists because refraining from both is possible.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut addresses a specific scenario in the interaction between absolute (mutlaq) and restricted (muqayyad) texts. When both are negative (e.g., prohibitions) and share the same ruling and cause, the Hanafi school holds that both can be implemented simultaneously, unlike the case when both are positive. The discussion then delves into the nature of the negated indefinite (al-nakira al-manfiyya), highlighting a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding whether such a construction indicates generality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule for dual negative texts
The passage states the rule: if both the absolute and restricted texts are negative (prohibitions) and share the same ruling and cause, they are both acted upon by consensus; one is not carried over to the other because there is no contradiction — one can simply refrain from both prohibited acts.
This contrasts with the case when both are positive, where interpretation or abrogation may be needed.
2
Examine the example from zihar
The author provides the example: 'لا تعتق مكاتباً' (Do not free a mukatab) and 'لا تعتق مكاتباً كافراً' (Do not free a disbelieving mukatab). Both are prohibitions; by refraining from freeing any mukatab, both are fulfilled.
The example illustrates that there is no conflict because the restricted is a subset of the absolute.
3
Analyze the dispute over the negated indefinite
The passage then engages in a discussion: Sharh al-Mukhtasar classifies the negated indefinite as general (amm), but the author of Sharh al-Sharh criticizes this, arguing that the negated indefinite is not a text for generality. The author of Fawatih al-Rahamut supports the Hanafi view that a negated indefinite (without the generic 'la') can refer to a single unit.
This step is crucial for understanding the difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the scope of the negated indefinite.
4
Understand the Hanafi response and the correct interpretation
The author justifies that the negated indefinite can be used for negation of a single unit (e.g., 'ما جاء رجل بل رجلان'), so the example is valid as an absolute prohibition without implying comprehensiveness. The absolute here means 'without restriction', and the restricted adds a condition; both are applied.
The author concludes that the preferred view is to interpret the absolute as having no restriction, even if general, and the restricted as having a restriction.

Source Text

لإمكان العمل بهما كما تقول في الظهار : لا نعتق مكاتباً ولا تعتق مكاتباً كافراً) فإنه يمكن العمل بالكف عنهما وفي شرح المختصر هذا من (العام) لأن النكرة تحت النفي الا من المطلق، فهو من باب آخر وهو إفراد المطابق لا تعتق المكاتب من غير (استغراق بل معهوداً ذهنياً (كما في اشتر اللحم، أقول) في رده (المقصود من الاعتراض (أن نفي الحصة المحتملة الذي هو معنى المطلق يعم، كالنكرة فكل نكرة أو معهود ذهني يقع تحت النفي فهو يكون نفياً للحصة المحتملة فيهم فليس مناقشة في المثال بل في الممثل له وما ذكره من المثال ففيه أن المعهود ذهناً، كالنكرة يعم تحت النفي، فهو أيضاً من باب العام وهذا غير وافٍ فإنك قد عرفت أن
