قائلو الاشتراك المعنوي بين الندب والوجوب وبينهما والإباحة (قالوا : ثبت الرجحان أو الإذن بالضرورة الاستقرائية أي قال الأولون ثبت ،الرجحان وقال الآخرون : ثبت الإذن (فلم يثبت الزائد من الحرج في الترك على الرجحان، أو لم يثبت الزائد هو الرجحان لعدم الدليل) عليه فلا مدلول إلا (ذلك وإذا قرر كلامهم هكذا وأعرض عن التقرير المشهور بأن الرجحان أو الإذن لازم لما استعمل فيه الصيغة وخصوص الوجوب من غير دليل فلم يثبت أقول فاندفع ما في «المختصر وغيره أن فيه إثبات اللغة بلازم الماهية وهو ممنوع عنه، وجه الدفع أن المقصود أن فهم الرجحان أو الإذن بالاستقراء والزائد من غير دليل (فافهم قلنا) قد ثبتت الزيادة) على الرجحان أو الإذن بأدلتنا المتقدمة فعدم الدليل على الزيادة (ممنوع) المتوقفون (قالوا) لو علم الوضع فإما بالعقل أو النقل والأول باطل، كيف العقل لا مدخل له) في معرفة الأوضاع (وأما النقل فالآحاد منه لا يفيد العلم بالضرورة والتواتر لم يوجد لوجود الاختلاف فيه وأيضاً يكون الخلاف حينئذ بهتاً وإذا بطل التواتر والآحاد بطل العلم بالنقل أيضاً، وهذا الدليل لو تم لدل على أن التوقف بمعنى لا ندري معناه كما مر في النقل الثاني من الأشعري. (قلنا : أوّلاً لا نسلم أن العقل لا مدخل له فيه بل العقل قد يكون له مدخل ما كما مر) في بيان طرق معرفة الوضع، نعم لا يكون له استقلال في المعرفة، فإن قلت : استقلال العقل مسلم ،البطلان فلا بد من النقل، وهو متواتر أو آحاد وكلاهما باطلان، فحينئذ لا توجه لهذا المنع، قلت: لو أريد بالعقل استقلاله ينتقل المنع إلى الشق الأخير، فإنا نقول : يجوز أن يكون نقل مقدمة متواتراً ولم يكن مختلفاً فيه، ثم يستمد بالعقل بانضمام مقدمة عقلية، فيلزم المدعي ويقع الخلاف فيه للخلاف في هذه المقدمة العقلية، أو لعدم اطلاع البعض عليها فافهم (و) قلنا (ثانياً) اخترنا أنه آحاد وسلمنا أنه لا علم بل يكفي الظن بالاستقراء) وهو كاف، في اللغويات، وإثبات الفرائض المقطوعة فانضمام القرائن الأخرى (و) قلنا (ثالثاً) اخترنا أن النقل متواتر، كيف لا تواتر استدلالات العلماء تواتر إنهاله وما ذكرتم من وقوع الاختلاف فلا نسلم تحققه سابقاً، بل إنما يتحقق لاحقاً والاختلاف لاحقاً لا يمنع الاتفاق سابقاً) وأما خلاف مثل القاضي والأشعري فلعله للغفلة عنه ( على أن التواتر قد يكون بالنسبة إلى طائفة دون أخرى فيفيد العلم لأولئك دون هؤلاء فيجوز الاختلاف ولا يكون بهتاً (وما قيل ذلك أي كون التواتر بالنسبة إلى طائفة (بعيد ، لأن سبب العلم مشترك بين الكل لأن الكل معتنون بمثل هذا الأمر العظيم (فأقول) اشتراك الكل في السبب (ممنوع ، لأن التواتر إذا كان متفاوتاً لكثرة المطالعة لأقضيتهم وتواريخهم مثلاً، وعدمها كان سبب العلم متفاوتاً) فمن أكثر مطالعة أقضيتهم وتواريخهم علم بالتواتر ومن لا فلا فتدبر).
Those who advocate for common meaning between recommendation and obligation and between them and permission said: 'Preference or permission is established by inductive necessity' meaning the first group established preference and the others established permission. So the extra [element] of difficulty in abandonment over preference, or the extra [element] of preference, is not established for lack of evidence. So the only signification is that. When their statement is thus formulated and we turn away from the famous formulation that preference or permission is necessary for what the form is used for, and the specific obligation without evidence is not established, I say: thus what is in Al-Mukhtasar and others—that it involves establishing language by a necessary concomitant of essence which is prohibited—is repelled. The repelling point is that the intention is that the understanding of preference or permission is by induction, and the extra without evidence. So understand. We said: The extra has been established over preference or permission by our previous proofs, so the lack of evidence for the extra is denied. The skeptics said: If the coinage is known, then either by reason or transmission, and the first is invalid because reason has no entry into knowing coinages. As for transmission, the isolated [report] from it does not yield necessary knowledge, and tawatur has not occurred due to the existence of disagreement about it. Also, disagreement would then be absurd. If both tawatur and isolated [reports] are invalid, then knowledge by transmission is also invalid. If this proof were complete, it would indicate that the suspension means we do not know its meaning, as mentioned in the second transmission from Ash'ari. We said: Firstly, we do not accept that reason has no entry; rather, reason may have some entry as mentioned in explaining the ways of knowing coinage. Indeed, it has no independence in knowledge. If you say: The independence of reason is admitted to be invalid, so transmission is necessary, and it is either tawatur or isolated, and both are invalid, then there is no response to this objection. I say: If by reason is meant its independence, the objection transfers to the last part. For we say: It is possible that a transmitted premise is mutawatir and not disagreed upon, then reason is utilized by adding a rational premise, so it follows the claimant and disagreement occurs due to disagreement about this rational premise, or due to some not being aware of it. So understand. And secondly, we choose that it is isolated, and we accept that there is no knowledge, but conjecture by induction is sufficient, and it is sufficient in linguistic matters and in establishing definite obligations, by adding other circumstantial evidence. And thirdly, we choose that the transmission is mutawatir. How is there no tawatur? The tawatur of the scholars' inferences, the tawatur of its usage. And as for the occurrence of disagreement you mentioned, we do not accept its actuality in the past; rather it occurs later, and later disagreement does not prevent earlier agreement. As for the disagreement of someone like al-Qadi and al-Ash'ari, perhaps it is due to neglect of it. Moreover, tawatur may be relative to one group and not another, so it yields knowledge for those without these, so disagreement is permissible and not absurd. And what is said that this—i.e., tawatur being relative to a group—is far-fetched because the cause of knowledge is common to all, for all care about such a great matter. I say: The commonality of all in the cause is denied, because tawatur, if it varies due to frequency of reviewing their judgments and histories, for example, and its absence, then the cause of knowledge varies. So whoever reviews their judgments and histories more knows by tawatur, and whoever does not, does not. So reflect.
Source pages p. 401

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute between the skeptics (اﻟﻤﺘﻮﻗﻔﻮن) who argue that we cannot know the meaning of the imperative form as obligation, and the Hanafi rebuttal. The skeptics claim that knowledge of the coinage (وضع) of the imperative either comes from reason (which has no role) or from transmission. The transmission is either mutawatir (which doesn't exist due to disagreement) or ahad (which gives only zann, not certainty). Therefore, they remain suspended (توقف). The Hanafi response has three points: 1) Reason does have some entry, though not independent; 2) Even if we accept that the transmission is ahad, the resulting conjecture (ظن) is sufficient in linguistic matters, especially when reinforced by other evidences (قرائن); 3) The transmission is actually mutawatir — there is consensus among early scholars about the imperative meaning obligation, and later disagreement (like that of al-Ash'ari) does not negate earlier tawatur. The passage also discusses relative tawatur (تواتر بالنسبة) — it may be common to a specialist group but not to others. This explains why scholars like al-Qadi and al-Ash'ari may have differed due to lack of exposure. The author concludes that the key is frequency of study; those who study the usage of the imperative in Arabic sources become certain of its primary meaning of obligation.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawatur): Multiple independent chains of transmission that yield certain knowledge; here it is argued that the usage of the imperative for obligation is mutawatir among scholars of language and law.
استقراء (istiqra'): Induction: examining many instances of the imperative in the Arabic language to conclude its default meaning of obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rebuttal in this passage, why is transmission of the imperative's meaning considered mutawatir despite later disagreements?
A) Because all scholars agreed during the Prophet's time, and later disagreements are due to ignorance of that consensus.
B) Because the majority of scholars always held that view.
C) Because the early usage was universally consistent, and later disagreements do not negate that earlier tawatur.
D) Because the Quran explicitly states it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defends the knowability of the imperative's meaning through relative tawatur and inductive conjecture, enabling a robust methodology for interpreting commands in the Quran and Sunnah.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
The Command After Prohibition: Permission or Obligation?
Usul dispute with expanded proofs and rebuttals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on al-amr ba'd al-hazr, apply the principle to a new example, and evaluate the opposing school's argument by identifying which usul principle is contested.

Core Idea
A command after a prohibition defaults to obligation due to the imperative form, unless a well-established custom indicates otherwise.

When the Lawgiver first prohibits an action and then commands it, what does that command mean? Does it merely permit what was forbidden, or does it now obligate it? This lesson unpacks a classic usul dispute between the Hanafi school and the majority (including al-Shafi'i) over the interpretation of such commands. You will examine the linguistic and customary arguments and see how a single usul principle can lead to different fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Recognize the issue: a command that comes after a prohibition (al-amr ba'd al-hazr). What are the two competing interpretations?
The majority (Shafi'i, al-Amidi) say permissibility (ibaaha); the Hanafis (and some Shafi'is like al-Razi) say obligation (wujoob).
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafis rely on the imperative form (sighah) as the factor (muqtadi) for obligation. They argue that since no preventer (mani') is established (the claimed custom is not proven), the default obligation remains.
Key principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub (the imperative indicates obligation).
3
Examine the opposing proof
The majority argue that the Shari'ah's custom ('urf) has made permissibility the prevalent meaning of such commands, so they indicate ibaaha unless a clue (qarinah) suggests otherwise.
They cite Quranic examples like hunting after ihram (5:2) and spreading after prayer (62:10).
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis respond that the claimed custom is not established because the examples contain contextual clues (qara'in) that indicate obligation or recommendation, not mere permissibility. Mere prevalence (ghalaba) does not create a custom that overrides the literal imperative.
The key usul point: for a custom to become the literal meaning (haqiqah 'urfiyyah), it must be so overwhelming that one jumps to it without any clue.
5
Apply the dispute to a fiqh example
Consider the hadith of mustahadah (chronic bleeding): the Prophet commanded the woman to pray. According to the majority, this command after the prohibition of prayer during menses indicates permissibility (she may choose to pray or not). According to the Hanafis, the command indicates obligation (she must pray).
Thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in whether prayer becomes wajib or just mubah.

Source Text

[الجمعة: ١٠] وقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم كنت نهيتكم عن إدخار لحوم الأضاحي فوق ثلاث (فادخروها) وفي صحيح مسلم في حديث طويل : كنت نهيتكم عن إدخار لحوم الأضاحي فوق ثلاث فأمسكوها ما يبدو لكم وقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم: «كنت نهيتكم عن زيارة القبور فقد أذن لمحمد في زيارة قبر أمه (فزوروها) فإنها تذكر الآخرة» رواه الترمذي. وفي هذا المثال نظر، فإنه للندب لا للإباحة إلى غير ذلك من الأمثلة نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَكُلُوا وَاشْرَبُوا حَتَّى يَتَبَيَّنَ لَكُمُ الْخَيْطُ الأَبْيَضُ مِنَ الْخَيْطِ الأَسود ﴾ [البقرة : ۱۸۷] ونحو: ﴿عَلِمَ اللَّهُ أَنَّكُمْ كُنتُمْ تَختَانُونَ أَنفُسَكُمْ فَتَابَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَعَفَا عَنكُمْ فَالْكَنَ بَشِرُوهُنَّ ﴾ [البقرة: ١٨٧] (وما قيل) في الجواب الإباحة فيها لدليل صارف عن الوجوب (وهو العلم بأنها شرعت لنا أي لانتفاعنا فإن الاصطياد مثلاً إنما شرع لنا أكله ونتلذذ بأكله قطعاً فلا ينقلب علينا) أي لا ينقلب مضراً بنا بالوجوب علينا حتى يكون تركه موجباً لاستحقاق العقاب (فغير متوجه إذ مقصودهم حمل المشكوك) في أنه للإباحة أم للوجوب لفقدان الدليل على الغالب المتيقن ولو بالدليل) والغالب الإباحة، وهذا غير متوجه، فإن دعوى المستدل كان صيرورة الإباحة حقيقة عرفية لا تثبت إلا إذا صارت بحيث سبقت إليها من غير قرينة فمنع المجيب الفهم من غير قرينة والذي في هذه الأمثلة قرينة فلم يثبت العرف ومطلق الغلبة لا يثبت العرف، بل قصارى أمره التعارف في الجملة والحقيقة مع القرينة قاضية عليه فتدبر (ولو منع حدوث العرف مستنداً بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِذَا انسَلَخَ الأَشْهُرُ الْحُرُمُ فَاقْتُلُوا الْمُشْرِكِينَ ﴾ [التوبة : ٥] فإنه للوجوب وقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم) حين جاءت فاطمة بنت حبيش إليه صلوات الله عليه وآله وسلم فقالت : يا رسول الله إني امرأة أستحاض فلا أطهر، أفادع الصلاة؟ قال: «لا إنما ذلك عرق وليس بحيض، فإذا أقبلت حيضتك فدعي الصلاة وإذا أدبرت الحيضة فاغسلي عنك الدم ثم صلي) رواه الشيخان مع الاكتفاء بالمضمر في أدبرت فههنا الأمر أيضاً للوجوب (لكان له وجه) فإنه لم يثبت الغلبة الموجبة للعرف فالمرجع إلى الاستقراء فعليك به وتمسك الحنفية بوجود وهي المقتضى للوجوب وهو الصيغة ولا مانع عنه فإنه كما يمكن الانتقال من التحريم إلى الإباحة يمكن منه إلى الوجوب) وإذا وجد المقتضى من غير مانع وجب القول به (وأجيب بأن العرف مانع عن الوجوب ومقتض) للإباحة قلنا : أين العرف إنما الدلالة في بعض المواضع بالقرائن الجزئية فتدبر، وتذكر الشافعية الذين وافقونا (قالوا: لو كان كذلك) أي لو كان الواقع بعد الحظر للإباحة لامتنع (التصريح بالوجوب، وهو باطل بالضرورة (وأجيب، بأنه قد يكون) التصريح (بخلاف الظاهر) فهو مغير عن الحقيقة العرفية وإن قرر بأن المقصود أنه لو كان للإباحة لناقض التصريح بالوجوب ظاهر معناه المتبادر ، قيل فحينئذ يمنع بطلان اللازم كيف والخصم يراه مغيراً وليس إلا لمنافاته الظاهر فتدبر.
The third essay on linguistic principles. Visiting graves - indeed visit them - or it is conditional upon removal of the cause of prohibition, like: When you are free from ihram then hunt (for permissibility according to the majority, including Imam al-Shafi'i and al-Amidi, and for obligation according to most Hanafis and it is narrated from al-Qadi al-Baqillani among the Shafi'is and Mu'tazilites, and chosen by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi among the Shafi'is). And the command after permission is like the command after prohibition, and the dispute is on whether it indicates permissibility or obligation, as transmitted in al-Mahsul. Imam al-Haramayn was hesitant about the command after restriction. And it was said: the command after restriction (is for what the restriction was upon, whether permissibility or obligation, and it was chosen by Shaykh Ibn al-Humam, which is close to correctness because of the overwhelming prevalence of permissibility in the custom of the Shari'ah - an overwhelming prevalence that one jumps to without a contextual clue, such that the literal meaning is abandoned, so it is given precedence over the language i.e. the linguistic literal meaning) because usage in it is metaphorical, since it is not what it was placed for in custom. And giving precedence to the customary literal meaning over the linguistic literal meaning is by consensus due to its abandonment. The disagreement between the Imam and his companion is only regarding the metaphorical customary usage that has become common, so understand. That is like His statement: And when you are free from ihram then hunt [5:2], His statement: And when the prayer is completed then disperse [62:10], his statement - peace and blessings be upon him: I used to forbid you from storing the meat of sacrificial animals beyond three days, so store it. In Sahih Muslim in a long hadith: I used to forbid you from storing the meat of sacrificial animals beyond three days, so keep it as long as you wish. And his statement: I used to forbid you from visiting graves, but now Muhammad has been permitted to visit his mother's grave, so visit them, for they remind of the Hereafter - narrated by al-Tirmidhi. In this example there is a view: it is for recommendation, not permissibility. And other examples like His statement: Eat and drink until the white thread becomes distinct to you from the black thread [2:187], and like: Allah knows that you were betraying yourselves, so He turned to you and pardoned you; so now consort with them [2:187]. And what was said in response: permissibility in those is due to a clue diverting from obligation, which is the knowledge that they were legislated for us i.e. for our benefit - for example, hunting was only legislated for eating it and enjoying its eating definitely, so it does not turn against us i.e. it does not become harmful to us by being obligatory upon us such that abandoning it would incur punishment. So it is not valid, since their intention is to carry the doubtful (whether it is for permissibility or obligation due to lack of evidence) to the prevalent and certain even by evidence. And prevalence is permissibility, and this is not valid. For the claim of the one who argues that permissibility has become a customary literal meaning is not established unless it becomes such that one jumps to it without a clue. So the responder denied understanding without a clue, and in these examples there is a clue, so custom is not established. And mere prevalence does not establish custom, rather at most it is common usage in general, and the literal meaning with a clue overrides it, so reflect. And if he denies the occurrence of custom, relying on His statement: And when the sacred months have passed, then kill the polytheists [9:5], for it indicates obligation, and his statement when Fatima bint Hubaysh came to him and said: O Messenger of Allah, I am a woman with chronic bleeding and I am not pure, should I abandon prayer? He said: No, that is just a vein and not menses; so when your menses approaches, leave prayer, and when it recedes, wash the blood from yourself and pray. Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim with sufficiency of the implicit reference in 'when it recedes'. So here also the command indicates obligation. Then there would be a point: The overwhelming prevalence that necessitates custom is not established, so recourse is to induction, so adhere to it. And the Hanafis cling to the existence of the factor requiring obligation, which is the imperative form, and there is no preventer from it, for just as transition from prohibition to permissibility is possible, so is transition to obligation. And when the factor exists without a preventer, it is necessary to accept it. And it is answered that custom is a preventer from obligation and a factor for permissibility. We say: Where is the custom? Indication is only in some instances by particular clues, so reflect. And recall the Shafi'is who agreed with us. They said: If that were the case i.e. if what occurs after prohibition were for permissibility, then explicit statement of obligation would be impossible, which is false by necessity. And it is answered that explicit statement may be contrary to the apparent meaning, thus it changes the customary literal meaning. And if it is established that the intention is that if it were for permissibility, the explicit statement of obligation would contradict its apparent evident meaning. Then it is said: So then the necessity is not proven false; how can it be when the opponent sees it as changing, and it is only because it contradicts the apparent, so reflect.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about a specific type of command: one that comes after a previous prohibition (al-amr ba'd al-hazr). The core question is whether such a command indicates permissibility (ibaaha) or obligation (wujoob). The text begins by stating that the majority (including Shafi'is) hold it indicates ibaaha, while the Hanafis (generally) hold it indicates wujoob. Some prominent Shafi'is like al-Razi and al-Baqillani agreed with the Hanafi view. The passage then examines evidence: Quranic examples like 'When you are free from ihram, then hunt' (5:2) and 'When the prayer is completed, then disperse' (62:10), and hadith examples about storing meat and visiting graves. The commentator explains that the Hanafi reliance on custom ('urf) is key: they claim that 'ibaaha' has become the customary meaning (haqiqah 'urfiyyah) due to overwhelming prevalence in the Shari'ah, so the command is understood as permissibility. The opponent argues that this custom is not established because the examples have specific clues (qara'in) that indicate obligation or recommendation, not mere permissibility. The text also discusses the argument from the factor (muqtadi) of the imperative form, which requires something to prevent it from indicating obligation. The Hanafis hold that since the imperative is present and no preventer (mani') exists (beyond a disputed custom), obligation is indicated. The response challenges this by stating that custom itself is a preventer. The passage ends with a subtle point: even if the explicit statement of obligation is made (as in the hadith about killing polytheists), it may be changing the apparent meaning of customary usage. The discussion reflects a deep usul analysis of how to reconcile linguistic principles with contextual evidence.

Key Terms
الأمر بعد الحظر (al-amr ba'd al-hazr): A command that occurs after a previous prohibition, e.g., 'When you are free from ihram, then hunt.'
الغلبة (al-ghalaba): Overwhelming prevalence in usage that establishes a customary literal meaning (al-haqiqah al-'urfiyyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the default ruling of a command that comes after a prohibition?
A) It indicates permissibility (ibaaha) because the Shari'ah custom has made that the meaning.
B) It indicates obligation (wujoob) because the imperative form is the factor (muqtadi) and no preventer (mani') is established.
C) It indicates recommendation (nadb) because the examples show that.
D) It depends on whether the command is from the Quran or hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis hold that a command after prohibition defaults to obligation due to the imperative form, rejecting the opposing view that Shari'ah custom has made permissibility the default meaning.
